# plan.md — Feature scope & build log

> _Created: 2026-06-03 · Last updated: 2026-06-20_

> [!IMPORTANT]
> **PRODUCT NAME: CADENCE.** The product is **Cadence**, and that is the only name to use. A brief 2026-06-10 rename experiment to a different brand was reverted on 2026-06-16; the retired name must not be reintroduced anywhere (code, docs, DB, env, caches, APIs). Any stray legacy token from that experiment is to be read as equivalent to `cadence`/`Cadence`.
>
> _Do not perform destructive refactoring of database column/table names or folder structures that are bound to Lovable Cloud and pgvector schemas. All modifications should map the name logically at the user and documentation level while keeping underlying plumbing compatible._

> The canonical record of **what Cadence is built to be** (the full feature scope), **the order we build it**, and **what already exists to reuse**. Product framing: [`README.md`](./README.md). Operating rules: [`AGENTS.md`](./AGENTS.md). Architecture: [`architecture/`](./architecture/). UI contract: [`DESIGN.md`](./DESIGN.md).
>
> **No MVP1/MVP2/MVP3 gating, no far-future phase deferral.** We build the full intended scope on the current stack ([`docs/decisions/tech-stack.md`](./docs/decisions/tech-stack.md)) and ship continuously. This doc is written to be read straight into a coding session (Claude Code / Lovable) and acted on.

---

## How this file is organized

1. **Feature scope** — the whole product, stress-tested as if nothing is built. The high-level feature list.
2. **Competitive feature comparison** — factory.ai · hyperagent · Linear → what Cadence should build.
3. **Granular feature catalog** — every feature from login/logout to agent-transfer/workspace level, with _what_ and _why_. This is the dev-ready map.
4. **Build order** — the sequence to build it, production-grade, reusing legacy code where it fits.
5. **Active build log** — what we actually ship, updated as we go (starts near-empty).
6. **Legacy build log (retained)** — the previous source build, kept as a reuse reference, not the plan.
7. **Product-agent roster** — re-examined (explicit vs. implicit).
8. **Testing, lessons, out-of-scope.**

---

## 1. Feature scope (stress-tested from scratch)

> [!IMPORTANT]
> **v4 supersedes this section for scope (2026-06-11).** The canonical feature scope is now [`docs/strategy/archive/v4-feature-map.md`](./docs/strategy/archive/v4-feature-map.md) — 7 platform laws, 6 stations over the 12-stage engine, the 19-agent mesh with handoff contract + HITL gate matrix, the 7-surface IA, station feature catalogs (SEN/DEC/DEF/BLD/LCH/LRN/ENG/OPS), and milestones M1–M5. The adversarial reasoning behind it: [`docs/strategy/archive/v4-stress-test.md`](./docs/strategy/archive/v4-stress-test.md). The 12-stage engine description below remains valid as the _internal_ loop reference; where wording differs, **the v4 map wins**. **v5 overlay (2026-06-11):** the _felt product_ — wedge UX, nav, vocabulary, June 22 demo scope — is governed by [`docs/strategy/archive/v5-chief-of-staff.md`](./docs/strategy/archive/v5-chief-of-staff.md) (PM Chief of Staff; 4 felt surfaces + Trust drawer; phases `F-V5-RITUAL` → `F-V5-DEMO`). v4 remains the expansion map.

Cadence runs the full product lifecycle as one governed, autonomous loop. The scope below is the target product — not a discovery tool. Each stage is run by autonomous agents; the human approves at the gates.

### Who we serve, what they expect, and the gap (grounding for the feature list)

The feature list below is a deliberate response to who the customer is and what the market already sets as table-stakes — not a wish list. Inspiration drawn from products worth learning from is captured in [`docs/references/competitive-reference.md`](./docs/archive/competitive-reference.md) (deferred; inspiration only).

**Personas (who orchestrates Cadence):**

- **P1 — Enterprise Director / VP of Product (The Portfolio Governor)**: owns portfolio-level alignment, agent spend budgets, and compliance. Pain: Swarm drift, lack of visibility into agent actions, security audits, budget overruns, and multi-product roadmap health.
- **P2 — Lead / Senior PM (The Daily Cockpit Operator)**: runs day-to-day discovery, spec definition, and feature delivery. Pain: Mechanical process work (spec writing, ticket updates, release logs, alert triage) eating up time needed for strategic judgment.
- **P3 — Engineering Lead / Tech Architect (The Code Gatekeeper)**: guards repository health, code quality, and branch stability. Pain: Agent-written code drifting from internal architecture guidelines, introducing regressions, or breaking sandboxed environments.
- **P4 — UX/UI Designer (The Visual Validator)**: ensures design tokens and brand style guide alignment. Pain: Generated code failing to match design system tokens or looking off-brand in mockups.
- **P5 — GTM Lead / Product Marketer**: handles positioning and product launch. Pain: Generating changelogs, marketing collateral, newsletter posts, and distribution updates by hand for every release.
- **P6 — Customer Success & Support Lead**: monitors product support feedback. Pain: High ticket volumes, slow bug triage, and user signals getting lost before reaching the product manager.

**Market expectations (table-stakes — must-haves, or we're not credible):** auth + SSO-ready tenancy; real (not mocked) data; connectors to the tools they live in; an assistant/chat surface; observability + cost visibility; approvals/audit for anything autonomous; multi-project support; export/no-lock-in.

**The gap (where the market is underserved — our opening):** point tools own single bands (engineering autonomy, or issue tracking, or research synthesis). **No one runs the _whole_ lifecycle — discover → build → ship → launch → support → learn — as one governed, autonomous, multi-product loop.** That gap is the spine of the feature catalog in section 2.

**What the customer actually wants (the job):** "Take this intent and run it end-to-end — autonomously, in parallel, across my products — and only stop me for the calls that matter." Every feature below maps to that job.

**The feature list derives from the PM's actual day.** The product manager is the cockpit operator — the features below exist to run the PM's day (triage inbox → decide → synthesize → spec → tickets → build/test/ship → launch/update → answer "why is this on the roadmap?" → report → repeat). The day-to-features mapping and the PM/eng-lead lenses are in [`docs/planning/considerations.md`](docs/planning/considerations.md). If a feature does not serve a real PM task, question it.

### Lifecycle stages (the 12-Stage Product Loop)

**S1 — Signal Capture**

- Multi-source signal ingest: support tickets, churn, usage telemetry, sales notes, reviews, NPS, interviews.
- Agent clustering → themes → ICE-scored opportunities; continuous (not one-shot) synthesis; dedupe by similarity.
- A continuously-updated discovery feed per product.

**S2 — Audio Sync (WhisperFlow)**

- High-context audio recording, transcription, and meeting spec extraction.
- Translates voice memos or team meetings into feature specs and backlog tickets with zero friction.

**S3 — ICE Prioritization**

- Prioritization queue management: opportunity scoring based on Impact, Confidence, and Ease.
- Automated re-prioritization as new signals arrive or existing ones scale in severity.

**S4 — Spec Definition**

- Opportunity → PRD/spec, retrieval-grounded and cited; inline `/ai` editing; versioned with diff.
- Acceptance criteria, non-goals, risks, success metrics auto-drafted; human edits and approves.

**S5 — Sprint Planning**

- Spec → dependency-aware task graph with estimates, owners, risk flags.
- Outcome-oriented roadmap (Now/Next/Later) synced automatically to Linear/Jira.

**S6 — Agentic Build**

- In-product multi-file coding: Builder Agent claims file locks, checks out branches, and writes code.
- Surgical modifications across files, committing atomically and resolving conflict flags.

**S7 — Visual QA**

- Sandbox preview environments generated automatically for visual validation of UI changes.
- Let designers and PMs audit layout and styling against design system tokens before merging.

**S8 — Safe Release**

- Merges PRs, runs deploy checklists, deploys, and monitors production health.
- Automated rollback triggered if error metrics or exception counts spike post-deploy.

**S9 — GTM Launch**

- Growth agent drafts release changelogs, marketing blog posts, newsletter copies, and announcement text.

**S10 — Support Triage**

- Support agent triages incoming customer tickets, drafts answers, and routes bug logs back into Signal Capture (S1).

**S11 — Cohort Analytics**

- Automated feature adoption tracking, cohort analysis, and outcome funnel monitoring.

**S12 — Learn & Reflect**

- Outcome evaluation: compares performance telemetry with the original PRD spec.
- Updates the Product Memory Graph and publishes a learning brief to the portfolio dashboard.

### Cross-cutting platform (mandatory, spans all stages)

**X1 — Orchestration & automation engine**

- Workflow definitions across stages; event/schedule/webhook triggers; an automation builder.
- **Many sub-agents running in parallel** within a mission; **many agent sessions running in parallel** across missions.
- A live orchestration view (the mission/agent graph) with per-node status, cost, and approval state.
- Planner/executor loop with max-step/max-cost caps, replay-and-branch, cancellation, checkpoints.

**X2 — Multi-product & multi-workspace**

- **Multiple products in flight — Product A/B/C — grouped under Workspaces (A/B/C).**
- Per-product/workspace isolation of data, agents, memory, budgets, and access (RLS by `user_id` + `workspace_id`; see [`architecture/data.md`](./architecture/data.md)).
- Product switcher; cross-product portfolio view.

**X3 — Trust & governance (the AI trust stack)**

- Per-call telemetry, LLM-as-judge scoring, guardrails (input + output), RAG with citations, prompt versioning + A/B, eval harness with regression gate, drift watch, budgets, live trace waterfall, incidents log, approval gates everywhere.

**X4 — Product Memory**

- Queryable graph of signals → themes → opportunities → decisions → experiments → outcomes, with `supersedes` lineage; the institutional context agents reason over; exportable as skill packs.

**X5 — Interop (agent-native)**

- MCP server (Cadence as a tool surface) + MCP client (consume external tools) + A2A (Agent Cards, delegate-to-agent, peer registry). Capability scopes, rate limits, prompt-injection guard on external results, audit log.

**X6 — Identity, auth, billing**

- Auth (email + OAuth), session management, per-workspace membership (future: roles/teams), BYO model keys (encrypted), usage/billing metering against budgets. See [`architecture/security.md`](./architecture/security.md).

---

## 2. Granular feature catalog (login to agent-transfer, with what + why)

> **Sub-feature-level expansion:** [`docs/planning/feature-backlog.md`](./docs/planning/feature-backlog.md) takes every area below down to addressable sub-features with stable IDs, states, acceptance signals, dependencies, and a status × build-order rollup. This section stays the narrative catalog; the backlog is the flat, ticket-ready list. Keep both true.

Every feature, grouped by area. Format: **Feature — what it is — _why we need it_.** This is the build checklist; each becomes an issue/spec. Status tags: `[reuse]` legacy survives, `[extend]` legacy base + new work, `[new]` build from scratch.

> **Inspiration, not comparison.** This catalog absorbs the best ideas from products worth learning from — factory.ai's autonomous build/ship + live "mission" view (we extend it past code into launch/support), hyperagent's team-of-agents with per-agent budgets and self-improving memory, and Linear's agents-as-first-class-users + saved-workflow skills + event automations. We take the inspiration and build it into _our_ features below; we are not maintaining a competitor scorecard.

### A. Identity & access

- **Sign up / onboarding** — email+password + Google OAuth; create first workspace + product; set display name, timezone, working hours. — _Entry point; personalization and scheduling depend on it._ `[reuse]`
- **Login / logout** — authenticated session, sign-out everywhere, session refresh, `Last-Event-ID` resume for streams. — _Baseline security and reliable streaming._ `[reuse]`
- **Password reset / email verification** — standard flows; verification on by default. — _Account safety._ `[reuse]`
- **Profile & preferences** — display name, role, timezone, working hours, default model per surface. — _Drives greeting, scheduling, model routing._ `[reuse]`
- **BYO model keys** — add/test/rotate/delete provider keys, encrypted; masked display. — _Model-agnostic; cost control; enterprise trust._ `[reuse]`
- **Roles & membership (future)** — invite, per-workspace roles, SSO/SAML. — _Team and enterprise readiness._ `[new]`

### B. Workspaces & products

- **Create / switch workspace** — top-level tenancy boundary. — _Isolates a client/company/initiative._ `[extend]`
- **Create product under workspace** — Product A/B/C inside a workspace; vision/problem/target-users/metrics/stage. — _Run several products in parallel without bleed._ `[extend]`
- **Product switcher + portfolio view** — fast switch; cross-product overview. — _One operator, many products._ `[new]`
- **Per-product isolation** — data, agents, memory, budgets scoped by `user_id`+`workspace_id`+product. — _Security + correctness across products._ `[extend]`
- **Archive / delete product** — lifecycle hygiene. — _Avoid clutter; data governance._ `[new]`

### C. Agents — configuration

- **Agent roster** — list durable agents + spawned sub-agents per product. — _See the team you command._ `[extend]`
- **Create / clone / configure agent** — system prompt, tool allow-list, model, temperature/top*p/seed, max tokens, schedule, approval mode, memory toggle. — \_Tailor behavior + governance per role.* `[reuse]`
- **Enable / disable / schedule agent** — cron schedules with next-run preview. — _Autonomy on a clock._ `[reuse]`
- **Agent detail + run history** — last runs (status/duration/score/cost), memory inspector. — _Trust through observability._ `[reuse]`

### D. Agent execution

- **Run on-demand / scheduled** — manual trigger or cron fan-out. — _Both reactive and proactive autonomy._ `[reuse]`
- **Planner/executor loop** — plan → tool calls → observe → reflect → answer; max-step/max-cost caps. — _Reliable multi-step autonomy._ `[reuse]`
- **Approval gates + Decision Queue** — `auto|confirm|review`; queue of runs awaiting review; one-click resume from checkpoint. — _Governed autonomy; the trust core._ `[reuse]`
- **Cancellation / replay-and-branch / checkpoints** — stop mid-run (save partial), re-run against different model/prompt, resume. — _Control + iteration._ `[reuse]`

### E. Agent communication, coordination & transfer (mandatory)

- **Sub-agent spawning** — Orchestrator spawns ephemeral specialists per task. — _Scale to the work without fixed seats._ `[new]`
- **Agent-to-agent messaging** — structured internal A2A messages between agents in a mission. — _Coordination without a human relaying context._ `[new]`
- **Agent transfer / handoff** — pass a mission + its context, memory, and artifacts from one agent to another (e.g. Planner → Engineer → QA → Release). — _Work flows across the lifecycle with zero context loss; this is the spine of the autonomous loop._ `[new]`
- **Parallel sub-agents** — many specialists working a single mission concurrently. — _Speed; mirrors a real team._ `[new]`
- **Parallel agent sessions** — many missions running at once across products. — _One operator, many things in flight._ `[new]`
- **Orchestration / mission graph view** — live DAG of agents/sessions with per-node status, cost, approval state; pause/steer. — _See and command the swarm._ `[new]`
- **Shared vs. private memory** — mission-shared context + per-agent long-term memory with importance decay. — _Coordination without leakage._ `[extend]`

### F. Discover

- **Signal ingest** — paste/CSV now; connectors (Intercom/Zendesk/reviews/sales) next; sentiment on insert. — _Raw material of discovery._ `[extend]`
- **Clustering → themes → opportunities** — embed + cluster + synthesize with evidence ids; ICE scoring; dedupe by similarity. — _Turn noise into ranked opportunities._ `[reuse]`
- **Continuous discovery feed** — always-fresh per-product feed. — _The lead use case; ongoing, not one-shot._ `[extend]`

### G. Define

- **PRD/spec generation** — opportunity → structured cited draft. — _Specs downstream of evidence, not vibes._ `[reuse]`
- **Doc editor + `/ai` + versions/diff** — Tiptap, inline AI commands, autosave, version diff, citation pills. — _Author + iterate with provenance._ `[reuse]`

### H. Plan

- **Task graph** — spec → dependency-aware tasks with estimates/owners/risk. — _Executable plan agents can run._ `[reuse]`
- **Outcome roadmap** — Now/Next/Later; each item declares its outcome + measure. — _Anti-feature-factory; ties work to results._ `[extend]`
- **Scheduling** — agent proposes work blocks in working hours. — _Time-aware execution._ `[reuse]`

### I. Build (autonomous)

- **Studio multi-file coding** — agents write across files; per-hunk diff accept/reject; atomic revisions. — _Agents build, not just suggest._ `[extend]`
- **Watch-the-agents-build surface** — live per-session view: step, files, tool calls, cost, status; pause/steer/approve. — _Trust + control over autonomous code._ `[new]`
- **Branch/worktree isolation per mission** — each mission on its own branch. — _Parallel safe building._ `[new]`

### J. Test (autonomous)

- **Test generation + run** — agents author and run unit/integration/E2E + evals. — _Quality without a human writing every test._ `[new]`
- **QA gate + self-correct loop** — failing tests feed back to the build agent until green or escalate. — _Closed-loop quality before ship._ `[new]`

### K. Ship

- **PR / deploy / release notes** — open PRs, run deploy checklist, deploy, draft notes — behind approval. — _Autonomous delivery, governed._ `[new]`
- **Rollback triggers** — documented per release. — _Safe shipping._ `[new]`

### L. Launch / GTM / price

- **Launch + positioning + pricing + distribution drafts** — agent-drafted, human-approved before external. — _The lifecycle past code, that point tools skip._ `[new]`
- **Customer-facing pages / announcements** — generated, approved. — _Close the go-to-market gap._ `[new]`

### M. Operate / support

- **Ticket triage + draft answers + route/escalate** — agents handle inbound; themes flow back to Discover. — _Support closes the loop into discovery._ `[new]`

### N. Learn

- **Decisions + `supersedes`** — outcomes write decisions with lineage. — _Auditable "why," and belief updates._ `[reuse]`
- **Re-score + insight memo + daily brief** — outcomes re-rank opportunities; memo surfaces in the brief. — _The loop compounds._ `[extend]`

### O. Product Memory

- **Knowledge graph + query** — signals→decisions→outcomes, typed nodes/edges. — _Institutional context agents reason over._ `[new]`
- **Currency / drift on facts + skill packs** — flag stale facts; export versioned skill bundles over MCP. — _Memory stays true; reusable expertise._ `[new]`

### P. Trust & observability

- **Telemetry + traces + judge scores** — per-call events, trace waterfall, LLM-as-judge. — _Measure every AI action._ `[reuse]`
- **Guardrails + prompt studio + eval harness + drift + budgets + incidents** — input/output guards, versioned prompts + A/B, regression-gated evals, drift watch, budget caps, incident log. — _Make autonomy safe, improvable, affordable._ `[reuse]`
- **AI message contract** — score/model/latency/tokens/cost/citations/feedback/trace/replay on every AI message. — _Trust is the UI._ `[reuse]`

### Q. Interop (agent-native)

- **MCP server + client** — expose Cadence as tools; consume external tools. — _Be the place agents plug in._ `[new]`
- **A2A server/client + Agent Cards + scopes/limits/audit** — peer agents, delegate-to-agent, governed. — _Cross-vendor agent ecosystem._ `[new]`

### R. Platform & ops

- **Command palette (⌘K) + global search** — resolve every destination/action/artifact. — _Keyboard-first speed._ `[reuse]`
- **Connectors / integrations** — Docs, Notion, Linear, Calendar, GitHub, Slack, CRM. — _Act on the systems the operator lives in._ `[extend]`
- **Notifications + budgets config + settings** — approvals, breaches, guardrail rules, integration health. — _Operate the platform._ `[extend]`

---

## 3. Build order (v4 milestones — each independently demo-able)

> Canonical milestone definitions with proof bars: [`docs/strategy/archive/v4-feature-map.md`](./docs/strategy/archive/v4-feature-map.md) §9. The foundation invariants (blast-radius limits, spend caps, kill-switch, prompt-injection defense, provider fallback, durable runtime, sandboxed execution — see [`docs/planning/considerations.md`](docs/planning/considerations.md)) remain P0 architecture, already largely in place; every milestone below builds on them, never around them.

1. **M1 — The Golden Path (demo-ready).** One continuous, watchable run: connect Slack/GitHub → Scout themes → Strategist ranks (Critic attached) → approve → Scribe cited spec → approve → Planner task graph → Builder PR + CI green → release-note draft → outcome card. Includes `F-IA-V4` (collapse 34 routes to the 7-surface IA), vocabulary enforcement, cost-per-mission chip, narrated empty states. _This fixes "not demo-ready" before anything new is added._
2. **M2 — The Loop Closes (the differentiator).** The right half becomes real: support triage loop (LRN-01), analytics inbound (SEN-05), launch kits (LCH-01), outcome reviews (LRN-02), visible re-score (LRN-03), memory consult/write on every mission (ENG-05), cost-per-artifact (ENG-06). Proof: a support-ticket cluster re-ranks the opportunity queue with zero human transport.
3. **M3 — The Team Arrives.** Roles + per-persona approval lanes (ENG-08), design scaffolds + handoff (DEF-04/05), visual validation (BLD-06), enablement notes (LCH-04), spec comments, multi-seat.
4. **M4 — The Org Runs Itself.** Portfolio view, budget enforcement UX, MCP server/client + A2A delegate-out (ENG-07, BLD-04), skill packs (LRN-05), enterprise plane (ENG-09), pricing briefs (LCH-03).
5. **M5 — Compounding.** Memory-graph querying as product surface, stale-fact drift, cross-product learnings, connector breadth, outcome-priced enterprise plans.

Sequencing rule unchanged: architecture first, so later stages are _additions, not rewrites_. See [`docs/decisions/tech-stack.md`](./docs/decisions/tech-stack.md).

---

## 4. Active build log (update as we ship)

### 2026-06-20

**[SECURITY, 2026-06-20 15:08 UTC] Scheduled backend hook auth hardened (✅).** Loaded all persisted security scan results, including connector security scan results (Wiz returned no findings). Fixed the active open-endpoint finding: `/api/public/hooks/*` no longer accepts the public app key as proof of caller identity. The hook guard now accepts only a private hook secret from `x-cron-key` or bearer auth, with optional env fallback; migration `20260620150512_a486e345-5722-48bd-80e4-49ee123b8179.sql` creates a locked `app_private` secret store and rewires the live scheduled jobs (`approvals-tick`, `event-reactor-tick`, `memory-tick-daily`, `resume-runs`) to send the private key. Verified the live job commands now use `x-cron-key` and the scanner finding was marked fixed; persisted scan results now show no active findings across app, connector, and backend scanners.

**[O3 drift slice, 2026-06-20] Fact-currency / drift flag shipped on the knowledge graph (parallel/knowledge).** The deterministic half of `O3`: a pure `computeStaleness` (`src/lib/knowledge-graph-view.ts`) flags a fact as stale when its NEWEST supporting `artifact_lineage` edge is older than a 90-day threshold (relative to an injected `nowMs`, so it stays testable), and is HONEST - nodes with no dated evidence are never counted. Surfaced minimally in the Graph view (`GraphCanvasView` + `GraphExplorer`): a "N of M facts may be stale" count + a dashed amber ring on stale nodes (functional flag, not a design pass). +3 unit tests (16 in the module). **Gate:** tsc 0 / `bun test` (drift) 16/16 / `bun run build` green. ◐ (live-verify on publish). **Deferred (the other half of O3):** outcome-driven contradiction drift (needs the supersession engine, AI/attended lane) + the versioned skill-pack export over MCP (needs Q1). **Branch:** `parallel/knowledge` to `main`.

**[O1 / DBR-1 v1, 2026-06-20] The knowledge-graph explorer shipped (parallel/knowledge lane).** The remaining slice of `O1` (the typed graph explorer over the provenance walk) is now built, as the first lane-built increment of the Decision Brain (DBR-1 v1, the "B+" cut, founder-enriched + approved this session). Spec: [`docs/features/knowledge-graph-explorer.md`](./docs/features/knowledge-graph-explorer.md). It DERIVES a typed `{nodes, edges}` graph deterministically from the existing `artifact_lineage` (no LLM extraction, no new tables, migration-free, fail-safe), rendered as a bounded, Obsidian-style visual graph at `/knowledge?tab=graph`: nodes color-coded by kind and sized by influence, pan/zoom, click-a-node-for-its-story (reusing `getLineage`/`getProvenance`), a truthful "as of" time axis over real edge `created_at`, and the `supersedes`/`contradicts` + `validTo` supersession SEAM laid in empty and ready (so the future inference engine renders with zero UI change). Pure core `src/lib/knowledge-graph-explorer.ts` (+`.test.ts`, 13 TDD tests: typing, rings, influence, bounding, time filter, supersession classification, fail-safe), server fn `src/lib/knowledge-graph-explorer.functions.ts` (RLS-scoped bounded both-ways walk, batched `.in()`, a fresh empty graph on any error), UI `src/components/knowledge/{GraphExplorer,GraphNodeStory,GraphPanel}.tsx`, route `_authenticated.knowledge.tsx` (new `graph` tab + `?focusKind`/`?focusId`). **Why B+ and not the full graph:** the bi-temporal supersession ENGINE (inferring `contradicts`/`supersedes` from outcomes) needs an AI write-path = recurring spend + the AI chokepoint, both founder-gated and out of this lane, so it is the explicit next DBR increment; v1 ships the visual + read substrate against a schema already shaped for it. **Gate:** `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0; `bun test` 328/328 (13 new); `bun run build` green; an adversarial review found and fixed a shared empty-graph singleton and added `.in()` batching, with a non-blocking `filterByTime` maxRing-gap logged as debt. ◐ (live-verify on publish). **Branch:** `parallel/knowledge` to `main`. **Deferred:** O3 (drift/skill-packs) + the supersession engine.

**[DBR-0, 2026-06-20] Decision Brain step 1: the Critic now cites decision precedent (plus a "stubbed loop" correction).** First slice of the topmost-priority Decision Brain bet (H1, [`docs/features/decision-brain.md`](./docs/features/decision-brain.md)). TDD'd a pure `formatDecisionPrecedent` in `src/lib/ai/outcome-memory.ts` (+5 tests, RED then GREEN) that renders a workspace's recent shipped outcomes into a compact, capped (8 outcomes, 200-char summaries) precedent block; wired a best-effort `learnings` query into `runCritic` (`src/lib/ai/critic.server.ts`) so the Critic (the launch wedge) cites the workspace's own outcomes (e.g. "we shipped a similar bet and it MISSED") instead of red-teaming in a vacuum. **Fail-safe:** the query is try/catch returning `[]` and an empty block leaves the Critic prompt byte-identical to before, so the wedge can never break. **Correction:** writing the test first disproved the plan's premise that the outcome to memory loop was "stubbed (`rememberOutcome` has no caller)", `recordOutcome` already calls it and the loop is closed and correctly human-gated (a verdict lands weeks after ship, not at ship-detection). The real gaps were the flat (non-graph) memory and the blind Critic; DBR-0 fixes the latter. Corrected the false claim across `horizon-bets.md`, `decision-brain.md`, `SOURCE-OF-TRUTH.md` §0/§4, `feature-dashboard.md` row 147, `session-decisions.md`, `strategic-inputs-log.md`. **Verification (what I ran):** `bunx tsc --noEmit` exit 0; `bun test` 303/303 (5 new); `bun run build` ✓. The live LLM+DB precedent path is not behaviorally verified unattended, so status is ◐ (verify on next publish). **Branch:** `main`. **Next:** DBR-1 (the typed bi-temporal decision graph, a migration) after the founder enrichment pass.

**[COCKPIT] Notification preferences and email/digest scaffolding (R3-PREFS) shipped (parallel/cockpit cycle 1).** Added per-user notification preferences to manage alert channels (In-App Feed, Instant Email, and Digest summaries) across 4 categories (Approvals, Health, Spend, and Drift).
- **Migration:** `20260620020000_user_notification_preferences.sql` adds the `user_notification_preferences` table with default values of `true`, daily digest frequency, and RLS policies allowing users to view and update their own preferences.
- **Server functions:** `getNotificationPreferences` (returns defaults if no database row exists) and `updateNotificationPreferences` (Zod-validated upsert) in `notifications.functions.ts`.

**[WM-M10, 2026-06-19 15:58, overnight cycle 29] credit unit + cost-to-credit conversion + the calm legibility layer (✅; pure module, fully unit-tested).** Added the credit metering math to `src/lib/ai/pricing.ts` (+ a new `pricing.test.ts`), the "what one credit is" the dormant `WM-M4` seam was waiting for. **What it does:** `CREDIT_COGS_USD` (the USD of blended COGS one credit represents; margin lives in grant-sizing, not the per-credit price; founder-tunable placeholder, §7) + an optional per-model `MODEL_CREDIT_RATE`/`creditRateFor` (defaults to 1 = pure COGS pass-through); `creditsForCost(estCostUsd, model) = ceil(estCostUsd / CREDIT_COGS_USD * rate)`, which is **0 for a non-billable call** (zero / negative / non-finite cost) and **never 0 for a billable one** (a positive cost always rounds up to >= 1 credit, margin-positive); `estimateCreditsForCall(model, prompt, completion)` composes the existing `estimateCostUsd` so the projection and the real post-call debit share one source of truth; and the **legibility layer** `actionCreditRange(actionKind)` returning a display-only `{min,max}` credit range per user-facing action (chat_reply / research / prd_draft / mission_step / embedding), derived by running calibrated representative token shapes through the SAME conversion so the shown range can never contradict the real meter (unknown kinds get a safe non-alarming default; never rendered as a flat charge). **Decisions (logged in session-decisions):** `actionCreditRange` is a PURE function (no DB, no `ai_events` query) to honor the "no DB, pricing.ts only" scope, the spec's "historical averages" being the future calibration source (WM-M16), not a live read; the numbers are documented §7 placeholders, the mechanism is final; `MODEL_CREDIT_RATE` ships empty (pure COGS pass-through) since no model needs a non-1 rate yet. **Verification (what I actually ran):** `bun test src/lib/ai/pricing.test.ts` 15/15 pass (29 assertions: billable-floor, 0-for-non-billable, NaN/Infinity guard, monotonicity, premium > cheap, estimator composition, legibility ordering + consistency); `bunx tsc --noEmit` exit 0; `bunx eslint` 0 on both files; `bun run build` ✓ (3.13s); humanization scan 0 hits. Adversarial review found no real fix (the never-0 invariant holds; Infinity/NaN → 0 credits; `actionCreditRange` returns a COPY of the default so callers cannot mutate the shared const; no overclaim, this is the credit LIBRARY and WM-M12 drives it into the live seam). **Marked ✅ (not ◐):** behavior is actually verified by the passing unit tests, no publish needed (a pure module, like WM-M1). **UI breadcrumb:** none yet (library; surfaces in the WM-M16 credit UI). **Branch:** `overnight/wm` (worktree, fast-forward to `main`). **Next:** WM-F1b, or now-unblocked WM-M11 (per-tier grant; needs WM-M2 + WM-M10, both done) / WM-M15 (margin levers; needs WM-M10).

**[WM-M11, 2026-06-19 16:31, overnight cycle 31] per-tier credit grant + monthly cycle reset (◐; grant math ✅, the writes + tick dormant).** Built the grant side of the credit engine in a new `src/lib/credits.functions.ts` + a new `src/routes/api/public/hooks/credit-tick.ts` cron hook. **What it does:** pure `monthlyGrantCredits(tier)` (reads `entitlements.creditMonthlyBase`: free 500 / pro 2500 / max 10000 / team 10000 / enterprise 0-custom) + pure `resetDelta(currentIncluded, monthlyGrant)` (the signed move to the new included balance; `currentIncluded + resetDelta === grant`); dormant `grantMonthlyAllowance(accountId, tier)` (sets the included balance to the tier amount, records the cycle anchor + a 'grant' ledger row; top-ups untouched) and `resetCreditCycle(accountId)` (re-grants included to the stored monthly grant, PRESERVES the purchased top-up balance, writes a 'reset' ledger row); and the `credit-tick` hook (mirrors `memory-tick.ts`: `requireHookCaller` auth, grants un-granted accounts, resets accounts whose `cycle_anchor` is over ~30 days old). **[WM-M5, 2026-06-19 19:30, overnight cycle 36] tier limit gates (◐; trigger behaviorally dry-run-verified on prod, gate ships dormant).** Turns the entitlements matrix (WM-M1, shipped) from feature-flags-only into enforced caps on product + workspace creation. Strategic pick of the cycle: it is the keystone that makes the 5-tier ladder mean something (no tier capped anything before this), advancing the founder-directed Monetization initiative (M-C). **What it does:** migration `20260619200000_wm_m5_tier_limit_gates.sql` adds the pure `tier_product_limit` / `tier_workspace_limit` SQL functions (free 2/1, pro 3/∞, max 5/∞, team+enterprise ∞/∞, a MIRROR of `entitlements.ts` `limitFor`) + `enforce_product_limit` / `enforce_workspace_limit` BEFORE-INSERT triggers (SECURITY DEFINER, `search_path` pinned). New `src/lib/limits.functions.ts` adds the typed `LimitReachedError { kind, currentTier, limit, upsellTier }` + pure `nextUpsellTier` / `isOverLimit` + the best-effort pre-migration-tolerant `assertCanCreateProduct`, wired into `createProject`. **Decisions (session-decisions):** (1) the **DB trigger is the authoritative guard**, because the client inserts products straight from the browser (`AppShell.tsx:406`) so a server-only check is bypassable; the server pre-check exists only for a typed, upsell-aware nice-path error. (2) the product cap is **account-WIDE** (counted across all the account's workspaces via `workspaces.account_id`), not per-workspace, so a paid user with pooled (unlimited) workspaces cannot dodge the cap by spreading products; the first workspace is never gated (existing-count 0 < every cap, resolved via `owner_id` to survive the alphabetical BEFORE-trigger fire-order ahead of `set_workspace_account`). (3) the gate ships **DORMANT** behind a new `limit_gates_enabled()` flag (= false), mirroring `credits_enabled()` / `memory_expiry_enabled()`, because activating hard caps before a live upgrade path (Stripe) would trap free users with no way to upgrade; the founder flips it when pricing is live (founder gate). The server pre-check reads the same flag (5-min in-process cache, mirroring `creditsEnabled` in `runtime.server.ts`) so server and DB agree. **Verification (what I actually ran):** a `BEGIN..ROLLBACK` behavioral dry-run on the LIVE prod DB (applied the WM-M2 essentials first since WM-M2 is not yet on prod, then WM-M5, with the flag flipped on): on a real free account, inserts up to the cap (2 products) succeeded and the 3rd was BLOCKED by the trigger with the exact message "Product limit reached for this plan (2 allowed)...", a 2nd workspace was BLOCKED with "Workspace limit reached for this plan (1 allowed)...", and all six pure limit-function values were correct; then rolled back (prod untouched). Offline: `bun test` 252/252 (13 new limits tests), `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0, `bunx eslint` 0 on the 3 changed files, `bun run build` ✓, humanization clean on the new files (the pre-existing em dashes in `projects.functions.ts` are outside my 8-line diff). **[WM-F1b, 2026-06-19 20:10, overnight cycle 37] agent-workspace isolation hardening (◐; migration dry-run-verified on prod, live isolation on publish).** The moat-hardening half of WM-F1: WM-F1 made recall workspace-aware but left the agent TABLES on the pre-tenancy owner-only RLS and let the non-loop insert paths land memory untagged. Strategic pick of the cycle: among the unblocked candidates (WM-F3 / WM-M15b / WM-F1b) it is the only one that directly advances the named memory/decision moat, and it finishes a partial. **What it does:** migration `20260619220000_wm_f1b_agent_workspace_hardening.sql` adds a `user_id`-fed BEFORE-INSERT trigger (`set_row_workspace_from_user`, reused from WM-F9, service-role-safe because it sources `NEW.user_id` not `auth.uid()`) to all 5 agent tables (`agents`, `agent_memory`, `agent_tools`, `agent_runs`, `agent_approvals`) so EVERY insert path is workspace-tagged at the DB layer (the `seed_default_agents` SQL function, the `memory.remember` tool, any service-role writer) without hand-editing a single app insert; plus a DUAL-KEY membership RLS (`auth.uid() = user_id AND is_workspace_member(workspace_id)`) replacing the owner-only `auth.uid() = user_id` policy on all 5. Code: `registry.server.ts` `memoryRemember` now tags the ACTIVE workspace (pre-migration-tolerant post-insert update, mirroring `rememberOutcome`), so a multi-workspace user's explicit memories land in the active workspace, not just the default. **Decisions (session-decisions):** (1) picked WM-F1b for strategic impact (the moat is the one North-Star item among the three candidates), navigating its risk with the proven WM-F9 patterns. (2) **Universal insert tagging via a DB trigger, not the bible's per-file audit**, editing the ~6 insert paths is fragile (easy to miss one, several are SQL/service-role), whereas the trigger guarantees every insert is tagged; strictly more robust. (3) **Dual-key, not pure membership**, the recall RPCs are user-scoped + workspace-narrowed, so the table RLS must match (a teammate must not read another member's raw memory); the dual key is strictly MORE restrictive than the prior owner-only policy, so it can never widen access or lock the owner out (`ensure_user_default_workspace` inserts a `workspace_members` row in every branch, so every backfilled row's workspace has the owner as a member). (4) **DEFERRED to WM-F1c:** NOT NULL on `workspace_id` (WM-F1's `ON DELETE SET NULL` preserves the moat across workspace deletion; NOT NULL forces `ON DELETE CASCADE` = irreversible memory loss on workspace delete, a founder-gated product call, the trigger + backfill already enforce isolation without the constraint), the `agents UNIQUE(user_id,slug) → UNIQUE(workspace_id,slug)` swap (verified `seed_default_agents()` uses `ON CONFLICT (user_id, slug)`, so the swap would break onboarding's seed unless its conflict target is recreated; it also couples to the WM-F8 roster read; low value with no multi-member workspaces yet, and unverifiable offline), and the types regen (the schema is not published, so a regen would emit pre-WM types). **Verification (what I actually ran):** `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0; `bunx eslint src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts` 0; `bun run build` ✓; `bun test` 252/252; humanization scan clean on both authored files; AND a two-pass `BEGIN..ROLLBACK` dry-run on the LIVE prod DB (via the Lovable MCP): applied WM-F1's column essentials then the full WM-F1b, 5 filler triggers + 5 dual-key policies created, **0 old owner-only policies remaining** (the dual-key actually enforces, no permissive-policy-wins bug), the trigger fills `workspace_id` on an insert that omits it (= the user's default workspace), `seed_default_agents` still succeeds (`ON CONFLICT` intact), `is_workspace_member(null) = false` (orphaned rows correctly hidden), and a **simulated-JWT read as a real owner returned all 23 of their `agent_memory` rows, no reader breakage**; a direct check found **0 memory-owners without a `workspace_members` row**; rolled back, then re-confirmed prod is untouched (still the old `own agent_memory all` policy, no `workspace_id` column, 0 triggers). Adversarial self-review folded 2 humanization fixes (em dashes in my own new comments); the highest-risk concern (owner locked out by the dual key) was disproved by reading `ensure_user_default_workspace` (it always ensures membership) + the live read. **Marked ◐ (not ✅):** behaviorally dry-run-verified on the real prod schema, but the LIVE isolation activates only on the founder's next publish, so it is not verifiable on the published app until then. **UI breadcrumb:** none (RLS plumbing). **Branch:** `overnight/wm` (worktree, fast-forward to `main`). **Next:** WM-F3 (RBAC enforcement) or WM-M15b (response cache).

**[WM-M15b + WM-M15b-fix, 2026-06-19, overnight cycles 38-39] response cache shipped, then its 3 runtime-fatal bugs fixed (◐).** WM-M15b (the cache half of the WM-M15 margin lever) was shipped by a PARALLEL session (`796513d181`): a content-hash `ai_response_cache` table (7-day TTL) read/written at the AI chokepoint, with a conservative surface whitelist (`brief`/`scheduler`/`test`) and guardrails required. This cycle (39) had independently picked the same item and was building it in the worktree; the per-cycle `origin/main` sync caught the collision after the parallel push, so instead of a duplicate this became the **fix** (`7897085004`), because the shipped version was tsc/build-green but broken at runtime in three ways. **(1) Migration FATAL:** `CREATE INDEX ... WHERE expires_at > now()` is rejected by Postgres (`now()` is STABLE; index predicates require IMMUTABLE), so the migration would have FAILED to apply on the founder's next publish. Verified live: the broken DDL returns `ERROR: 42P17` on the prod DB; the corrected plain-index DDL applies cleanly (throwaway-table dry-run, dropped); the real `ai_response_cache` is confirmed not-yet-applied, so editing the migration in place is correct (a new migration could not help, since the broken `...230000` would run first and fail). **(2) Cache no-op FATAL:** `callModel` ran the provider retry loop unconditionally even on a cache hit (the `if(!cacheHit)` guard wrapped only the cache-write), so the cache saved zero COGS; the provider call is now skipped on a hit. **(3) readCache always missed:** it passed the literal string `"now()"` to `.gte("expires_at")`, which Postgres cannot cast to timestamptz, so every read errored; now `new Date().toISOString()`. **Also hardened:** `generateCacheKey` switched to Web Crypto (`crypto.subtle`, the `rag/indexer.server.ts` pattern) off a bare-`"crypto"` dynamic import whose Worker runtime was unverifiable (and would have crashed every cacheable call if it failed to resolve); `writeCache` now stores under `effectiveModel` + skips fallback responses so later reads keyed by `(model, cache_key)` stay consistent; the `supabase` params are typed (`SupabaseClient`, no-explicit-any). **Verification (what I actually ran):** `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0; `bun run build` ✓ (3.33s); `bunx eslint` 0 on the 3 files; `bun test src/lib/ai/cache.test.ts` 10/10; AND the prod migration dry-run above (broken DDL fails with 42P17, fixed DDL applies + drops cleanly). Adversarial self-review confirmed definite-assignment of `providerOut`, `lastErr` scope, no double-write on a hit, `via="cache"` preserved, and complete NOT-NULL inserts. **Marked ◐ (not ✅):** the migration now applies and the cache control-flow is correct, but live cache-serving activates only on the founder's next publish. **Lesson:** a green tsc/build does not cover a migration's apply-time validity or a cache-skip control-flow path; the K2-class floor (the prod migration dry-run + the runtime-fatal review) is exactly what caught all three. **UI breadcrumb:** none (AI chokepoint). **Branch:** `overnight/wm` (worktree, fast-forward to `main`). **Next:** WM-F2 (account-level memory pooling) or WM-F4/F5 (ownership transfer + invites).

**[WM-F2-fix, 2026-06-19 22:05, overnight cycle 40] restored the security + correctness invariants the shipped WM-F2 regressed (◐; behaviorally dry-run-verified on prod).** The WM-F2 ship above (`18db474d3b`, by a PARALLEL session) was tsc/build-green but rewrote the recall RPCs in a way that REGRESSED the WM-F1 baseline it replaced, and its "Acceptance criteria verified / no cross-account leak / no runtime-fatal bug" claim was not borne out. **[WM-F3-fix, 2026-06-19 22:20, overnight cycle 41] the shipped RBAC migration used invalid `create policy if not exists` and would have failed to apply on publish (◐; dry-run-verified on prod).** NOT a collision: a PROACTIVE adversarial review of the recently-shipped SECURITY DEFINER / RLS migrations (the highest-risk parallel-built code), prompted by two prior broken parallel ships (WM-M15b, WM-F2). It found the THIRD broken ship: the WM-F3 RBAC migration (`2b1c429591`, by a parallel session) used `create policy if not exists` for all four account/account_members policies. **Postgres `CREATE POLICY` has NO `IF NOT EXISTS` clause** (unlike `CREATE TABLE`/`INDEX`), so this is a hard syntax error (`ERROR: 42601`); the migration would have FAILED to apply on the founder's next publish, blocking the entire migration run. `tsc`/`build` were green because it is pure SQL, and the shipped dashboard row claimed "verified: tsc/test/build green". **Fix (`70c0ca7db5`):** all four `create policy if not exists "X"` are now `drop policy if exists "X"` + `create policy "X"` (valid + idempotent; the four names differ from WM-M2's account policies, so no name collision and no double-grant beyond the harmless redundant SELECTs), and the `prevent_workspace_owner_demotion` trigger is now `drop trigger if exists` + `create` so the migration is genuinely re-runnable as its header claims. **Verification (what I actually ran):** confirmed on the LIVE prod DB via `BEGIN..ROLLBACK` (stubbing the unpublished WM-M2 `accounts`/`account_members` deps): a `create policy if not exists` probe errors with `42601`; the corrected full migration applies cleanly (the 6 RBAC helper functions + the 5 policies + the demotion trigger all created); rolled back, then prod re-confirmed untouched (the real `"ws owner manage"` policy I dropped inside the txn was restored, stub tables + `has_workspace_role` absent). Also DATA-checked the new role-keyed `"ws owner admin manage"` policy for owner-lockout: all 7 workspaces have their owner as a `workspace_members(role='owner')` row (0 lockouts), so swapping `owner_id = auth.uid()` for `has_workspace_role(id, ['owner','admin'])` locks no current owner out. `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0; `bun run build` ✓ (3.12s); full `bun test` 270/270 (SQL-only change, TS untouched). **Marked ◐ (not ✅):** the migration now applies and the owner-lockout is disproven on current data, but live RBAC enforcement activates only on the founder's publish. **Lesson:** three consecutive parallel ships (WM-M15b, WM-F2, WM-F3) were tsc/build-green but carried a publish-blocking migration, a cross-user security regression, and an unappliable migration; the standing response is now to proactively review every parallel-shipped SECURITY DEFINER / RLS / migration before the founder publishes, not only the item this loop is itself building. **UI breadcrumb:** none (RLS plumbing). **Branch:** `overnight/wm` (worktree, fast-forward to `main`). **Next:** WM-F4/F5 (ownership transfer + invites) or a continued review sweep of the remaining unverified-by-me ◐ migrations.

**[WM-F5, 2026-06-19 23:03, overnight cycle 44] workspace invitations BACKEND (◐; table + accept RPC + server fns behaviorally dry-run-verified on prod, UI deferred).** The team-growth on-ramp: there was no invite flow (membership was manual). New `inviteMember`/`listInvitations`/`revokeInvitation`/`acceptInvitation` server fns in `workspaces.functions.ts`. **Decisions:** (1) the accept path is a definer RPC, not RLS, because the invitee is not a member yet, so membership RLS would block the read; (2) the token is bound to the invited email (the signed-in user's `auth.users.email` must match the invitation) so a leaked or forwarded token cannot be redeemed by a different account; (3) single-use via a `FOR UPDATE` lock + a `status` flip to `accepted` (a second accept hits the `status <> 'pending'` guard, which is also how revoke takes effect: a revoked token is no longer pending); a second accept was rejected ("This invitation is no longer valid."), a token whose invited email differed from the caller was rejected ("This invitation was sent to a different email address."), and an expired token was rejected ("This invitation has expired."); rolled back, then prod re-confirmed untouched (the table + RPC absent, the seeded membership gone). **Marked ◐ (not ✅):** the table + RPC + server fns are built and behaviorally dry-run-verified on the real prod schema, but the join route + Settings UI are deferred, and live invites activate on the founder's publish (WM-F5 depends on the unpublished WM-M2 + WM-F3, the latter as fixed in `70c0ca7db5` so `can_manage_workspace` exists — without that fix the whole migration run would have failed before reaching WM-F5). **UI breadcrumb (once UI ships):** Settings > Team > Invite, and a public `/join/$token` accept page. **Branch:** `overnight/wm` (worktree, fast-forward to `main`). **Next:** WM-F6 (move product between workspaces) or WM-F7/F8 (settings IA, switch hardening) backend.

**[WM-F8, 2026-06-19 23:18, overnight cycle 45] workspace switch hardening — query-cache reset (◐; core cache-hygiene shipped + gate-green + driven, full no-flash payoff scales with server-side read-filtering).** The bug: `setActiveWorkspaceId` in `src/hooks/use-workspace.tsx` mutated React state on a workspace switch but never touched the TanStack Query cache, so any workspace-scoped query whose key omits the workspace id kept serving the PREVIOUS workspace's cached rows until it happened to refetch — a stale-data flash that "reads like a leak" (the spec's exact framing), and worse for inactive queries (navigating to a not-yet-mounted page after a switch surfaced the old workspace's cache). **What it does:** on a real switch (`id !== activeWorkspaceId`), `setActiveWorkspaceId` now calls `queryClient.removeQueries({predicate})` to clear every workspace-scoped cache entry — active AND inactive — so nothing stale renders and active observers refetch under the new workspace context; a new pure module `src/hooks/workspace-query-scope.ts` (`GLOBAL_QUERY_KEY_ROOTS` + `isWorkspaceScopedQueryKey`) is the allowlist that PRESERVES the user/account-global queries (`workspaces` list, `profile`, `billing`, `connections`, `calendar-connections`, `integrations`, `api-keys`, `mcp-tokens`) and fails safe to "workspace-scoped" for any unlisted or non-string root, so a newly-added query is isolated by default. **Decisions:** (1) chose the single-site cache reset over threading `activeWorkspaceId` into ~40 query keys — the one switch chokepoint catches every workspace-scoped query (including the un-keyed ones) in one surgical, offline-verifiable change, whereas the per-key approach is a sprawling ~40-file diff easy to miss one of; the per-key work is logged as defense-in-depth follow-up WM-F8b. (2) `removeQueries` (not `invalidateQueries`) because invalidate keeps the stale data visible during the background refetch — the exact flash we're killing — while remove clears it so observers show loading then fetch fresh. (3) exact-match Set membership (not a prefix test) so `workspace-bindings`/`workspace-brief` are correctly treated as workspace-scoped, never confused with the global `workspaces` key. (4) extracted the predicate into its own React/supabase-free module so the unit test runs without initializing the supabase client (which reads env at module load). **Adversarial review (HARD GATE 4):** no runtime-fatal bug — `useQueryClient()` is safe (the same component already calls `useQuery`, so a provider exists); the Case-1 stale-closure-refetch risk is absent (keyed queries like `["swarm","hud",activeWorkspaceId]` refetch on key change; server-fn queries like `() => fMissions()` hold no client workspace closure); driven by the AppShell switcher (`AppShell.tsx:516`) + create/delete paths, so not staged-but-never-wired; the guard avoids needless clears on a same-workspace re-select. **Verification (what I actually ran):** `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0; `bunx eslint` on the 3 touched files = 0 errors (1 pre-existing `react-refresh` warning on the untouched `useWorkspace` export); `bun run build` ✓ (4.28s); `bun test` 274/274 (4 new in `workspace-query-scope.test.ts`). **Marked ◐ (not ✅):** the cache reset is correct, gate-green, and driven, BUT most server-fn reads are still user-scoped server-side today (e.g. `missions.functions.ts` / `guardrails.functions.ts` reference no `workspace_id`), so the full user-visible "no cross-workspace flash" lands as reads become workspace-filtered (WM-F9b); and the two-seeded-workspace Playwright assertion needs a publish. No live behavioral test of the switch was run, so not ✅. **UI breadcrumb:** AppShell > workspace switcher. **Branch:** `overnight/wm` (worktree, fast-forward to `main`). **Next:** WM-F6 (move product between workspaces) or WM-M9 (remove self-serve BYOK).
**[F-BUILDER-MULTIFILE, 2026-06-19 23:39, parallel/build lane cycle 1] Scoped multi-file build: pre-declared touch list + max-files cap on a Studio changeset (◐; pure logic unit-tested, server+UI gate-green, live-verify pending publish + migration sync).** The thin slice of I1: a scope contract over a multi-file changeset so a session stays inside its sanctioned blast radius before the confirm-gated commit. **What it does:** additive migration `20260619270000_studio_multifile_constraints.sql` (a mission-keyed `studio_changeset_constraints` table — `allowed_paths text[]` + `max_files int` — RLS mirrored from `studio_changesets`: workspace-member read, owner write); pure, unit-tested logic in `src/lib/ai/studio-hunks.ts` (`matchesTouchList` exact/dir-prefix/`*`+`**` globs, `evaluateFileSetPolicy` in/out-of-policy split + over-cap count, `applyChangesetHunkSelections` cross-file merge primitive); server fns in `studio.functions.ts` (`setChangesetConstraints` declare/clear mission-keyed, `enforceTouchList` drop out-of-scope staged files, `dispatchStudioSession` optional pre-declaration, `getStudioSession` returns `constraints` + `fileSetPolicy`); and a `Build > session > Changes > Scope` card (live in/out-of-scope + over-cap status, touch-list editor + max-files input, one-click "Apply scope", per-file "out of scope" badge). **Decisions:** (1) enforcement is operator-layer, not agent-tool — the agent's `studio.stage`/`studio.commit` tools live in the forbidden chokepoint (`tools/registry.server.ts`), so the human curates against the policy before approving the commit; staying strictly in lane. (2) The cap is a warning, never an auto-drop (which files to shed is the operator's call). (3) The changeset-wide "merge across files" stays a pure tested helper, NOT a server endpoint, since the operator path drives per-file curation via the existing `applyStagedHunkSelection` — an un-driven server fn would be a "staged but never driven" gap (caught + removed in adversarial review). (4) `getStudioSession`'s constraints read degrades to an unconstrained policy if the table is unsynced (pre-migration window), so the session read never errors. **Verification (what I actually ran):** `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0; `bunx eslint` 0 on all 5 changed files; `bun test src/lib/ai/studio-hunks.test.ts` 24/24 (58 asserts) covering glob edge cases (single vs double star, dir prefix, zero-segment globstar), policy split + over-cap, and cross-file merge; full studio suite 56/56; `bun run build` ✓ (3.09s); authored-diff scan for em/en dashes + control bytes 0 hits. NOT a behavioral live test (the agent loop + the new migration cannot run locally — no AI key, table syncs via Lovable on publish), so marked **◐**, not ✅. **UI breadcrumb:** Build > session > Changes > Scope. **Branch:** `parallel/build` (worktree, fast-forward to `main`). **Lane queue now DRY** (§15 stop-and-report; K2b/BLD-05/BLD-04 are out of lane).

**[WM-F6, 2026-06-19 23:42, overnight cycle 46] move product between workspaces (◐; transactional `move_product` RPC + server fn behaviorally dry-run-verified on prod, UI deferred).** Products could not move; cross-workspace consolidation (paid/team) needs it. Built the backend per the founder ruling (keep building backend, batch UI to the design pass). **Key finding (verified live before building):** the spec's "harden product-level scoping first (product_id has no RLS on those ~10 tables today)" is ALREADY satisfied - querying `pg_policies` on prod shows every product-scoped table is read-gated by `is_workspace_member(workspace_id)` (SELECT) and `is_workspace_member(workspace_id) AND user_id=auth.uid()` (UPDATE/DELETE). So reassigning `workspace_id` IS the move: destination members gain access and source-only members lose it automatically, with NO separate RLS-hardening migration. **What it does:** migration `20260619280000_wm_f6_move_product.sql` adds a SECURITY DEFINER `move_product(_product_id, _dest_workspace_id)` that, after a guard (caller is owner/admin of BOTH workspaces via WM-F3 `can_manage_workspace`, both workspaces in the SAME account via WM-M2 `workspaces.account_id`, a `FOR UPDATE` lock on the product), atomically reassigns `workspace_id` on the product (`projects`) + 13 product-scoped tables. New `moveProduct` server fn in `projects.functions.ts` (validated wrapper calling the RPC via `context.supabase` so the RPC's `auth.uid()` checks apply). **Decisions / the untyped-client trap (HARD GATE 4):** verified the live schema before writing - the product foreign key is `project_id` on 8 tables (signals/themes/opportunities/prds/docs/tasks/decisions/conversations) but `product_id` on 4 (ai_events/connection_bindings/rag_chunks/studio_changesets); a single wrong column name would silently leave orphan rows tsc can't catch, so each UPDATE uses the right column (and `project_id OR product_id` for the 8 tables that carry both). Also caught 3 product-scoped GRANDCHILDREN that carry `workspace_id` but link to the product only via a parent - doc_versions (doc_id), messages (conversation_id), learnings (opportunity_id/prd_id) - and move them through their parent so they don't orphan; the remaining `workspace_id` tables (missions/agent_runs/budgets/evals/...) are workspace-scoped not product-scoped and correctly stay (memory stays at the workspace, per spec). connection_bindings/studio_changesets DO move (same-account moves only + connections are account-level, so the bound resource stays valid). **Verification (what I actually ran):** `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0; `bunx eslint src/lib/projects.functions.ts` 0; `bun run build` ✓ (3.38s); full `bun test` 274/274; AND a two-pass `BEGIN..ROLLBACK` behavioral dry-run on the LIVE prod DB (Lovable MCP, stubbing the unpublished WM-M2 `account_id` + WM-F3 `can_manage_workspace` + WM-F9 notes/prototypes `workspace_id`, simulating the owner's JWT): moving a real product (`9857019e…`: 9 signals / 2 prds / 10 tasks / 3 decisions / 8 messages) to a same-account destination reassigned the product + EVERY child/grandchild (signals left in src = 0, messages moved 8/8 with 0 orphaned), a cross-account move was blocked ("A product can only move between workspaces in the same account."), and a non-manager caller was blocked ("You must be an owner or admin of the destination workspace."); rolled back, prod untouched. **Marked ◐ (not ✅):** the RPC + server fn are built and behaviorally dry-run-verified on the real prod schema, but there is NO UI affordance yet (deferred to the design pass), and live move activates on the founder's publish (depends on the unpublished WM-M2/F3/F9). **Follow-up WM-F6b:** scope `artifact_lineage` + other generic-provenance tables (their product linkage is via generic artifact ids across tables, deferred this cycle to avoid a wrong remap). **UI breadcrumb (once the UI ships):** Product > Settings > Move to workspace. **Branch:** `overnight/wm` (worktree, fast-forward to `main`). **Next:** WM-M9 (remove self-serve BYOK) or the next non-gated WM/strategy item.

**[DATA-RETENTION, 2026-06-20 00:20, overnight cycle 47] AI-telemetry retention purge (◐; dormant, behaviorally dry-run-verified on prod).** **Pick rationale:** the WM backend lane is thinning; the last in-initiative item WM-M9 (remove self-serve BYOK) is best sequenced with the founder-gated pricing surfaces per its own spec (and removing a live capability at the AI chokepoint while credits are dormant is premature), so it was skip-and-queued. Cross-referencing `docs/planning/considerations.md` surfaced a clean, unclaimed, non-gated P1 gap the WM accounts/tenancy/enterprise thrust genuinely needs: `ai_events` (+ per-call siblings) grow unbounded - one+ row per AI call, forever - a cost/scale and data-minimization (GDPR/CCPA) problem enterprise/team buyers ask about. **What it does:** migration `20260620000000_data_retention.sql` adds `data_retention_enabled()` (a dormant flag returning false, mirroring `credits_enabled()`/`limit_gates_enabled()`) + a SECURITY DEFINER `purge_old_telemetry(_older_than_days integer default 180)` that self-gates on the flag, applies a hard 30-day floor (a mis-call with days=0 floors to 30, so it can NEVER delete recent data), and deletes `ai_events`/`prompt_runs`/`tool_calls` older than the window. New `retention-tick` hook (`src/routes/api/public/hooks/retention-tick.ts`, mirrors `credit-tick`: `requireHookCaller`-gated, `supabaseAdmin` service-role, pre-migration-tolerant). **Decisions:** (1) verified on the live schema that `token_usage` does not exist (token data lives in `ai_events`) and that the 3 target tables have NO inbound foreign-key references (so the deletes neither cascade nor restrict) before writing the purge; (2) made the purge STRICTER than the codebase's other SECURITY DEFINER RPCs - execute revoked from public/anon/authenticated, granted to `service_role` only - because a global telemetry purge is destructive and no authenticated user should trigger it; (3) the function self-gates (`{skipped:dormant}`) so even a direct pg_cron call is inert until the flag flips; (4) deferred the right-to-be-forgotten per-account/workspace erase cascade (DATA-RETENTION-b) as destructive + policy-coupled. **Verification (what I actually ran):** `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0 (after the build regenerated `routeTree.gen.ts` to register the new route); `bunx eslint` 0 on the new hook; `bun run build` ✓ (3.19s); full `bun test` 287/287; AND a `BEGIN..ROLLBACK` behavioral dry-run on the LIVE prod DB (Lovable MCP, backdating two real `ai_events` rows to 200d and 50d): flag false → `skipped:dormant`, deleted nothing (200d row survived); flag true → `purge_old_telemetry(180)` deleted the 200d row and KEPT the 50d row; `purge_old_telemetry(0)` floored to 30 days and deleted the 50d row; rolled back, prod untouched. **Marked ◐ (not ✅):** built + behaviorally dry-run-verified on the real schema, but it stays DORMANT until the founder (a) flips `data_retention_enabled()` to `select true` and (b) wires a pg_cron / external scheduler to POST `/api/public/hooks/retention-tick`; live purge activates only then. **Follow-up DATA-RETENTION-b:** the right-to-be-forgotten erase cascade. **UI breadcrumb:** none (cron + DB plumbing). **Branch:** `overnight/wm` (worktree, fast-forward to `main`). **Next:** the WM lane is near-dry on clean backend items; weigh WM-M9 (chokepoint, founder-surface-coupled) vs the next v9/v8/considerations item.

New `listExportLog` read fn (RLS-scoped, newest-first, capped at 100). **Decisions:** (1) the audit-write is BEST-EFFORT and wrapped in try/catch - the export is the user's data-portability right and must never fail because the audit row could not be written (e.g. pre-migration, before `export_log` is published); (2) append-only (no update/delete policy) over a "soft delete" so the trail cannot be tampered with by authenticated users; (3) write via the user's RLS-scoped `context.supabase` (cast to the untyped `SupabaseClient` for the not-yet-typed table, the codebase's established pattern) with `user_id` defaulting to `auth.uid()` and a with-check `user_id = auth.uid()`; rolled back, prod untouched. **Marked ◐ (not ✅):** the audit table + the per-export write + the read fn are built and behaviorally dry-run-verified on the real schema, but U6 stays ◐ because its export-history UI (DataExportCard) is deferred to the design pass, and live audit rows accrue only after the founder's publish. **Adversarial review folded one fix:** wrapped `recordExport` in try/catch so an unexpected throw from `.insert()` can never fail the user's export (bulletproofing the best-effort intent). **UI breadcrumb (once the UI ships):** Settings > Data > Export history. **Branch:** `overnight/wm` (worktree, fast-forward to `main`). **Next:** the clean my-lane backend lane is thinning; **[APP-HEALTH, 2026-06-20 02:10, overnight cycle 50] public app-level health/readiness endpoint (◐; endpoint + pure assembly unit-verified, live DB-probe + alerting deferred).** **Pick rationale:** the chokepoint bundle (PROVIDER-FALLBACK / PLAN-ENFORCE / MODEL-REGISTRY-DEPRECATION) stays attended; the Data/Privacy vein is now well-mined (3 consecutive: retention c47, export-audit c48, sub-proc c49); the other clean queue items are parallel-lane-owned. It is also genuinely greenfield (new files, zero blast radius to existing code), unlike a core-file edit such as KI-16's mission-advance cap. **What it does:** new route `src/routes/api/public/health.ts` (`GET /api/public/health`) returns HTTP 200 `{status:"ok",...}` healthy or 503 `{status:"degraded",...}` when a dependency is down, so an uptime monitor / load balancer reacts on the STATUS CODE without parsing the body; it runs a cheap, timeout-bounded DB reachability probe and reports per-check states (`worker`, `database`). New pure `src/lib/app-health.ts` (`assembleHealth(checks, nowIso)` → `{body, httpStatus}`). **Decisions:** (1) **public + unauthenticated** (monitors don't auth), so it is designed not to be an attack surface - it leaks NOTHING beyond ok/error check states (no error messages/stack traces; a test asserts the exact response key set), keeps the DB probe trivially cheap (one indexed-id head-read), and bounds it with a 2s timeout (a DoS-amplification guard so a slow DB can't pile up requests); (2) the HTTP status code carries the signal (200/503) so load balancers and monitors need not parse the body; (3) verified `profiles` is a REAL table (queried in onboarding/connections/calendar) before using it as the probe target - the untyped-client trap (HARD GATE 4); (4) kept the status assembly PURE (timestamp injected) so it is fully unit-testable, with only the live DB probe in the route; (5) liveness is implicit (reaching the handler means the worker serves) so no separate liveness check is needed. **Verification (what I actually ran):** `bun run build` ✓ (3.68s, regenerated `src/routeTree.gen.ts` for the new route); `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0; `bunx eslint` 0 on the 3 new files (after a prettier auto-fix); `bun test src/lib/app-health.test.ts` 5/5 (ok→200, db-down→503, worker-always-ok, no-leak exact-key-set, purity); full `bun test` 303/303 (298 prior + 5 new). **Marked ◐ (not ✅):** the endpoint + the pure assembly are built and unit-verified, but the LIVE DB-probe behavior was not run unattended (no live worker; verify with a `curl` on the next publish), and the ALERTING half (wire a monitor → notify) + a status page are infra/founder + design-pass. **Adversarial review:** no runtime-fatal bug - confirmed `profiles` exists, the probe is timeout-bounded + leak-free, every probe path returns a `CheckState` (never throws out of the handler), and the route is a driven live endpoint (not staged). **UI breadcrumb:** none (infra endpoint; a future status page is design-pass). **Branch:** `overnight/wm` (worktree, fast-forward to `main`). **Next:** the clean unattended lane is thinning to lower-impact ops items; weigh the next `considerations.md` P0/P1 gap (e.g. a full-account GDPR data-portability export) vs surfacing to the founder that the high-impact remainder is the attended chokepoint bundle + founder-gated work.

### 2026-06-18

**AGENT-EXP · the agent experience (roster model, faces, identity, the relay).** Resolved the long-standing "19 vs 6" agent question and made the engine legible without a roster. Built in a dedicated worktree (`worktree-agent-experience`, off the overnight tip; not the overnight loop). **Model:** 19+ = a growable backend specialist catalog; 6 stations (Sense, Decide, Define, Build, Ship, Learn) = the spine the user navigates; the cast appears in motion as a relay; the full mesh lives behind one Engine Room door. The catalog (`src/lib/agent-vocabulary.ts`) is the SINGLE source for station/face/tier/hue/glyph (client + server), so NO DB columns were added. **Phase 1 (foundation):** the three-tier catalog + total resolvers (fixes the real bug where seeded slugs like `discovery-scout` mapped to no face and leaked raw names); reconciled `memory-view.ts`; two migrations (`20260618200000` canonical seed of 12 specialists incl. the new `critic` + the `handle_new_user` seed-gap fix; `20260618200100` idempotent backfill that re-seeds every user + re-asserts the roster cut; no schema change, no slug rename); 13 cast system prompts authored + adversarially proofread (parallel workflow) to a fixed skeleton (Role, Objective, Inputs, Steps, Output contract, Guardrails, Handoff, Voice); station-aware orchestrator planning (the planner groups the roster by station and may run parallel specialists within a station). **Phase 2 (the experience):** per-agent identity (`AgentMark`/`AgentBadge`: a hue from a safe agent palette + a unique glyph, color never the only signal; documented as a color-law extension); the `<AgentRelay>` (with `relay.ts` mappers) shown full on the mission lede + mini on Today; the 6-station `LoopStations` spine on Product; the Engine Room "Team" tab (`AgentRosterPanel`, relocating the TrustDial + AgentInspector); retired the Missions roster grid (the Agents tab and the ad-hoc dispatch-from-Today are gone; `/agents`, `/swarm`, and the command palette repoint to `/govern?tab=team`). **Naming:** friendly archetypes (Scout, Researcher, Voice, Strategist, Critic, Scribe, Sketch, Planner, Maker, Reviewer, Herald, Echo, Chief of Staff). Cast vs Crew: crew (Reactor, Archivist) is engine-only, never user-facing. **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `bun run build` green (24.8s), humanized (zero em/en dashes in authored files), lint-clean on every changed file (0 errors; the repo's pre-existing full-lint debt in untouched files is unrelated). **Merged to main 2026-06-18 (this merge); live-verify on publish (especially the signup smoke-test for the `handle_new_user` change, the KI-13 blast radius).** **Files:** new `src/lib/relay.ts`, `src/components/agents/{AgentMark,AgentRelay}.tsx`, `src/components/product/LoopStations.tsx`, `src/components/governance/AgentRosterPanel.tsx`, `supabase/migrations/20260618200000_agentexp_roster.sql`, `20260618200100_agentexp_backfill.sql`; edited `src/lib/agent-vocabulary.ts`, `memory-view.ts` (+ test), `orchestrator.server.ts`, `_authenticated.{index,product,govern,missions.index,missions.$missionId,agents,swarm}.tsx`, `CommandPalette.tsx`, plus docs (`docs/features/agent-experience.md` canonical, `design-context.md`, strategy `README`/`session-decisions`/`strategic-inputs-log`, `feature-dashboard.md`, `SOURCE-OF-TRUTH.md`, this log).
