**D4-REPLAY (cycle 25) · replay-and-branch (re-run a mission with a different model).** The cancel half of D4 shipped earlier; this adds replay-and-branch. The headline ("re-run with a different model") was mostly UI exposure: `startOrchestratedMission`/`StartSchema` already accepted `model` and threaded it to `runAgentLoop`, but the `retry` button never offered the choice. Generalized `retry` into a `replay` mutation with a **model picker + "Replay" button** in the mission header (shown for terminal non-failed missions; the failure panel keeps its contextual replay, default model). Added the **branch link**: migration `20260618160000_d4_replay_branch_link.sql` adds `missions.replayed_from_mission_id` (additive, idempotent, FK `ON DELETE SET NULL` so deleting an original never orphans/cascades) + a partial index; `StartSchema` gained `replayedFrom`, written to the new mission in a SEPARATE pre-migration-tolerant update right after `createMission` (so chat's mission path is untouched and the replay still runs if the column is absent); `getMission` resolves `replayed_from_mission_id` via a SEPARATE error-tolerant read (the main select and the whole detail page keep working before the migration applies); the new mission shows a "Replayed from an earlier mission" link to the parent. Replay re-plans from the goal via the orchestrator, so the model affects both planning and execution (A/B a goal across models). **Decision:** the rich side-by-side checkpoint-diff is deferred as D4b; the branch link is the lightweight diff affordance (open both). **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `bun run build` green, `eslint` clean on the three touched files, humanization scan of additions clean, migration-safety hook passed. **Adversarial review:** no real fix (additive migration, tolerant set + read so pre-migration is safe, no redundant replay affordances between header + failure panel, model defaults to undefined when unset). Clean sync (no parallel commit). **Pending publish + live verify (migration + dispatch + UI).** **Files:** `src/lib/orchestrator.functions.ts`, `src/lib/missions.functions.ts`, `src/routes/_authenticated.missions.$missionId.tsx`, `supabase/migrations/20260618160000_d4_replay_branch_link.sql`, `docs/features/d4-mission-cancellation.md`, `docs/planning/feature-dashboard.md`, `docs/planning/SOURCE-OF-TRUTH.md`, `docs/strategy/session-decisions.md`, `docs/planning/overnight-build-report.md`, this log.

**K2 (cycle 24) · operator revert-to-revision (one-action rollback).** The Build engine recorded a revision per `studio.commit` (I1b) but had no way to roll back. K2 adds a confirm-gated "Revert" button on every prior revision in the Changes tab. New shared helper `src/lib/ai/studio-revert.server.ts` (`revertChangesetToRevision`) performs a NON-DESTRUCTIVE revert via the GitHub Git Data API: GET the target revision's commit tree, GET the current branch head, POST a new commit `{ tree: targetTree, parents: [headSha] }`, then PATCH the ref with `force:false`. History only moves forward (the revert is itself a normal, revertible commit) and a stale-parent race is refused by GitHub rather than clobbering work; the revert is recorded as the next revision. `revertToRevision` (server fn in `studio.functions.ts`) resolves GitHub auth for the changeset's workspace via `resolveGitHub` and delegates to the helper. The ChangesPanel button (`useConfirm`-gated) shows only while the branch is live (`committed`/`pr_open`) and never on the latest revision (a no-op). The helper is self-contained (its own gh fetch helpers, no `registry.server.ts` import) so a future `studio.revert` agent engine-tool can reuse it without a circular dependency. **No migration.** **Decision (operator-first):** shipped the operator door first because it needs no `agent_tools` migration, is self-authorizing (the human clicks), and is the literal "revert button" the spec names; the agent engine-tool (K2b) is deferred since the loop only exposes tools seeded in `agent_tools`. **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `bun run build` green, `eslint` clean on all three touched files, humanization scan of additions clean. **Adversarial review:** no real fix (non-destructive by construction, revision lookup scoped to the changeset, GitHub commit applied before the best-effort revision record so a DB hiccup can't falsely report a failed revert, queries RLS-scoped). Clean sync (no parallel commit). **Pending publish + live verify (GitHub mutation + UI).** **Files:** new `src/lib/ai/studio-revert.server.ts`, `src/lib/studio.functions.ts`, `src/components/studio/ChangesPanel.tsx`, `docs/features/studio.md`, `docs/planning/feature-dashboard.md`, `docs/planning/SOURCE-OF-TRUTH.md`, `docs/strategy/session-decisions.md`, `docs/planning/overnight-build-report.md`, this log.

**P4-GATE (cycle 23) · eval-regression as a hard merge gate.** The Studio/Build merge tool `studio.pr.merge` was hard-gated only on CI (the J2 gate, `studio-ci.ts`). P4-GATE adds its quality-side twin so the BUILD→SHIP loop cannot ship code unattended while output quality is measurably regressing. New pure module `src/lib/ai/eval-gate.ts` (`evalRegressionReadiness` + `EVAL_REGRESSION_THRESHOLD_PTS = 10` + `SuiteScorePair`), mirroring `studio-ci.ts`: given the latest-vs-prior completed avg_score per suite (0-100), it blocks if any suite dropped ≥10 points, naming the worst. The merge tool (`registry.server.ts`) reads the user's completed `eval_runs` (latest two per suite, `.eq("user_id")` + `status='completed'` + non-null avg_score, ordered desc, capped at 80), fetches suite names, and throws `MergeBlocked` when not allowed, right after the existing CI gate, inside the same `if (!prJson.merged)` block. **Scale:** avg_score is 0-100 (confirmed via `20260614160000_p3_ki14_eval_score_0to100.sql`), so the threshold is 10 points on 0-100. **Semantics (J2-analogous):** evals run on a schedule (`eval-tick`), so the gate reads the already-measured trend and never triggers a run; it is read-only, degrades to allowed when no suite has two completed runs, and the operator can always merge from GitHub directly (the gate governs only the agent's tool). **No migration.** **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `bun run build` green, `eslint` clean on both touched files, humanization scan of additions clean. **Adversarial review:** no real fix (0-100 scale correct, drop = prior minus latest is the correct direction, `Number()` coercion + the non-null DB filter make NaN/null safe, both queries explicitly user-scoped). Clean sync (no parallel commit this cycle). **Pending publish + live verify.** **Files:** new `src/lib/ai/eval-gate.ts`, `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts`, `docs/features/studio.md`, `docs/planning/feature-dashboard.md`, `docs/planning/SOURCE-OF-TRUTH.md`, `docs/strategy/session-decisions.md`, `docs/planning/overnight-build-report.md`, this log.

**P5-ALERT (cycle 22) · drift threshold → in-app Attention feed.** Drift was a passive watcher: the detector (`ai/drift.server.ts`) opens `drift_incidents` rows when a metric crosses the user's baseline, but they only showed on the `/drift` page. P5-ALERT surfaces them where the operator already looks: a 4th probe in `getNotifications` (`src/lib/notifications.functions.ts`) reads open `drift_incidents` (most-recent 6, over the existing `(user_id, status, detected_at)` index) and pushes them into the R3 Attention feed as severity-coded cards. Severity maps `critical` → warning, anything else → info (drift is a heads-up, never a human-decision "action"); the card names the drifted metric (latency / cost / token use / error rate / quality score, via a label map) with the signed `delta_pct` vs baseline + the surface and model, and links to `/drift`. **No migration** (live-derived from an existing table, same pattern as the approval/stall/budget probes), capped so a noisy week cannot flood the feed, degrades to no items on error. **No UI change needed:** both consumers (`NotificationsPanel`, `AttentionBell`) key off `severity`, not `kind`, so adding the `drift` kind to the union was enough. **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `bun run build` green, `eslint` clean on the touched file, humanization scan of additions clean. **Adversarial review:** no real fix (numeric `delta_pct` coercion is `Number.isFinite`-guarded, severity safe-defaults to info, query is RLS-scoped + explicitly `.eq("user_id")`). Clean sync (no parallel/runaway commit this cycle). **Pending publish + live verify.** **Files:** `src/lib/notifications.functions.ts`, `docs/features/r3-notifications.md`, `docs/planning/feature-dashboard.md`, `docs/planning/SOURCE-OF-TRUTH.md`, `docs/strategy/session-decisions.md`, `docs/planning/overnight-build-report.md`, this log.

**F-AGENTS-MENTIONABLE (cycle 21) · composer @-picker + case-insensitive parse, feature completed.** The server half of this feature (parse `@agentslug` → pre-planned single-step `mission_steps` dispatch via `advanceMissionCore`; see the cycle-19-labeled entry below for the server design) was auto-committed mid-build by a parallel process (`40646dce0a` + report `ffbf5c50c0`) while the main loop was still working the same worktree, so the committed `chat.ts` already matched the main loop's server work. This cycle layered the genuinely-new value on top: (1) the **composer @-agent picker** in `_authenticated.chat.tsx`, a floating list above the composer (reuses `listAgents`, filtered to enabled non-orchestrator agents) with arrow-key nav + Enter/Tab/click to insert `@slug `; the picker drives those keys ONLY while open, so the Enter-to-send path is byte-identical when it is closed and can never be hijacked; placeholder + helper line advertise the affordance; (2) a **case-insensitive parse fix** in `chat.ts` (`parseAgentMentions` `/gi` + lowercased candidate, `stripMention` `i` flag) so a manually-typed `@Strategist` resolves to the lowercase `strategist` slug, matching the composer's already-case-insensitive `detectMentionQuery`. **Why single-step DAG (not "just run the agent"):** `maybeCompleteMission` keys off `steps.length > 0`; a mission with zero steps and no orchestrator run hangs at `running` forever, so the mention pre-plans one step and lets the deterministic `advanceMissionCore` cron dispatch + finalize it (cheaper + faster than the orchestrator path, exact agent honored). **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `bun run build` green, `eslint` clean on both touched files, humanization scan of additions clean (zero em/en dashes). **Adversarial review folded one real fix:** the server parse was case-sensitive while the composer was not, so a typed `@Strategist` would silently miss; made both case-insensitive. **Process note (recurring):** a background process is committing/pushing autonomously again (same pattern as the F3 `c304bf6396` incident); logged in `session-decisions.md`. **Pending publish + live verify.** **Files:** `src/routes/_authenticated.chat.tsx` (composer @-picker), `src/routes/api/chat.ts` (case-insensitive parse), `docs/features/agents-mentionable.md` (new), `docs/features/README.md`, `docs/planning/feature-dashboard.md`, `docs/planning/SOURCE-OF-TRUTH.md`, `docs/strategy/session-decisions.md`, `docs/planning/overnight-build-report.md`, this log.

**F3-CRON (cycle 20) · continuous auto-cluster, built gated-off, verified + closed.** The auto-cluster cron deferred at cycles 11/17 (recurring AI spend = founder-gated) is now BUILT in the autonomous-safe shape: shipped off by default so applying it commits zero spend, with the recurring-spend scheduler left as the one founder activation step. Extracted the LLM clustering body into a shared core `clusterSignalsCore` (`src/lib/ai/cluster.server.ts`) called by both the user-triggered `clusterSignals` and a new `cluster-tick` hook (`src/routes/api/public/hooks/cluster-tick.ts`); the core explicitly filters `signals.user_id` so the service-role cron path (RLS off) clusters one owner at a time (never across users), passes `workspaceId` so the kill-switch + budget caps still govern spend, and stamps `themes.workspace_id` explicitly (the cron has no `auth.uid()` for the DB default). Owner-gated `getWorkspaceClusterSettings` / `toggleAutoCluster` server fns back a "Auto-cluster new signals" toggle in `SignalsPanel.tsx` (owner-only, shows last-run time). Migration `20260618140000_f3_auto_cluster.sql` adds `workspaces.auto_cluster_enabled` (NOT NULL DEFAULT false) + `last_auto_cluster_at` + a partial index for the cron query; additive, idempotent, zero spend on apply. The cron is batch-capped at 5 workspaces (oldest-run-first) and tolerates the pre-migration window (`42703`/`PGRST204` soft-pass). **Adversarial review (prior session) caught + fixed a service-role `workspace_id` NOT-NULL bug.** **Gate (this turn):** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `bun run build` green (the `cluster-tick` route bundles), `eslint` clean on all four touched files, F3 source + migration scan zero em/en dashes. **Activation (founder, section 4 of the SSOT):** apply the migration on publish, owners enable the toggle, then point pg_cron at the hook (snippet in the migration header). **Pending publish + live verify.** **Files:** new `src/lib/ai/cluster.server.ts`, `src/routes/api/public/hooks/cluster-tick.ts`, `supabase/migrations/20260618140000_f3_auto_cluster.sql`; edited `src/lib/discovery.functions.ts`, `src/components/product/SignalsPanel.tsx`, generated `src/integrations/supabase/types.ts` + `src/routeTree.gen.ts`; `docs/features/f3-continuous-discovery.md`, `docs/planning/SOURCE-OF-TRUTH.md`, this log.

**O1 (cycle 19) · provenance in the shared Lineage drawer — gate-green, pending publish.** Extended the O1 provenance slice (root-signal trace) from the two drill surfaces (opportunity, spec/PRD) to the cross-cutting `LineageDrawer`, so "why does this exist?" is answerable wherever lineage opens, not only on two detail pages. A new "Traces back to" section sits below the existing "Came from" parents and reuses `getProvenance` (no new server fn, no migration). It is shown only when the chain is deeper than one hop (`signal_count > 0 && depth > 1`), so it never just duplicates "Came from" for a theme (whose immediate parents already are signals). **Adversarial review folded one fix:** the section listed `source_signals.slice(0, 8)` while the header printed the full `signal_count`, so a deep artifact (>8 root signals) silently dropped the rest; added a "+N more source signals" overflow line so the visible list and the count agree. **Decision:** this was uncommitted in-progress work recovered from the prior session's mid-build rollover; verified sound (field contracts + the `signal` route all check out) and finished rather than discarded. **Verification:** `tsc --noEmit` 0 errors, `eslint` clean, `prettier` clean, `bun run build` green, humanization scan clean. **Files:** `src/components/cadence/LineageDrawer.tsx`, `docs/features/o1-provenance.md`, `docs/planning/feature-dashboard.md`, `docs/planning/overnight-build-report.md`, this log.

**RULE · data minimalism ("every field earns its place") + onboarding `role` removed — landed on `main`.** Founder principle, made a standing convention: we capture nothing by default; no field, input, stored column, or pixel of screen real estate exists unless a _named consumer_ needs it (now, or with a documented credible near-term use), and a captured field ships in the same change as its consumer (no "collect now, use later"). Unearned capture costs the user's time, our storage, privacy surface, and maintenance, forever. **Applied immediately:** an audit of `profiles.role` found it is never mapped to anything — no role→agent config, settings, or gating; its only "use" was being incidentally swept into the chat-grounding JSON blob. The persona that actually customizes the workspace is the onboarding track selector, not a free-text role. So `role` was removed from `BasicDetailsStep` (name only now); it returns only when wired to a real consumer (e.g. role-based personalization). **What shipped:** new convention [`docs/conventions/data-minimalism.md`](./docs/conventions/data-minimalism.md) (the Value Test + the wiring rule + the narrow future-use clause + the `role` worked example), indexed in the conventions README, wired into [`AGENTS.md`](./AGENTS.md) §3.0b (sibling to the Engine-Room Doctrine) + a §5 trigger row ("adding a captured field → run the Value Test first"); `BasicDetailsStep.tsx` role field + state + write removed (docstring explains the name-only-by-design choice). **Verification:** `tsc --noEmit` 0 errors, `eslint` clean, `bun run build` green. **Files:** `docs/conventions/data-minimalism.md` new, `docs/conventions/README.md`, `AGENTS.md` (§3.0b + §5), `src/components/onboarding/BasicDetailsStep.tsx`, this log.

**ONBOARDING · basic-details step + credentials-only signup (fixes the OAuth `abc.def` name) — shipped on `main` (no migration).** Founder report: a Google signup had no name, so the whole app addressed the user by the email local-part (`abc.def`). Root cause: identity capture was asymmetric — email/password grabbed name inline at `/signup`, the Google path captured nothing and the `handle_new_user` trigger only ever set `full_name` (never `display_name`), so both greeting surfaces fell back to `email.split("@")[0]`. **Decision (founder deferred the call):** adopt the industry-standard split (Linear/Notion/Vercel) — authenticate first, capture profile second, prefilled from the OAuth provider — rather than keep name on the signup form for one path only. **What shipped:** (1) new `src/components/onboarding/BasicDetailsStep.tsx` — first/last name + role, the single identity-capture surface for BOTH signup paths; rendered as the first gate in `OnboardingFlow` only when the profile lacks a `display_name`; prefills from auth `user_metadata` (`given_name`/`family_name`/`full_name`) for Google, blank for bare email, and NEVER seeds from the email local-part; on submit writes BOTH `profiles` (via `updateProfile`) AND auth `user_metadata` (via `supabase.auth.updateUser`) because Today reads the profiles row while the AppShell chip + chat header read the session metadata — fixing one without the other leaves the wrong name on the other surface. (2) `/signup` reduced to credentials only (email + password + Google); name/role inputs removed; profile upsert now `{ onboarded: false }` so the gate routes into onboarding where the details step runs. (3) Fixed a pre-existing humanized-output violation (em-dash in the password placeholder). **Engine-Room:** none (calm-front identity capture). **Verification:** `tsc --noEmit` 0 errors, `eslint` clean, `bun run build` green, and both screens visually verified on-brand via a throwaway preview route + Playwright at 1440px (Ember Editorial: parchment, ember reserved for the single CTA, serif italic-em title, mono-label kicker; preview route reverted before commit). Live walkthrough (fresh Google signup → name prefilled → setup) confirms on the next publish. **Files:** `src/components/onboarding/BasicDetailsStep.tsx` new, `src/components/onboarding/OnboardingFlow.tsx`, `src/routes/signup.tsx`, `docs/features/auth-flows.md`, `docs/features/onboarding-tracks.md`, this log.

**HOTFIX · onboarding track-pick crashed every new user with an RLS error — fixed on `main` (no migration).** The published demo blocked at "Setup · Step 1 of 4": clicking any track (Solo PM / Founding PM / Tech Founder) raised **"new row violates row-level security policy for table 'projects'"**, and the user could not enter the app. **Root cause (systematic-debugging, traced through the migrations):** `seedWorkspaceForTrack` inserts into `projects` / `signals` / `opportunities` without setting `workspace_id`, trusting the `current_user_default_workspace()` column default added in the tenancy retrofit (`20260530120200_tenancy_c`). That migration also swapped those tables' write RLS from `auth.uid() = user_id` to **membership-keyed** `is_workspace_member(workspace_id)`. The default resolves to the caller's earliest `workspace_members` row — but a brand-new user reaches onboarding (their first write) before that row reliably exists: `handle_new_user()` calls `ensure_default_workspace()` inside a swallow-all `EXCEPTION WHEN OTHERS` block, that function isn't in our migrations (Lovable-managed, drift-prone, and the KI-13 saga shows the trigger body keeps getting reverted), and demo accounts skip the provisioning entirely. No membership → `is_workspace_member(NULL)` is false → the `projects` INSERT is rejected. Every track button fails identically because they all hit the same insert. **Fix:** made onboarding self-healing. New `ensureDefaultWorkspace(supabase, userId)` helper in `onboarding.functions.ts` resolves the default workspace via the RPC, else reuses an owned-but-unmembered workspace, else creates `workspaces {owner_id, name}` + the owner `workspace_members` row (all permitted to the user-scoped client by the `ws owner manage` / `owner manages members` policies); `seedWorkspaceForTrack` calls it first and sets `workspace_id` **explicitly** on all three inserts — the path migration C documented as intended ("set workspace_id explicitly in server functions"). Defense-in-depth: onboarding can no longer fail this way even after signup provisioning is repaired. **Why a server-function fix, not a migration:** it ships on the next Lovable publish with no migration-sync gate (the exact gate that keeps reverting `handle_new_user`). **Verification:** `tsc --noEmit` 0 errors (the real gate), `eslint` clean, `prettier` clean, `bun run build` green. Live proof requires a fresh non-demo signup → pick a track after republish (could not reproduce locally — Supabase MCP unauthenticated this session). **Standing follow-up:** the deeper signup-provisioning fragility (`ensure_default_workspace` absent from repo migrations + swallowed in the trigger) remains a known issue — see `docs/planning/known-issues.md`. **Files:** `src/lib/onboarding.functions.ts`, `docs/features/onboarding-tracks.md`, `docs/planning/known-issues.md`, this log.

**Onboarding · first-run gate fix + 4-step redesign — shipped on `main`.** The founder published W6 and signed up with Google: onboarding never appeared, landing straight on Home. **Root cause:** the first-run gate (`_authenticated.tsx` + `onboarding-gate.ts`) redirects only on `profiles.onboarded === false`, but the only path that reliably wrote that flag was the email/password client-side upsert in `signup.tsx`; the Google (Lovable OAuth) path has no such write and leans on the unreliable `handle_new_user` trigger (KI-13), whose resilient body swallows a failed profile insert. So an OAuth signup had no profile row, and the gate's "missing row counts as onboarded" fail-open rule sent them past onboarding. **Fix:** the gate now treats a missing row as a brand-new account, upserts `{ onboarded: false }` (ignoreDuplicates, never clobbers an existing row) and routes into first-run, making the gate the single source of truth for every signup path (`82281c21c3`). **Redesign** (founder: "UI/UX looks crap, no value"): built in an isolated `git worktree` (a parallel session was actively resetting the main tree and had already wiped the uncommitted fix once) with `impeccable` (onboard) + `emil-design-eng` against the Ember Editorial canon; all 4 steps rendered + screenshotted via a throwaway preview harness (reverted before merge). Step 1 `TrackSelector` now names the outcome — each persona card previews the real workspace + first teardown it delivers, read from the seed data — instead of "we'll seed sample data"; steps 2-4 get serif italic-em titles (`listen` / `staff` / `goal`), value copy that names the outcome, and the user-facing em-dashes removed (humanized-output); ember reserved for the single CTA; staggered transform-only entrance + `.lift` press feedback, reduced-motion gated (`40a0f51a5b`, `00a051a1c3`). Logic, mutations, and the founder skip-as-primary ruling unchanged. **Verification:** `tsc` / `eslint` / `prettier` / `bun run build` all green; the OAuth round-trip is verifiable only on the next publish. **Files:** `src/lib/onboarding-gate.ts`, `src/components/onboarding/TrackSelector.tsx`, `src/components/onboarding/OnboardingFlow.tsx`, `docs/features/onboarding-tracks.md`, `docs/features/README.md` (W6 index row), `docs/planning/feature-dashboard.md`, this log.

**DEC-02-LOOP · the Critic promoted to a routable agent-loop tool — built + tsc/build-verified on `main`.** Closes the v10 M-B "Critic as an explicit loop step" item with the _safe_ increment (recon blueprint from a 3-reader engine map): make the Critic a registered, agent-callable tool WITHOUT touching the fragile mission-DAG machinery. Before, `runCritic` was a private fn in `discovery.functions.ts` reachable only from 4 inline call sites; now the orchestrator or any specialist can red-team an opportunity/PRD **in-loop**. **What shipped:** (1) extracted `runCritic` + `CriticReview` verbatim into new `src/lib/ai/critic.server.ts` + a `runCriticTool({target_kind,target_id}, ctx)` adapter (never throws; returns `{ok, review}`); (2) `discovery.functions.ts` imports `runCritic` and re-exports the `CriticReview` type (≈8 modules import it from there) — the 4 call sites + `runCriticReview` ("Re-run Critic" badge) behave identically; (3) registered `critic.evaluate` (category `planning`) in `TOOL_REGISTRY`; (4) added `critic.evaluate` to `ORCHESTRATION_CONTROL_FLOW_TOOLS` in `loop.server.ts` so it runs inline (the verdict is advisory + side-effect-free beyond the row's `critic_review`; gating it could strand a run); (5) migration `20260617160000` seeds it into `agent_tools` for new users (via `seed_default_agent_tools`, mirrored verbatim + 1 row) and backfills existing users — does NOT touch `handle_new_user`. **Deferred (Phase 2):** the full `mission_steps` DAG-node promotion — the recon flagged it touches the handoff completion-guard (an unconsumed critic step hangs the mission / trips the orphan-sweep), bounded-retry on a non-deterministic judge, and verdict-routing; **hard rule: a `kill` verdict stays advisory, never auto-fails dependent steps.** **Adversarial review** (3 perspective-diverse lenses): behavior-equivalence APPROVE (byte-identical), engine-correctness/security APPROVE (RLS-scoped via `ctx.supabase`, no cross-tenant reach, no DAG/mission-advance edits), migration-safety APPROVE_WITH_FIXES (1 MEDIUM: aligned the DB tool description with the registry, added the omitted kill-criteria). **Verification:** `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0 errors (the real gate); **"Agent manager" framing decision (Part A, docs-only) — LANDED on `main` workflow.** A founder brainstorm ("2026 is the year of the agent manager") proposed surfacing an explicit, named "Agent Manager" in-app and on the landing page, showing every agent's task + consumption (cost, API, time, output, efficiency). **MOAT-VIS · make the compounding visible (v10 P0 #3) — SHIPPED to `main`.** Picked the next v10 item after WEDGE. **Recon (background Explore agent over the just-shipped LRN-02 loop) reframed the work:** the `learnings` table already stores the rescore (`prior_ice → new_ice`) and its cause (verdict + summary) directly, with an FK to `opportunities`, and the LRN-02 work already renders the raw rescore on _both_ target surfaces — Today's "What changed" card and Brain's `MemoryPanel`. And `countPriorityMoves` (the literal "this learning moved these priorities" metric) existed but was only wired into the Gauntlet, never shown on Brain. Built three lockstep pieces: (1) enriched `listLearnings` (`outcome.functions.ts`) to embed `opportunity:opportunities(title)` and **flatten to `opportunity_title`** — additive and back-compatible, and **precisely typed** (not `unknown`-widened) so callers keep strong field types; `numeric` ICE columns arrive as strings over PostgREST so the type is `number | string | null` and callers keep coercing with `Number()`; (2) Brain `MemoryPanel` rescore rows now read _"moved **{opportunity}** · ICE x → y"_ and the Product-memory rail gains a **"Priorities moved"** stat via the existing `countPriorityMoves` helper (the same honest metric the Gauntlet reads, over the loaded learnings); (3) Today's "What changed" card now **names the moved opportunity** instead of "a priority" (the data flows for free from the enriched fn). **A real type trap was caught and fixed before it shipped:** my first cut typed the flattened row with an index signature (`[k: string]: unknown`), which would have weakened `latestRescore.verdict` to `unknown` and broken Today's JSX (`{latestRescore.verdict}` is not a valid `ReactNode`) — the original returned `any` so it had compiled; replaced with a precise `LearningWire` type, and `tsc` then confirmed Today renders. **Coordination:** built on the LEARN lane, file-disjoint from WEDGE; the working tree arrived with an **accidental deletion of the committed `WedgeTeardown.tsx`** (WEDGE lane) that broke the whole build (`tsc` error: cannot find the module the committed Today route imports) — restored it from `HEAD` (returns the tree to committed truth; **WEDGE · Critic-teardown first-run (the v10 launch wedge, P0 #2) — SHIPPED to `main`.** Picked the next item in the v10 pick-order after LRN-02. **Recon first (background Explore agent) confirmed the wedge is pure integration, not new capability:** the Critic engine (`runCritic`, DEC-02), the `opportunities` table (`critic_review jsonb`), and the `VerdictChip`/`CriticBadge` renderers already exist, so there is **no new AI infra and no migration** — the work is intake + surface. Built two pieces in lockstep: (1) a server fn `runWedgeTeardown({ idea, problem?, target_user?, project_id? })` in `discovery.functions.ts` that records the idea as an opportunity **verbatim** (neutral ICE 5/5/5 — we don't fake a score the operator didn't give; `missing_evidence` carries most of the first-run value) scoped to the active product, then calls the module-private `runCritic({kind:"opportunity"})` inline, returning `{ opportunity, review }`; and (2) `WedgeTeardown.tsx`, a self-contained form→result surface that leads the **cold-start** "Start here" section on Today (above the existing signal on-ramp), reusing the `VerdictChip` tones. The verdict renders in place (Ship/Revise/Kill + summary + Risks / What would kill it / What you cannot prove yet). **Engine-Room:** the surface names the outcome ("see why your idea might be wrong"), not the machinery; greppable stamp at the top of the component. **Adversarial self-review caught one real correctness bug:** the first teardown creates the workspace's first opportunity, which flips `getColdStart → isCold` to false; because the result renders inside the `isCold` branch, a window-focus refetch of `["cold-start"]` would unmount it and discard the verdict mid-read (`new QueryClient()` uses the v5 defaults, `refetchOnWindowFocus: true`). Fixed two ways: the component holds the result in local state and does **not** invalidate `["cold-start"]`, and the cold-start query now sets `refetchOnWindowFocus: false` + `refetchOnReconnect: false` so it only re-evaluates on a genuine remount. Also handled the no-AI-key path honestly (`review` can be `null` → "Saved, the Critic could not run" fallback, not a broken card), and swapped smart quotes for straight quotes in the one user-facing title line (humanized-output gate). **Verification: `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0 errors (the real type gate — `bun run build` strips types without checking); `bun run lint` shows zero problems in the three changed files.** Full end-to-end (the real cited verdict) needs the deployed app — local dev has no AI key, and cold-start needs an empty workspace. Collision-free from other lanes (new component + one server fn + the cold-start branch of the Today index). **Files:** `src/components/today/WedgeTeardown.tsx`, `docs/features/wedge.md` new; `src/lib/discovery.functions.ts` (`runWedgeTeardown`), `src/routes/_authenticated.index.tsx` (mount + cold-start query hardening); `docs/planning/feature-dashboard.md`, `docs/planning/v10_implementation-plan.md`, `docs/features/README.md`, this log.

**LRN-02 · Outcome reviews — Historian verdict (predicted vs actual) — SHIPPED to `main`.** Picked the v10 P0 #1 (`LRN-02` + `W1-AUTO`, the "close the loop / moat" item). **Recon first saved a rebuild:** the core was already built and the dashboard status was stale — `recordOutcome` already takes a human verdict, re-scores the linked opportunity's ICE, writes a `learnings` row, and (W1-AUTO) calls `rememberOutcome`, which embeds the outcome into a recallable global `agent_memory` row so future runs compound it. So W1-AUTO is done/wired (marked ✅ with evidence), and only the genuine gap vs v10's wording ("predicted vs actual, **Historian verdict**") remained: the verdict was entered **purely manually**. Built that: a new `suggestOutcomeVerdict({prdId, metricLabel?, metricValue?, notes?})` server fn assembles the **prediction** (the opportunity's problem / hypothesis / predicted ICE, plus — once the H2 sync lands — its committed roadmap outcome + measure; read via `select("*")` so it's pre-migration tolerant) and the **actual** signal so far (metric + operator notes), then calls the AI chokepoint (reusing `surface:"judge"` so it needs no edit to the shared `runtime.server.ts` — collision-free with the parallel engine lane) for strict JSON `{predicted, verdict, summary}`, enum-clamps the verdict (validated/missed/mixed, default mixed), and returns it. On the `OutcomeCard`, a "Draft with Historian" button pre-fills the verdict + summary and shows a "Predicted:" line; the human still confirms and fires the unchanged `recordOutcome`, so the rescore + memory write stay human-gated. The whole thing only DRAFTS — no autonomous write. **Adversarial review (ecc:code-reviewer): APPROVE, 0 HIGH;** folded 1 MED (clear the stale `predicted` line via `onMutate` on a re-draft) + 1 LOW (dropped a no-op `fallbackModel` equal to the primary). Prompt-injection risk assessed LOW (user's own workspace data + enum-clamped output + human-confirm gate). **Verification: `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0 errors, `bunx eslint` clean, `bun run build` green.** **Files:** `src/lib/outcome.functions.ts` (`suggestOutcomeVerdict`), `src/components/product/OutcomeCard.tsx`; `docs/planning/feature-dashboard.md`, this log. (Did NOT commit a stray `headroom-ai` dep that appeared in `package.json` from another lane.)

**OPS-01 audio · real ElevenLabs soundscapes generated (experimental free-tier set).** Connected the ElevenLabs MCP and generated the Flow-mode ambient tracks into `public/soundscape/`. Final set (all ElevenLabs **Sound Effects**, 5s, looped, ~80KB each): **Ocean · Monsoon (rain + temple bells) · Bansuri (flute texture) · Forest (Himalayan) · Heartbeat (bass-rich ~75bpm) · Fireplace**; default is Ocean. Two iterations with the founder: the first cut included **Tanpura** and **Singing bowls**, both removed as too harsh; root cause documented (a 5s SFX loop repeats a transient _attack_ like a pluck/strike every 5s, so it "hits", whereas continuous textures like water, fire, rain, and forest loop invisibly), and the heartbeat was regenerated bassier/punchier. The **Music API (`compose_music`) is paid-only** (free tier returns 402), so real melodic/cultural music (lo-fi raga, a full bansuri melody, Balinese gamelan, a smooth long tanpura) is **deferred with a full pick-up plan + exact prompts** in `public/soundscape/README.md` (the "TODO when on a paid plan" + "Tried and rejected" sections). Presets renamed across `session.ts` / `FlowWidget.tsx` / `use-flow-mode.tsx` (+ test); the audio engine, dim, timer, custom-length, and notification-quieting are unchanged. **License note:** these are committed as an _experimental_ free-tier set (generally non-commercial); confirm commercial terms before treating as production assets (gate recorded in the README table). **Verification:** 21 `bun test` green, `tsc --noEmit` 0 errors, `eslint` clean (one pre-existing react-refresh warning). **Files:** `public/soundscape/*.mp3` (6) + `README.md` new; `src/lib/flow/{session.ts,soundscape.ts}` (+`session.test.ts`), `src/components/cadence/FlowWidget.tsx`, `src/hooks/use-flow-mode.tsx`, `docs/features/flow-mode.md`, this log.

**B5 · Product lifecycle (archive / restore / export / delete) — SHIPPED to `main`.** Built the full product lifecycle onto the `/product` **Portfolio** (the continuation of B3), extracting the inline portfolio into `src/components/product/PortfolioBoard.tsx`. Four per-product actions: **soft archive + restore** (reversible — an Undo toast, and a durable Archived section to restore from; archived products drop out of the sidebar + product tabs), **JSON export** of the product's whole footprint (project + signals + opportunities + specs + tasks — the escape hatch / U6-lite), and an **honest export-then-delete**. The delete follows the destructive-actions doctrine: `useConfirm({ destructive, typedConfirm: name })` (type the exact product name) with **honest copy** — because the FK is `on delete set null`, deleting a product _detaches_ its signals/opps/specs/tasks to the workspace rather than destroying them (the old AppShell sidebar delete's "everything inside it" copy was factually wrong); a JSON snapshot auto-downloads first as the safety net. **Server (`projects.functions.ts`):** new `setProjectArchived({id, archive})` (verified write — `.eq("user_id").select("id")`, throws on 0 rows), `exportProduct({id})` (RLS-scoped reads), hardened `deleteProject` (now a verified delete, not a phantom-ok bare delete); `listProjects` JS-filters archived out (pre-migration tolerant — no SQL reference to the not-yet-existing column) and `getPortfolio`/`PortfolioProduct` gained an `archived` flag. **Migration** `20260617120000_b5_project_archive.sql` adds `archived_at` + a partial index `WHERE archived_at IS NULL`; the existing "own projects all" RLS (FOR ALL on user_id) already scopes it. **Adversarial review (ecc:code-reviewer) caught a real HIGH:** `useConfirm()` returns the confirm fn directly (AppShell does `const confirm = useConfirm()`), so my `const { confirm } = useConfirm()` yielded `undefined` and would have thrown on every delete at runtime — **and the Vite build never caught it because esbuild strips types without checking.** Folded that + two LOWs (verified delete, partial index), and a separate `tsc`-only error the source review couldn't see: the TanStack server-fn boundary rejects a `Record<string, unknown>` return as non-serializable, so `ProductExport` now uses a recursive JSON-safe type. **Verification: `bunx tsc --noEmit` 0 errors (the real type gate — `bun run build` alone is not), `bunx eslint` clean, `bun run build` green.** Collision-free from the parallel engine lane (owns AppShell, which keeps only its bare sidebar delete). **Files:** `src/components/product/PortfolioBoard.tsx`, `supabase/migrations/20260617120000_b5_project_archive.sql` new; `src/lib/projects.functions.ts`, `src/routes/_authenticated.product.tsx` edited; `docs/planning/feature-dashboard.md`, this log.

**H2 · Outcome roadmap (Now/Next/Later) — SHIPPED to `main`.** Built the outcome/commitment layer over the agent-ranked opportunities, as a **Roadmap tab on `/product`** (`?tab=roadmap`). This is explicitly NOT the task/sprint kanban that v6 deleted: the human _commits_ an opportunity to a Now/Next/Later bucket and declares an **outcome** (what changes) + a **measure** (how we know), and the agent's continuous ICE ranking orders the cards _within_ each bucket. Reconciled the v6 `/roadmap` deletion this way (outcome curation, not manual sequencing) rather than reviving the kanban. **Build:** a four-column board (Backlog · Now · Next · Later) with native HTML5 drag (no `@dnd-kit` — that dep isn't installed and the supply-chain guard would block adding it), optimistic move (onMutate snapshot → onError rollback → onSettled invalidate), and inline outcome/measure edit per card. **Data:** new `roadmap.functions.ts` — `getRoadmap` reads `select("*")` so it is **pre-migration tolerant** (until the next Lovable sync adds the columns, every opportunity reads as unplaced and sits in the backlog; reads never error), and `updateRoadmapItem` patches the three roadmap columns. Migration `20260617000000_h2_roadmap_outcome.sql` adds `roadmap_bucket` (CHECK now/next/later) + `roadmap_outcome` + `roadmap_measure` to `opportunities`, idempotent, with a partial index on committed items; the existing "own opportunities all" RLS policy (FOR ALL on user*id) already scopes the new columns, so no new policy. **Adversarial review (3 fixes folded):** (1) the write now does `.eq("user_id", …).select("id")` and throws if zero rows return, so an RLS-blocked or no-match update fails loudly instead of returning a phantom `ok:true` that would leave the optimistic UI lying; (2) added a keyboard/click bucket `<select>` per card (aria-labeled) so bucket-moves aren't drag-only (a11y); (3) the inline edit now resets its outcome/measure fields on save so a stale value can't leak into the next card opened. **Gate:** the place-into-bucket \_write* needs the migration, so it activates on the next Lovable sync; the board reads and renders today (everything in backlog). **Verification:** `bun run build` green, `bunx eslint` clean on all three files. Built collision-free from the parallel engine lane (`/product` + new files only; no AppShell/CommandPalette/Govern). **Files:** `supabase/migrations/20260617000000_h2_roadmap_outcome.sql`, `src/lib/roadmap.functions.ts`, `src/components/product/RoadmapBoard.tsx` new; `src/routes/_authenticated.product.tsx` (Roadmap tab wiring); `docs/planning/feature-dashboard.md`, this log.

**OPS-01 follow-up · Flow audio reworked from synthesis to real recordings + a custom timer (founder feedback).** The founder tested the shipped Flow mode and found all three synthesized presets (Rain/Wind/Deep, filtered white noise) harsh, which defeats a calm-focus feature. Reworked the audio engine: `src/lib/flow/soundscape.ts` is now a real-audio buffer player that fetches one looped recording per preset, decodes it once, loops it gaplessly via Web Audio (an HTMLAudioElement loop seams audibly), and crossfades on preset change with volume on a master gain. New presets are Rain/Ocean/Forest/Lo-fi/Heartbeat. The files live in `public/soundscape/<preset>.mp3` and are sourced separately, because I could not autonomously fetch great, no-attribution, loopable, license-clear audio (Pixabay is gated/403; Wikimedia Commons quality was poor and attribution-encumbered) and cannot audition for quality, so committing scraped audio would be a legal + quality risk. `start()` now resolves a boolean; when a file is absent the preset shows "This sound has no track yet" and stays silent while the rest of Flow mode (dim, timer, quieting) still works. Also added the requested **custom focus length**: a clamped minutes field (1 to 240) beside the 25/50/90/Open chips. `public/soundscape/README.md` documents the exact filenames, royalty-free/CC0 sources, and a per-file license-provenance table. **Verification:** 21 `bun test` green (+4 new: `presetSrc`, `clampMinutes`), `tsc --noEmit` clean, `eslint` clean (same pre-existing provider+hook react-refresh warning), humanization gate clean, dev server serves `/` 200 with no errors. **Decision:** logged in `session-decisions.md` (reverses the original "synthesized in-browser" OPS-01 choice). **Files:** `src/lib/flow/{soundscape.ts,session.ts}` (+`session.test.ts`), `src/hooks/use-flow-mode.tsx`, `src/components/cadence/FlowWidget.tsx`, `public/soundscape/README.md` new; `docs/features/flow-mode.md`, `docs/strategy/session-decisions.md`, this log.

### 2026-06-16

**OPS-01 · Flow mode (ambient calm-state) — SHIPPED.** A one-click calm operating stance, living in the `AppShell` sidebar footer beside the theme toggle (chrome, not Today — it's a global stance, so the home-and-today IA rubric puts it in the chrome). Turning it on dims the sidebar + TopBar (`html.flow`, lifting on hover; main content stays full), plays a synthesized ambient soundscape (Web Audio, no audio files: Rain/Wind/Deep presets are filtered looping noise with a slow LFO, + volume), runs a focus timer (25/50/90/open) that chimes and auto-exits at zero, and **quiets non-urgent notifications**. Quieting is the one structural piece: a `lib/notify.ts` facade re-exports `toast` with sonner's exact API, so a mechanical one-line import swap across **44 files** (`sonner` → `@/lib/notify`) routes every toast through it; while flow is on, success/info/message/default toasts are held in a buffer and replayed as one summary line on exit (`While you were focused · N updates`), while errors/warnings (and anything `{critical:true}`) always pass through. State mirrors `use-theme.tsx` (context + `localStorage` + a documentElement class); no server table. A session resumes across reload (audio re-arms on a tap, per the browser autoplay policy). Engine-Room stamp recorded in the spec. Decisions were founder-chosen in planning: ambient calm-state (not a full-screen room), hold-then-summarize (not silent-suppress), synthesized audio (not bundled files). **Verification:** 163 `bun test` green (+17 new: notify facade + pure session/timer helpers), `tsc --noEmit` clean, `eslint` clean (one pre-existing provider+hook react-refresh warning, same as `use-theme`), humanization gate clean (0 dashes/invisible/buzzwords), dev server boots and serves `/` + `/login` 200 with no import errors. The ESLint regression-guard (ban `toast` from `sonner`) was blocked by the config-protection hook, so the convention is documented in the spec instead. **Files:** `src/lib/notify.ts` (+`.test.ts`), `src/lib/flow/{session.ts,soundscape.ts,chime.ts}` (+`session.test.ts`), `src/hooks/use-flow-mode.tsx`, `src/components/cadence/FlowWidget.tsx` new; `src/routes/_authenticated.tsx` (provider), `src/components/cadence/AppShell.tsx` (footer), `src/styles.css` (`html.flow` + `flowBreathe`), 44 files import-swapped; `docs/features/flow-mode.md` (+ index), `docs/planning/feature-dashboard.md`, `docs/conventions/home-and-today-ia.md`, this log.

**G3 engine lane — adversarial review + 4 fixes (closeout).** Ran an `ecc:typescript-reviewer` correctness+security pass over the riskiest pieces (J2 merge gate, K1 release notes, I1 hunk apply). Fixed: **(HIGH/J2)** the CI gate fetched check-runs at `per_page=50` with no pagination, so a failing check beyond #50 (common in matrix builds) could read as green and let a red PR merge — the dangerous false-allow direction; now `per_page=100` plus a fail-safe block when `total_count` exceeds the page (refuses rather than risks a false allow). **(HIGH/J2)** a closed-but-unmerged PR fell through to the GitHub merge call and returned a misleading "conflicts or pending checks" 405; now a clear `state != "open"` guard throws first. **(MED/I1)** stale hunk-ids from the UI under a concurrent edit could silently corrupt staged content (positional ids shift if `new_content` changed); added optimistic concurrency — the UI passes the row's `updated_at` as `expectedUpdatedAt` and the server's UPDATE is conditional on it, returning a refresh-and-retry conflict instead of writing wrong content. **(MED/K1)** uncapped `studio_changeset_revisions.message` text flowed verbatim into the release-notes prompt (injection surface); each commit message is now capped to 500 chars (matching the work-order cap). The reviewer confirmed the rest correct: `overallFromChecks` priority ordering, `mergeReadinessFromCi` exhaustiveness, the `!merged` guard + gate placement outside `withIdempotency`, `applyHunkSelection` round-trips, the status='staged' guards, and K1 RLS tenancy. `bun test` 146 green, `bun run build` green. **Files:** `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts` (J2 gate), `src/lib/studio.functions.ts` (K1 cap + I1 concurrency), `src/components/studio/ChangesPanel.tsx` (I1 `expectedUpdatedAt`), active-task (closeout + post-deploy verify gate), this log.

**G3 / I1b — Studio changeset revision history — DONE (revert deferred). Engine lane complete.** Each `studio.commit` now records an atomic revision so the operator sees a changeset's commit history in-platform (not only on GitHub). Built: (1) migration `20260616230000_i1b_studio_revisions.sql` — `studio_changeset_revisions` (changeset_id FK, revision_no, commit_sha, commit_url, message, files jsonb), RLS mirroring `studio_changes` (workspace via parent changeset), UNIQUE(changeset_id, revision_no) + index. (2) In `registry.server.ts` `studio.commit`, after the commit succeeds, a best-effort insert of the next revision (revision_no = count+1, sha/url/message + the file set), gated on `!outcome.cached` so an idempotency replay never double-records and wrapped in try/catch so a missing table (pre-sync) or any error never breaks shipping. (3) `getChangesetRevisions` read fn + `StudioRevision` type in `studio.functions.ts` (RLS-scoped, newest first). (4) A compact "Revisions (N)" strip in `ChangesPanel.tsx` (r-number, message, file count, short sha linking to the GitHub commit); the query degrades to a hidden strip if the table is absent pre-sync. Honest scope: **revert-to-revision is deferred** (it needs per-revision content storage or git operations; the history view is the valuable non-speculative core). **Verification:** full `bun test` 146 green, `bun run build` green. Migration applies on the next Lovable sync; UI/insert need a live commit flow to fully e2e. **G3 engine lane (I3 → J1 → J2 → I1 → I1b) is COMPLETE.** **Files:** `supabase/migrations/20260616230000_i1b_studio_revisions.sql` new, `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts` (revision insert), `src/lib/studio.functions.ts` (read fn + type), `src/components/studio/ChangesPanel.tsx` (revisions strip), dashboard/active-task/this log.

**G3 / I1 (per-hunk accept/reject) — operator curation of a staged changeset — DONE; revision history deferred (I1b).** Multi-file staging already shipped (`studioStage`, up to 20 files); the gap was operator control before the gated commit (all-or-nothing). Built: (1) pure `src/lib/ai/studio-hunks.ts` — `computeHunks(base, modified)` (LCS line diff to stable-id hunks) + `applyHunkSelection(base, modified, rejectedIds)` (rejected hunks revert to base; no rejections reconstructs `modified` exactly, all rejections reconstructs `base`), 11 tests incl. round-trips, partial accept, trailing-newline, create/delete edges. (2) Two workspace-scoped server fns in `studio.functions.ts`, gated to `status='staged'` (cannot curate after commit, since the content is then on the branch): `applyStagedHunkSelection` (recompute `new_content` from the rejected set via the same pure fn the UI used, so hunk ids line up) and `rejectStagedFile` (drop a whole file). (3) `ChangesPanel.tsx` UI (engine lane owns it; the I2 watch-lane must not touch it): when the changeset is `staged`, each file shows its hunks with tap-to-reject + an Apply button, plus a Reject-file button; refetches via partial key `["studio-session"]` so it stays decoupled from the I2 route. Honest scope: "atomic revision history" (the other half of the original I1) is split out as **deferred I1b** (needs a `studio_changeset_revisions` table + commit-time snapshots, a distinct slice) rather than half-built. **Verification:** `studio-hunks.test.ts` 11/11, full `bun test` 146 green, `bun run build` green. UI interaction needs a live staged changeset to fully e2e (same limit as all Studio UI). **Engine lane (I3 → J1 → J2 → I1) complete.** **Files:** `src/lib/ai/studio-hunks.ts` (+`.test.ts`) new, `src/lib/studio.functions.ts` (import + 2 fns), `src/components/studio/ChangesPanel.tsx` (curation UI), dashboard/active-task/this log.

**G3 / J1 + J2 (honest path) — test-authoring discipline + CI-green merge gate — DONE.** Founder ruling: the Studio engine is GitHub-API-only (no Cadence execution sandbox), so a `studio.test.run` runner + `studio_test_runs` table would be speculative; tests run in the connected repo's GitHub Actions CI, which `github.ci.read` already reads. So the honest decomposition: J1 = the agent AUTHORS tests; J2 = enforce CI-green-before-merge. **J1:** migration `20260616220000_j1_studio_test_discipline.sql` rewrites the Studio (`builder`) agent system prompt to make test-authoring an explicit step (step 4 "INCLUDE TESTS", step 2 "note how the repo runs tests", step 7 "the tests you added") and restates the CI-green-before-merge loop; `CREATE OR REPLACE seed_default_agents` (other 3 agents reproduced verbatim, Studio prompt via `$studio$` dollar-quoting) for new users + a scoped `UPDATE ... WHERE slug='builder'` backfill for existing. Applies on the next Lovable sync. **J2:** new pure `src/lib/ai/studio-ci.ts` (`overallFromChecks` derives the verdict, `mergeReadinessFromCi` decides merge-readiness; 12 tests), now the single source of truth shared with `github.ci.read` (its inline derivation replaced). `studio.pr.merge` does a fresh CI read before merging and throws `MergeBlocked` while CI is red or pending (a Cadence-level gate independent of GitHub required-checks), kept outside `withIdempotency` so a blocked attempt re-checks each time and only a green merge caches. The gate is fail-safe (only ever blocks, never wrongly allows). With the J1 fix-on-red prompt, the self-correct loop closes without speculative orchestration. Known limit: a perpetually-queued check reads `pending` forever and blocks Cadence-merge (operator merges on GitHub if needed). **Verification:** `studio-ci.test.ts` 12/12, full `bun test` 135 green, `bun run build` green. Migration unverifiable live until Lovable sync (Supabase MCP unauthenticated here), like every migration in this repo. **Files:** `src/lib/ai/studio-ci.ts` (+`.test.ts`) new, `supabase/migrations/20260616220000_j1_studio_test_discipline.sql` new, `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts` (import + shared verdict + merge gate + tool description), dashboard/active-task/this log.

**G3 / I3 — branch isolation per mission, collision-safe branch naming — DONE.** The Studio build engine already isolates concurrent missions well: per-path `builder_file_claims` (a second mission touching the same file gets a typed `BuilderFileConflict`, claims auto-released on merge/terminal), a per-mission `studio/*` branch, idempotent commit/PR/merge, and a clean open→squash-merge→release path. The one latent isolation bug: the branch fallback `studio/${missionId.slice(0,8)}` truncated the mission UUID to 32 bits, so two concurrent missions whose UUIDs shared a leading hex prefix would compute the SAME branch and silently build on each other's head (the file-claim guard only catches same-FILE collisions, not two missions sharing a branch with different files). Fixed by binding the branch to the changeset's own UUID: new pure `src/lib/ai/studio-branch.ts` `studioBranchName(missionId, changesetId)` → `studio/<mission8>-<changeset12>`, an always-valid single git ref segment, now the only place the branch name is computed (`registry.server.ts` `studio.commit`). Backward-compatible: only the first-commit fallback changed; existing changesets keep their persisted `branch`, and no consumer recomputes the name (`studio.functions.ts` reads `changeset.branch` from the DB). No migration. **Verification:** new `studio-branch.test.ts` 6/6 (incl. the explicit regression: two missions sharing an 8-hex prefix now get different branches), full `bun test` 123 green, `bun run build` green. Engine-core lane, serial; next J1. **Files:** `src/lib/ai/studio-branch.ts` (+`.test.ts`) new, `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts` (import + branch line), dashboard/active-task/this log.

**Viral loop · per-IP rate limit on the public `/d/<slug>` page — DONE (closes the one deferred gate before heavy promotion).** The shareable-decision page was the only public, unauthenticated read surface with no rate limit (the explicitly-deferred item from the 2026-06-16 share-security re-verification). Added a per-IP cap on the anonymous `getPublicDecision` read: 600 reads / 1-hour rolling window per client IP, mirroring KI-10's ingest limiter shape. The guard runs _before_ the DB read, keyed on `cf-connecting-ip` (Cloudflare-set → unspoofable on the Workers deploy; `x-forwarded-for`/`x-real-ip` are dev fallbacks). It is **fail-open** by construction (any DB error or unresolved IP → the read proceeds), so the limiter can never make a legitimate shared link 404; a blocked caller sees the same "not available" page as a private/missing slug, which is fine because slugs are unguessable CSPRNG (this is anti-DoS, not anti-enumeration). The window/limit math is a pure `decidePublicReadRateLimit` with 7 `bun test` cases (boundary at exactly windowMs, increment, block + retry-after, count-overshoot race, custom params); the DB wrapper uses `onConflict: "client_ip"` on the UNIQUE key so a window reset UPDATEs rather than inserting a duplicate. Bundle-safety verified: the service-role `supabaseAdmin` import (a lazy Proxy) compiles into the server-only chunk and leaks nothing to the client bundle (grep-confirmed). **Verification:** `bun test` 108 green (+7), `bun run build` green, client bundle clean of `SERVICE_ROLE`/the limiter table. **Gate:** the migration applies on the next Lovable sync (until then `public_decision_rate_limits` doesn't exist, the checker fails open, and reads are unlimited — exactly today's behavior). Built file-disjoint from the parallel M-A Slice 2 (Today) lane. **Files:** `supabase/migrations/20260616190000_p3_public_decision_ratelimit.sql`, `src/lib/decisions-ratelimit.server.ts` (+`.test.ts`) new; `src/lib/decisions-share.functions.ts` (guard + IP resolver) edited; `docs/features/shareable-decisions.md`, `active-task.md`, this log.

**M-C pricing and paywall foundation: plan tier + entitlements + billing surface + gated Stripe (BUILT, working tree).** The monetization foundation from v7 section 9. `workspaces` gains `plan_tier` (free/pro/team, default free), the two stripe ids, and `plan_updated_at`, with a `BEFORE INSERT OR UPDATE` trigger (`protect_workspace_billing_columns`) that makes the billing columns service-role-write-only: a non-service-role INSERT is forced to free with no billing ids, a non-service-role UPDATE preserves the prior values. So a free user cannot self-grant a paid plan by PATCHing or INSERTing the column directly (the `ws owner manage` RLS policy is FOR ALL, so both write paths had to be guarded, not just UPDATE). Pure `src/lib/entitlements.ts` (free does not persist memory, retention 14 days; pro and team persist forever; Critic-everywhere + team-only shared memory / approval lanes) with 9 `bun test` cases and a fail-safe `normalizePlanTier` that defaults unknown values to free. `src/lib/billing.functions.ts`: `getBillingState` (authed, pre-migration tolerant, defaults free) + owner-only `createCheckoutSession` (Stripe Checkout via the REST API over fetch, no SDK dependency, gated on `STRIPE_SECRET_KEY` + a price id). `src/routes/api/stripe/webhook.ts` verifies the Stripe HMAC signature with Web Crypto + a replay window (accepts any of multiple v1 sigs for key rotation) and maps subscription state to `plan_tier` via the service-role client (gated on `STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET`; a 200 no-op until configured). A Settings -> Plan tab (`BillingTab`) shows the current plan, the three tiers, and an owner-only Upgrade CTA that degrades to an honest "billing not connected yet" until keys exist (nothing is charged). **Deferred on purpose:** the memory-expiry enforcement (free memory expiring) is kept out of this lane to stay file-disjoint from the parallel M-A Slice 2 (Today) work; it lands as a clean additive follow-up (an `expires_at` + a recall-path filter) after Slice 2. **Verification:** `bun test` 117 green (+9), `bun run build` green, client bundle grep-clean of `STRIPE_SECRET_KEY` / service-role; a focused adversarial security review verdict was clean on the criticals (INSERT + UPDATE self-grant both closed) with one LOW folded in (the webhook now accepts any of multiple v1 signatures for key rotation). **Gate:** migration `20260616200000` applies on the next Lovable sync; live charging waits on the founder provisioning the Stripe secrets (`STRIPE_SECRET_KEY`, `STRIPE_PRICE_PRO`, `STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET`). Built file-disjoint from M-A Slice 2. **Files:** `supabase/migrations/20260616200000_mc_plan_tier.sql`, `src/lib/entitlements.ts` (+`.test.ts`), `src/lib/billing.functions.ts`, `src/routes/api/stripe/webhook.ts` new; `src/routes/_authenticated.settings.tsx` (Plan tab + `BillingTab`) edited; `docs/features/pricing.md` (new) + features index, `active-task.md`, this log.

**M-C memory expiry: the "charge for memory persistence" gate is now enforced (BUILT, working tree).** The plan-tier foundation defined the entitlement (`memoryPersists`); this wires the mechanic. Free workspaces keep distilled `agent_memory` for 14 days then it expires; pro and team keep it forever. Implemented entirely additively so it never touched the parallel M-A Slice 2 files (which only added `ExecutedCard.tsx` + `today.functions.ts` + the Today route): a `BEFORE INSERT` trigger (`set_agent_memory_expiry`) stamps `agent_memory.expires_at` from the owner's plan (free = `created_at` + 14 days mirroring `FREE_MEMORY_RETENTION_DAYS`, pro/team = NULL), so the TS write path (`rememberOutcome`) is unchanged and pre-migration tolerant; the `match_agent_memory` recall RPC gains `AND (expires_at IS NULL OR expires_at > now())` so the loop never recalls expired memory (body copied verbatim from the P1 rescope with the one predicate added, security boundary `user_id = COALESCE(auth.uid(), for_user)` preserved); and the daily `memory-tick` cron hard-deletes expired rows (pre-migration tolerant: a missing-column error is ignored, the existing decay passes still run). Existing rows are grandfathered (`expires_at` NULL = never expires) so nothing is retroactively wiped, including the demo seed. **Adversarial review (NEEDS-FIXES, both folded before commit):** (A) a free user could self-grant permanent memory by inserting an explicit far-future `expires_at` (the trigger now only honors a client-supplied value for the service-role; every other caller has it recomputed from the plan, so the value is uncheatable); (B) non-owner team members got FREE expiry (the paid check now keys on `workspace_members` membership, not just `owner_id`, so owners and invited members of any pro/team workspace keep memory). Recall-boundary, trigger-cannot-break-inserts, paid-never-swept, and grandfathering all reviewed clean. **Verification:** `bun test` 117 green, `bun run build` green. **Gate:** migration `20260616210000` applies on the next Lovable sync, after `20260616200000` (plan_tier), in filename order. Built file-disjoint from M-A Slice 2 (which had already landed). **Files:** `supabase/migrations/20260616210000_mc_memory_expiry.sql` new; `src/routes/api/public/hooks/memory-tick.ts` (expiry sweep) edited; `docs/features/pricing.md` (How it works + deferred flipped), `active-task.md`, this log.

**M-C scope ruling: pricing ENGINE only, gates DORMANT at the prototype stage (founder, 2026-06-16).** The founder clarified that at this working-prototype stage we build the pricing engine (plan tiers, entitlements as data, billing surface, Stripe plumbing) but do NOT wire active paywall gates yet, since the product itself is not fully built. So the memory-expiry enforcement shipped just above (the only active gate) is made dormant rather than reverted: a `memory_expiry_enabled()` SQL flag (returns false) gates the stamp trigger, so while off every memory row stays `expires_at = NULL` (never expires) and the recall filter + the `memory-tick` sweep are automatic no-ops. The code is built and reviewed; flip the flag (`CREATE OR REPLACE ... SELECT true`) when ready to enforce. Critic-everywhere and other entitlement gates are explicitly NOT wired now. The entitlements map still documents the intended per-tier policy as pure data (nothing reads it to block). **Files:** `supabase/migrations/20260616210000_mc_memory_expiry.sql` (flag + trigger guard), `docs/features/pricing.md`, `active-task.md`, this log.

**H3 · Scheduling — calendar-aware deep-work blocks — SHIPPED to `main` (Feature Dashboard pick, claimed before building, adversarially reviewed).** The Calendar surface gains a **"Plan deep work"** action: a new read-only `proposeWorkBlocks` server fn fits the operator's open deep-work tasks (`is_deep_work`, not done) into free time within their working hours, reusing the proven `proposeSlots` conflict logic — one block per task, back to back across the next working days, skipping weekends, hours outside the profile's working window, and existing calendar events. It is a pure proposal (never writes); each proposed block has an "Add to calendar" affordance that creates the event via `createCalendarEvent`. **Honest by construction:** it only schedules what genuinely fits, so a packed calendar yields fewer (or zero) blocks with an honest empty state, never a forced plan. **Verification:** `bun run build` green, `bunx eslint` clean; Playwright-verified live both ways — the empty state ("Nothing to schedule…") on the demo (no open deep-work tasks), and the populated path (temporarily relaxing the deep-work filter, then reverting) produced 6 correct back-to-back hourly blocks (Wed 9am–2pm) all inside working hours, correctly starting the NEXT working day because it was already past 6pm. **Adversarial review (2-lens workflow, ultracode):** surfaced one real HIGH bug — the working-hours boundary used the truncated `getHours()`, so a block from a :30 cursor could overrun `whEnd` by up to the block length (e.g. 17:30→18:30 past a 6pm end); fixed by comparing the block END in minutes in **both** `proposeWorkBlocks` and the pre-existing `proposeSlots` (same one-line bug, same file). Also fixed a MEDIUM: a user-facing em-dash in the empty-state copy (humanized hard gate). A LOW timezone limitation (server-UTC hour checks, shared with `proposeSlots`) was already disclosed in the doc comment and left as a separate platform fix. All-new fn + the Calendar panel; **collision-free** with the parallel lanes (Today/Govern/studio). Dashboard row flipped to ✅, G2 at-a-glance updated (Done 5→6, Pending 3→2). Live on the next Lovable Publish. **Files:** `src/lib/calendar.functions.ts` (`proposeWorkBlocks` new + the boundary fix in `proposeSlots`), `src/components/knowledge/CalendarPanel.tsx` ("Plan deep work" + the blocks panel), `docs/planning/feature-dashboard.md`, this log.

- **2026-06-15 · `brand · split build-in-public into its own private repo`.** The brand system moved out of this product repo into a new PRIVATE repo, `RohitGajaraj/build-in-public` (commit `8af548a`), so the founder's personal brand, voice, drafts, and (soon) social tokens never live in a codebase that may be shared with a team, investors, or open-sourced. Removed `docs/brand/` here and re-pointed the references in `CLAUDE.md`/`GEMINI.md` §1.65, `AGENTS.md`, and `docs/README.md` to the new repo (no dangling links; do not recreate `docs/brand/`). The build-to-content coupling is preserved one-way: build sessions append real insights to the brand repo's `content-well.md` (mechanism in that repo's `insight-feed.md`), and a weekly Claude Code cloud routine (Friday 19:00 IST) reads it, researches, drafts per the voice rules, pushes to Buffer via the Buffer API token (no MCP connector needed), commits, and notifies the founder (prompt in the brand repo's `routine.md`). **Pending founder setup for the routine:** `/web-setup` to connect GitHub for the cloud agent, and a Buffer API token (publish.buffer.com/settings/api) as the routine secret; this week's posts are already staged/scheduled, so no gap. **Engine rationale (founder asked where the intelligence lives):** the scheduled cloud agent IS the intelligence (web research + drafting + repo read/write), reaching Buffer over HTTPS with the token; the fully-owned zero-Claude alternative (a Worker cron calling a model API + a search API + the Buffer API) is documented as the later option. **Files (this repo):** removed `docs/brand/`; edited `CLAUDE.md`, `GEMINI.md`, `AGENTS.md`, `docs/README.md`, `active-task.md`, this log.

- **2026-06-15 · M-0 · the orchestrated agent loop is VERIFIED LIVE end to end (KI-22 + KI-23 both resolved).** After the KI-23 fix was Published, the previously-stuck mission `973800a8` unstuck itself and hopped its full 6-step DAG unattended: Strategist completed → Sprint Planner completed (~1m) → Critic running, dependencies respected (`after 1`, `after 2`), each specialist resumed and executed by the per-minute `resume-runs` cron with no operator intervention. This closes the M-0 core loop: plan → dispatch → execute → hop on live data. The whole multi-week "hollow mission" saga reduced to one bug — a `model` reference to a column that does not exist on `agent_runs` — across three sites (two inserts fixed by Lovable as KI-22, one select fixed here as KI-23, plus a Build-surface sibling). Remaining M-0 exit items are now just a real signup (KI-13) and one live ingest source. **No code change** (verification + doc-loop only); records in `docs/planning/{known-issues.md,v7-build-status.md}`, this log.
- **2026-06-15 · M-0 · KI-23 fixed: dispatched specialist runs now resume (the same `model`-column bug, in a SELECT Lovable's insert-only fix missed).** With the hollow-completion fixed, the loop planned and dispatched but the first specialist sat `queued` forever and never executed. Root cause: `resumeAgentLoop` (`loop.server.ts`) selected a `model` column from `agent_runs` that does not exist, so the PostgREST select errored, the run read back null, and the function threw `run not found` on every per-minute `resume-runs` tick — so no queued specialist run was ever resumed. Lovable's KI-22 fix removed `model` from the two INSERT sites but missed this SELECT (and a sibling `studio.functions.ts:432` on the Build surface). Fixed by dropping `model` from both selects; the model now falls back to the checkpoint state then the `google/gemini-2.5-flash` default, exactly as `runAgentLoop` already does. `bun run build` green (3.16s), `bun test` 88 green. **Deploys on the next Lovable Publish, then re-verify a mission hops discovery-scout to strategist to completion end to end.** **Files:** `src/lib/ai/loop.server.ts`, `src/lib/studio.functions.ts`; doc-loop in `docs/planning/{known-issues.md,v7-build-status.md}`, this log.
- **2026-06-15 · M-0 hollow orchestrated missions RESOLVED and verified live; the true cause was a schema-mismatched `agent_runs` insert.** A long multi-layer hunt (approval gating, governance halt, slug drift, deploy divergence) bottomed out on the real blocker: `src/lib/ai/loop.server.ts` inserted a `model:` field into `agent_runs`, a column the table does not have, so the orchestrator's launch INSERT was silently rejected by Postgres (no run row, no trace, no error surfaced) and every orchestrated mission completed hollow or failed at launch. - **2026-06-15 · `M-0 · orchestrated missions were completing HOLLOW; root-caused live and fixed (the real mission-run blocker)`.** Live re-verification of the prior gating fix on the hosted app (Project GlassWing, demo account) confirmed that fix works (no new control-flow approvals queued) but surfaced a deeper, separate defect: every orchestrated mission finished with 0 steps and 0 hops yet was labeled "completed". A full live trace (`6471cbaa`, 10 hops, 21,183 tokens) proved the cause and ruled out the governance-halt theory (kill-switch off, real tokens spent): the orchestrator's `mission.plan` planner emits a colloquial agent slug (`discovery`), but the seeded roster slug is `discovery-scout` (the same slug drift the 2026-06-14 migration standardized on the event-reactor path), and `mission.plan`'s strict exact-match validator threw on the miss, dropping the WHOLE plan; the orchestrator then observed 0 steps, retried, and finalized "unresolvable internal planning", after which the cron completed the 0-step mission. That is why missions never "hopped". **Fix, two layers:** (1) `mission.plan` (`orchestrator.server.ts`) now resolves each planned slug against the live roster (exact, then a single unambiguous prefix or substring match) so `discovery` maps to `discovery-scout` instead of dropping the plan, throwing clearly only when a slug is genuinely unresolvable; (2) `maybeCompleteMission` (`handoff.server.ts`) now marks a never-planned (0-step) terminal mission `failed` (retryable) instead of hollow-`completed`, and skips decision-capture for it, so any future zero-plan cause surfaces loudly rather than as a fake "done". **Verification:** `bun run build` green, `bun test` 88 green. **Live re-verification pending the next Lovable deploy** (the fix cannot be observed on the hosted app until it deploys). **Infra note:** confirmed with the founder we keep ONE Lovable-managed Supabase (no new account, no DB fork); schema continues to flow through `supabase/migrations/*` applied by Lovable. **Files:** `src/lib/ai/tools/orchestrator.server.ts`, `src/lib/ai/handoff.server.ts`; `docs/planning/{known-issues.md,v7-build-status.md}`, `active-task.md`, this log.

- **2026-06-14 · `M-0 · orchestrator control-flow tools no longer approval-gated (the live mission-stall fix)`.** Live end-to-end verification on the hosted app (the M-0 exit gate) surfaced the real blocker, which neither the migration sync nor code review had: a freshly launched orchestrated mission stalled. Root-caused via a recon workflow plus a live server-fn response-trace capture (Playwright): the orchestrator's OWN control-flow tools (`mission.plan`, `mission.dispatch`) were being sent to the approval queue at the `observing` arc (`resolveApprovalMode` forces auto to review there), so the plan never persisted; the orchestrator then observed zero steps and finalized with "mission steps are not being registered". The 7 stuck Today approvals were exactly these expired queued plan/dispatch calls. Founder ruling: orchestration control-flow tools always run inline. **Fix:** a new `ORCHESTRATION_CONTROL_FLOW_TOOLS` allowlist (`mission.plan/dispatch/observe/finalize`) at the single loop gate (`loop.server.ts:647-665`) bypasses approval creation for those four (no external side effect; `mission.dispatch` only enqueues child runs; the specialists' real-world tools stay gated per arc on the child runs; kill-switch/budget/guardrails still apply because they live in `callModel` upstream of the gate). **Plus three defense-in-depth guards** (the RCA + its adversarial verifier showed a completion-guard alone was insufficient and could strand a mission): the `agent_runs` insert now throws on error (no silent 0-run loop); `startOrchestratedMission` marks the mission `halted` on a thrown launch before re-throwing (so the UI retry, gated on failed/halted, fires instead of leaving it `running`); and `maybeCompleteMission` no longer silently completes a zero-step mission unless a terminal orchestrator run exists (closing the hollow-completion the RCA found, without stranding, since a failed launch now goes to `halted`). **Verification:** `bun run build` green, `bun test` 88 green, adversarial review safe-to-land (allowlist exact, governance not bypassed, no mission stranding); diff scrutinized at the gate. **Live re-verification pending the Lovable deploy of this commit** (the fix cannot be observed on the hosted app until it deploys). **Files:** `src/lib/ai/{loop.server,trust.server,handoff.server}.ts`, `src/lib/orchestrator.functions.ts`; this log + `active-task.md`.

- **2026-06-14 · `M-0 #4 · humanizeText() runtime sanitizer`.** The hard gate from the humanized-output convention (Level 2) is now wired at the AI chokepoint, so the platform's generated prose carries no machine fingerprints. New pure `src/lib/ai/humanize.ts` (`humanizeText`) segments prose from fenced and inline code, normalizes em/en dashes to honest ASCII by context (a numeric range like 1-6 becomes "1 to 6"; a separator dash becomes a comma), strips the convention's invisible and exotic-space set, collapses double spaces, trims trailing whitespace; its own source spells the code points as escapes so it stays fingerprint-free and lint-clean. Wired into `runtime.server.ts`: `callModel` humanizes prose output, `callModelStream` humanizes on a line-buffered, fence-aware boundary (`createStreamHumanizer` holds an open fenced block until it closes, so streamed concatenation equals `humanizeText(whole)`), plus a soft `HUMANIZE_DIRECTIVE` on prose system prompts (`prompts.server.ts`). JSON is never touched: every gate keys on `responseFormat !== 'json_object'` and `callModel` parses JSON off the raw text, so the agent loop and all tool JSON stay byte-exact. The per-lane adversarial reviewer ran 164 probe assertions (streaming-equals-whole-text, prefix stability, purity, idempotence, JSON parse-safety) and caught one real gap: `lineage.functions.ts` (PRD to task-graph) returned `{"tasks":[...]}` without declaring json-mode, so the sanitizer would have rewritten task-title strings; fixed by adding `responseFormat: 'json_object'`. The eval-runner subject call is intentionally left humanized (its output is scored as a string, never parsed, so evaluating the shipped form is correct). **Verification:** `bun run build` green, `bun test` 88 green (+27 humanize cases), eslint clean on all touched files. Takes effect on deploy (no migration). **Files:** `src/lib/ai/humanize.ts` (+`.test.ts`) new; `src/lib/ai/{runtime.server,prompts.server}.ts`, `src/lib/lineage.functions.ts` edited; `docs/conventions/humanized-output.md`, `docs/planning/v7-build-status.md`, `active-task.md`, this log.
- **2026-06-14 · `M-0 · KI-19 enabled-agent dispatch hole closed`.** A latent gap the slug-drift RCA surfaced: `resolveAgent` (`handoff.server.ts`) resolved a target agent by slug with no `enabled` filter, so a disabled or off-roster agent could still be dispatched a child run (via the `agent.handoff` tool or the mission dispatcher, which both route through that one chokepoint). Fixed at the chokepoint: `resolveAgent` now filters `enabled = true` and throws a clear, slug-named error (`Target agent 'X' is disabled or not in the roster`) when nothing enabled matches. The throw is caught per step, by `failOrRequeueStep` on the dispatcher path and by the agent loop on the tool path, so a bad target terminalizes one step instead of crashing a run; the orchestrator sender lookup keeps its null-sender fallback, so enabled specialists are unaffected. `agents.enabled` is `BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT true`, so the filter has no null footgun. Adversarial review verdict safe-to-land, no code edits needed. **Residual (logged as KI-20):** two adjacent surfaces still resolve agents without an enabled filter, the run-start path in `loop.server.ts` (an already-queued run whose target was disabled in the gap) and the operator-initiated `runAgent` direct invocation. **Verification:** `bun run build` green, `bun test` 88 green, eslint clean. - **2026-06-14 · `M-0 · unseeded-slug drift sealed (doc-loop + RCA correction)`.** The migration shipped in `5b0b0b93ea`; this entry completes its doc loop and corrects the record. The tracker had claimed the orchestrator prompt's stale slugs made `mission.plan` throw and kill any sensing-step mission. A 10-agent adversarial root-cause (workflow `wf_71a7dc78`: 6 readers, a synthesizer, 3 refuters) disproved it: `mission.plan` plans against the live enabled roster and re-validates (`orchestrator.server.ts:125,173-179`), so it never deterministically throws.
