- **2026-06-14 — `M-B · memory-compounds metric` — the moat is now measured, not just visible: a "Memory compounds" card on the Gauntlet (`/govern?tab=gauntlet`).** The `/memory` view made the recall store visible; this instruments the honest, scale-independent proof that it COMPOUNDS (defensible even at one user, per the v7 canon): of what the loop stored, the share it has recalled back at least once (`reuseRate = recalled/stored`), plus weekly growth (`+N this week`) and `prioritiesMoved` (recorded outcomes that moved an opportunity's ICE, via the same rounded-compare honesty guard the loop uses, so a sub-0.1 drift never reads as a move). - **2026-06-14 — `M-B · compounding-memory view` — the memory moat is now visible: a read-only `/memory` surface renders the `agent_memory` store the loop writes to and recalls from.** Phase 2's W1 already distilled every outcome into a global-scope `agent_memory` row and threaded recalled memories across hops, but the data had no surface, so the Decision-System moat was real yet invisible. - **2026-06-14 — `convention · humanized output (zero AI fingerprints)` — a standing, cross-tool rule that no shipped or generated text carries a machine fingerprint, at two levels.** Founder ruling: (1) everything we author (code, docs, UI copy, comments, commits, seed data) and (2) everything the platform generates for a user (PRDs, drafts, chat, research) must read as a sharp human wrote it. Banned: em/en dashes, invisible Unicode (zero-width, NBSP, BOM, soft hyphen, directional marks), AI-cliche phrasing, and over-uniform rhythm; positive bar is a distinct, "looks like Cadence not one-in-a-thousand" voice. Authored the master convention `docs/conventions/humanized-output.md` (the existing `ui-voice.md` becomes its UI-string application; added an invisible-Unicode ban there too). **Level 2 (runtime) is specced, not yet wired:** a soft prompt directive in `src/lib/ai/prompts.server.ts` + a hard `humanizeText()` sanitizer at the AI chokepoint `src/lib/ai/runtime.server.ts` (both `callModel` + `callModelStream`, skipping code fences, buffering the stream) so generated output is sanitized before it reaches the user. **Wired into every entry point:** `AGENTS.md` §3 (rule 9a), `CLAUDE.md`/`GEMINI.md` §1.6, `README.md` (standing rule), `.lovable-config.txt`, the conventions index, and `v7` §13 ruling 8. **Deferred (tracked):** a build-time pre-commit hook (em-dash + invisible-char detector on staged text) and a one-time codebase-wide sweep of pre-rule work (a good Workflow: detect then fix per file). All new text this session written to the rule. **Files:** `docs/conventions/humanized-output.md` new; `docs/conventions/{README,ui-voice}.md`, `AGENTS.md`, `CLAUDE.md`, `GEMINI.md`, `README.md`, `.lovable-config.txt`, `docs/strategy/v7-agentic-product-os.md`, `session-decisions.md`, this log edited. **Next (implementation):** the `humanizeText()` sanitizer + tests, the prompt directive, the hook, then the sweep.

- **2026-06-14 — `v6 Phase 3 · KI-14` — the suite-eval score scale is now honest: standardized on 0–100, killing a silent column overflow + a false "below gate" read.** `eval_runs.avg_score` / `eval_case_results.score` were `numeric(4,3)` (max 9.999 — a 0–1 design), but the live judge (`eval-runner.server.ts`) writes 0–100 and `eval_suites.pass_threshold` is INTEGER 0–100: a real run ≥ 10 OVERFLOWED the column, and the 0–1 demo seeds rendered "score 1 · below gate 80" (a false failure on the screen-7 eval drill). Fix (migration `20260614160000`, no app-logic change): widen both columns → `numeric(6,3)` (holds 0–100, keeps the 3-decimal scale so the widen is precision-lossless) + rescale existing 0–1 rows ×100 across **three** persisted copies — `eval_runs`, `eval_case_results`, and the derived `drift_snapshots.avg_eval_score` (drift materializes the same metric at rollup). **Why no app code:** verified against source that `trust.server.ts` reads a DIFFERENT table (`ai_evals.score`, the per-message chat-judge system, still 0–1) and `drift.server.ts` feeds the score only through a scale-invariant pct-delta — so the recon agents' "trust wraps / drift breaks" alarms were both false (lesson: verify recon against source before editing). Only the drift UI formatter changed (`DriftPanel`/`DriftSurfaceDetail`: render the 0–100 integer, not `0.84`→`84.00`). **Adversarial review (3-lens workflow `wf_8850182b`, 12 confirmed findings, none blocking)** sharpened the fix: added the `drift_snapshots` rescale (same metric, missed in the first cut); switched `numeric(5,2)`→`numeric(6,3)` to avoid a 3→2 dp precision loss; documented the `<= 1` guard's {0,1} edge + that the migration is forward-only; and caught that `seed_demo_workspace` is not merely "dormant" but the **documented operator re-seed** (`demo-credentials.md`) for the investor-demo accounts — so rather than reproduce the untestable 354-line function, the re-seed doc now warns + ships the corrected procedure (seed, then the same three ×100 normalizations). Doc-consistency: the unbuilt "≥0.1 eval regression" deploy-gate restated as "≥10-point (0–100)" across AGENTS.md / architecture/runtime.md / plan.md / feature-backlog.md. **Verification:** `bun run build` green, `bun test` 32/32. **Gate:** the migration applies on the next Lovable sync (until then a live eval run still overflows; existing demo data still reads 0–1). **Files:** `supabase/migrations/20260614160000_p3_ki14_eval_score_0to100.sql` new; `src/components/observe/{DriftPanel,DriftSurfaceDetail}.tsx`, `docs/operations/demo-credentials.md`, `docs/planning/known-issues.md` (KI-14 ✅ + KI-13 row corrected), `AGENTS.md`, `architecture/runtime.md`, `docs/planning/feature-backlog.md`, `docs/strategy/session-decisions.md`, `active-task.md`, this log.

- **2026-06-14 — `v6 Phase 3 · slice 1 / Track 1 (KI-13)` — live signup made resilient so a real account can finally be created (the whole Phase-3 gauntlet was blocked at the door).** KI-13 — signup 500s ("Database error saving new user") — root-caused (static migration read; the live Supabase MCP was unauthenticated) to migration drift: `on_auth_user_created` runs `handle_new_user()` AFTER INSERT on `auth.users`, so any seed step that throws (a helper/table absent on the live DB) aborts the whole INSERT → 500 → no real account. Fix is defensive-by-construction (correct regardless of which object is missing): each seed step (profile · `ensure_default_workspace` · the three `seed_*`) now runs in its own PL/pgSQL `BEGIN..EXCEPTION` subtransaction — a failure logs a WARNING and signup STILL completes. Body otherwise an exact replica of the latest trigger (`20260612100000`): same seed set, SECURITY DEFINER, `search_path` pin, REVOKE. - **2026-06-14 — `v6 Phase 3 · slice 1 / Track 2` — the Gauntlet: the three north-star proof metrics, instrumented on a real surface (honest empty states), built in a parallel worktree then hardened by a 12-finding adversarial review before landing.** New `/govern?tab=gauntlet` tab (inserted after Analytics) with three cards, each a real computation over owner-scoped tables — no fabricated numbers; sparse windows read "not enough data yet." **A · Acceptance rate** (`getAcceptanceRate`): `accepted/(accepted+rejected)` over DECIDED rows (`decided_at` set) where accepted = status ∈ {approved, executed, failed} — an approved call that then ran (resolveApproval→executeApproval flips approved→executed/failed) is still an acceptance, so the worktree agent's first cut (count only `status='approved'`) read artificially low; review caught it, fixed at the DB layer + in the 7d-vs-prior-7d trend. The user rollup of the per-agent acceptance already in `ai/trust.server.ts`. **C · Autonomy ratio** (`getAutonomyRatio`): `unattended/(unattended+gated)` where unattended = SUCCESSFUL (`ok=true`) side-effecting `tool_calls` rows (a failed inline attempt isn't carried work — review fix) and gated = side-effecting `agent_approvals` rows, side-effecting decided by `isSideEffectingTool()` (`tool-consequences.ts`); copy is explicit that rising ≠ no-human (the gated count is exactly the work that still comes to you). **B · Ritual retention** (`getRitualRetention`): distinct days-active 7/14/30 + current streak from the new `ritual_sessions` table, plus an on-the-fly, user-wide real-vs-demo signal (≥1 connected `connections` row OR ≥1 `signals` row) that returns null (the tag is omitted) if its probe errors, rather than mislabeling a real account "demo" (review fix). **Pre-migration-tolerant:** the `ritual_sessions` read catches a missing-relation error (`42P01`/`42703`/`PGRST205`/"relation does not exist") and returns `tableReady:false` → card reads "not enough data yet" rather than throwing (same probe idiom as `mission-advance.server.ts:hasRetryColumns`). Today (`_authenticated.index.tsx`) fires `recordRitualSession` once on mount (ref-guarded) — never blocks render, swallows table-missing/any failure; the write is an idempotent per-UTC-day upsert (unique `(user_id, opened_on)`) so repeated opens never accumulate, and `workspace_id` is left null (a client id isn't trusted — cross-tenant; all three review fixes). Pure helpers (`trendOf`, `isMissingRelation`) split into client-safe `src/lib/gauntlet-metrics.ts` with 9 unit tests. **Gate:** migration `20260614150000_p3_ritual_sessions.sql` (owner-scoped RLS mirroring `agent_approvals`, unique index on `(user_id, opened_on)` for per-day idempotence) applies on the next Lovable sync; until then Metric B reads "not enough data yet" by design. **Verification:** `bun run build` green, `bun test src/lib/gauntlet-metrics.test.ts` 9/9 green, eslint/prettier clean on all touched files. **Files:** `src/lib/gauntlet.functions.ts`, `src/lib/gauntlet-metrics.ts` (+`.test.ts`), `src/components/observe/GauntletMetricsPanel.tsx`, `supabase/migrations/20260614150000_p3_ritual_sessions.sql` new; `src/routes/_authenticated.govern.tsx`, `src/routes/_authenticated.index.tsx` edited; `docs/features/gauntlet-metrics.md` (+ index row in `docs/features/README.md`), this log.

- **2026-06-14 — `v6 Phase 2 · W2 + W3` — autonomy made legible: the loop's unattended work is audited, the A2A contract is hardened, and the moat is on the cockpit.** Grounded by two parallel Explore sweeps (which caught that the `/swarm` Swarm HUD already IS the "agents at work" OS view — so we enriched it instead of building a redundant `/system` route). **W2 — "Executed unattended" audit:** the trust arc already executes write tools inline at trusted/ambient; this surfaces it honestly. `getMission` now flags each `HopToolCall.is_unattended` via the new client-safe `isSideEffectingTool()` (`src/lib/tool-consequences.ts`), and `/missions/$id` renders an "Executed unattended" card (between the gate — _what needs you_ — and the trace — _what already ran_), each row showing the tool's catalogued effect + reversibility + ok/latency. **Correctness crux (verified by review):** every `tool_calls` row is an inline auto-execution — gated tools queue an `agent_approvals` row and `executeApproval` updates the approval, never writing `tool_calls` — so a side-effecting `tool_calls` row is _provably_ unattended (claim-never-outruns-wiring holds). **W3 — A2A hardening + moat visibility:** (a) `enqueueHandoff` (`handoff.server.ts`) now validates `payload.memory_refs[]` against real `agent_memory` ids the user owns, dropping phantom refs before they reach a receiver's prompt (best-effort: a transient query error keeps refs as-is, never strips valid ones; works under both the user client and the admin sweeper). (b) `getSwarmHud` gains `outcomes_remembered` (count of `agent_memory` kind='outcome' — the W1 moat output) surfaced as "N outcomes in memory" in the Agents-tab HUD header (cumulative, placed apart from the "last hour" throughput strip so it never reads as a rate). Artifacts left free-form by design (validated on use by the receiver's tools). **Adversarial review (1 agent) confirmed the core correctness + found 2 honesty issues, both fixed:** added the two genuinely-missing side-effecting tools to the consequence catalogue (`tasks.update_status`, `research.synthesize` — so the audit doesn't under-report), and replaced a blanket "each is undoable" subtitle with per-row reversibility (some auto tools are only partly reversible). **Verification:** `bun test` 23 green, `bun run build` green, lint clean; no blast radius (`is_unattended`/`outcomes_remembered` each have exactly one constructor). **Files:** `src/lib/tool-consequences.ts`, `src/lib/missions.functions.ts`, `src/routes/_authenticated.missions.$missionId.tsx`, `src/lib/ai/handoff.server.ts`, `src/lib/swarm.functions.ts`, `src/components/cockpit/AgentsPanel.tsx`; docs: `architecture/orchestration.md`, `docs/strategy/session-decisions.md`, `active-task.md`, this log.

- **2026-06-14 — `v6 Phase 2 · W1` — the memory moat is real: recorded outcomes now become memory the agents recall.** Phase 2's first demoable unit (the Decision-System moat, v6 §3 Pillar 2), grounded by an Explore sweep that found the loop was only _half_-wired: `recordOutcome` re-scored the opportunity ICE and wrote a `learnings` audit row, but that row lived in a table **no agent ever reads** — `match_agent_memory` (the loop's recall) only reads `agent_memory`. So the product _showed_ "we learned this" while every agent stayed amnesiac (claim-outruns-wiring). Fix: on `recordOutcome`, after the learning insert, distil the outcome into a **global-scope, embedded `agent_memory` row** (`src/lib/ai/outcome-memory.ts` pure `buildOutcomeMemory`/`outcomeImportance` + `src/lib/ai/memory.server.ts` `rememberOutcome`), entity-linked in `metadata` to the prd/opportunity/learning. Because the row is `scope='global'`, `match_agent_memory`'s `m.scope='global'` clause returns it to a future run of **any** agent (when semantically relevant), and Phase 1's `memory_refs[]` threading carries it across hops — so a Strategist re-encountering the opportunity now recalls "we shipped this; it was {verdict} (ICE {prior}→{new})." Importance 4 (decisive) / 3 (mixed) keeps it above the memory-tick decay floor. **Adversarial review (1 agent) found 4 real issues, all fixed:** (1) a null-embedding row is silently _unrecallable_ (the RPC hard-filters `embedding IS NOT NULL`) and there's no re-embed sweep → now we **skip the write entirely** rather than insert a ghost (also closes an `embedOne` sparse-return path); (2) the idempotency delete used `.eq("metadata->>source",…)` — the repo's proven jsonb idiom is `.filter("col->>key","eq",…)` (per `today.functions.ts`/`traces.functions.ts`) → switched, so re-records replace not duplicate; (3) a clamped-confidence outcome could render a misleading "8.3→8.3" ICE move → the move line now guards on the _rounded_ values; (4) RLS/blast-radius confirmed safe (`recordOutcome`'s extra `memory_id` return field is ignored by `OutcomeCard`). **Verification:** `bun test` 23 green (9 new pure-policy tests incl. the rounding-honesty case), `bun run build` green, touched files prettier/eslint-clean. No new UI: the recall surfaces in any run's "Relevant memories from past sessions" prompt block + trace (and the existing Memory panel still shows the `learnings` audit). **Files:** `src/lib/ai/outcome-memory.ts` (+`.test.ts`) new; `src/lib/ai/memory.server.ts` (+`rememberOutcome`), `src/lib/outcome.functions.ts` (distil hook + title selects) edited; `architecture/orchestration.md`, `docs/strategy/session-decisions.md`, `active-task.md`, this log.

- **2026-06-14 — `v6 Phase 1 (The Loop Runs Itself)` COMPLETE: autonomy, wired — a multi-hop mission now runs unattended, retries transient hop failures, sizes its own step budget, and threads compounding memory across hops.** Closes the four gaps the runtime audit named (v6 Appendix B) — _not_ with messaging, with code. Founder design rulings this session (AskUserQuestion, logged in session-decisions): auto-advance folds into the existing `resume-runs` sweeper (no new pg*cron → no migration-apply gate); hop retry is bounded (2 attempts + exponential backoff); the step budget is arc + mission-size aware. **(1) Deterministic auto-advance** — new `src/lib/ai/mission-advance.server.ts` (`advanceMissionCore`): reflect child-run outcomes onto `mission_steps` → dispatch every newly-ready step → finalize a terminal DAG, all **model-free**. Key insight: the old `advanceMission` re-invoked the orchestrator \_LLM* each wave, but `mission.plan` already rejects re-planning, so that call only ever did mechanical observe→dispatch→finalize — replacing it with deterministic DB ops is cheaper, faster, and concurrency-safe while preserving behavior (the LLM now runs only for the initial plan). The per-minute `resume-runs` cron calls it for every running mission; the manual `advanceMission` server fn calls the same core; `mission.dispatch` (the orchestrator tool) routes through the shared `dispatchReadySteps`. **Claim-first CAS** (`planned→dispatched` before enqueue) makes overlapping ticks safe from double-dispatch; a step stranded `dispatched` with null `run_id` (worker eviction mid-enqueue) is recovered after a 3-min window. **(2) Bounded hop retry** — migration `20260614090000` adds `mission_steps.{attempts,max_attempts,next_retry_at}` and teaches `next_ready_mission_steps` the backoff window (identical signature, backward-compatible: NULL backoff = eligible now); pure policy in `src/lib/ai/retry.ts`. Pre-migration-tolerant via a per-isolate `hasRetryColumns` probe that only caches a genuine missing-column error (a transient blip re-probes), degrading to no-retry without ever throwing. **(3) Adaptive step budget** — new `src/lib/ai/budget.ts` (`adaptiveStepBudget`) replaces the static `maxStepsFor`: role base + earned-trust headroom (`arc`) + orchestrator-scales-with-DAG-size, under a hard ceiling; orchestrator base kept at the proven 14 so the initial run never regresses (review catch). Threaded through `executeLoop` (both `runAgentLoop` + `resumeAgentLoop`) with a live `mission_steps` count. **(4) `memory_refs[]` populated** (the W5 contract field) — new `src/lib/ai/memory.server.ts` (`recallMemoryRefs`) returns the `id`s the RPC already exposed; the loop's recall now writes `agent_memory.last_used_at` on every recall (decay input), and each dispatched hop threads relevant memory into the handoff payload. Migration `20260614091000` rescopes `match_agent_memory` to `COALESCE(auth.uid(), for_user)` so the **service-role sweeper path** actually matches semantic memory (was `auth.uid()`-only → null on the autonomous path — the exact claim-outruns-wiring gap Phase 1 exists to close) while keeping the per-user security boundary (auth.uid() always wins). **Verification:** new `bun test` path (bun's built-in runner — zero new deps, dodges the supply-chain guard) covers the pure budget/retry policy (14 tests green); `bun run build` green; touched files prettier/eslint-clean; a 2-agent adversarial review over the diff surfaced 10 findings — 4 real (orchestrator budget regression, transient-error caching, stranded-dispatch recovery, the `match_agent_memory` `auth.uid()` gap), all fixed; 3 confidently wrong (verified against source — one proposed "fix" would have introduced an infinite retry loop), rejected. **Gate (unchanged pattern):** the two P1 migrations apply on the next Lovable sync; until then retry is off and autonomous-path `memory_refs` carries reflections only — both degrade gracefully. **Files:** `src/lib/ai/{mission-advance.server,memory.server,budget,retry}.ts` (+ `budget.test.ts`/`retry.test.ts`) new; `src/lib/ai/{loop.server,handoff.server}.ts`, `src/lib/ai/tools/orchestrator.server.ts`, `src/lib/orchestrator.functions.ts`, `src/routes/api/public/hooks/resume-runs.ts` edited; `supabase/migrations/{20260614090000_p1_mission_step_retry,20260614091000_p1_memory_recall_for_user}.sql` new; `package.json`/`tsconfig.json` (test path); `architecture/orchestration.md`, `docs/features/{loop-runs-itself.md(new),README.md}`, `docs/planning/known-issues.md`, `docs/strategy/session-decisions.md`, `active-task.md`, this log.

mid-session steer injection (`agent_messages kind='steer'`, consumed per step; `consumeInboundHandoff` now filters `kind='handoff'` so steers are never eaten); safety floors (commit/PR ≥ `confirm`, merge always `review`); **shipping gates pause the run** — checkpoint at i+1, `status='waiting_approval'`, sweeper re-enters once the gate is decided AND executed, injecting the approval outcome (tracked by id in checkpoint state, no double-inject); `executeApproval` carries mission ctx. **KI-02 tick hardening:** resume-runs now also picks `running` runs with NULL `last_checkpoint_at` + stale `created_at` (SQL `lt` never matches NULL — these were invisible) and gate-resolved `waiting_approval` runs. **Server (`studio.functions.ts`, new):** `dispatchStudioSession` (PRD/opportunity/prompt work order, queue-then-return `{missionId}`, model on the run row, prd→mission lineage — `ArtifactKind` gained `'mission'`), `listStudioSessions` (legacy Builder missions included; cost via checkpoint-trace→`ai_events`), `getStudioSession` (timeline steps from checkpoints, changeset+changes, gates, CI snapshot, steers, per-run cost), `steerStudioSession`, `getChangesetDiff`, `refreshStudioCi`. **Surface (`/studio`, first Monaco use):** index = composer (NL prompt, approved-PRD picker, `ModelSwitcher`) + live session list (5s poll; `waiting_approval` reads "waiting on you"); `$missionId` = left timeline (thoughts/tool calls/finals + steers interleaved + inline approve/reject gate cards via `decideApproval`) and right tabs `?tab=changes|pr|cost` (lazy `DiffEditor` per file, PR+CI with refresh, per-run cost); - **2026-06-11 — `F-CRITIC-AGENT` + `F-SCRIBE-CITATIONS` shipped: M1 Golden Path middle hops are now demoable.** The Critic agent (DEC-02) runs inline on every new opportunity (theme- or signal-promoted) and every freshly generated PRD; verdict (ship / revise / kill) + risks + kill criteria + missing evidence land in `opportunities.critic_review` / `prds.critic_review` before the operator sees the row. `OpportunitiesPanel` and the PRD detail header render a verdict chip that opens a side sheet with the full review and a re-run button. `generatePrd` now calls the existing hybrid RAG retriever (`retrieve()`) against the opportunity title+brief, injects up to 8 top chunks as `[n]`-numbered context, instructs Gemini to cite inline, and persists the chunk list to `prds.citations`; a Citations card on the PRD detail page deep-links each entry back to its source (signal → Product · Signals, doc → Knowledge · Docs, meeting → Knowledge · Calendar with `?meeting=`). Critic + Citations turns those two gates into "AI red-teams its own work and cites sources, human governs" — the M1 product claim verbatim. **Files:** new migration `_critic_and_citations`; edited `src/lib/discovery.functions.ts` (added `runCritic` helper + `runCriticReview` server fn + wired into `promoteThemeToOpportunity`, `promoteSignalToOpportunity`, `generatePrd`; RAG retrieval + citation persistence in `generatePrd`); new `src/components/governance/CriticBadge.tsx`, `src/components/product/CitationsCard.tsx`; edited `src/components/product/OpportunitiesPanel.tsx`, `src/routes/_authenticated.prds.$id.tsx`; `docs/planning/feature-backlog.md`, `architecture/runtime.md`, `architecture/orchestration.md`, `docs/features/critic-agent.md` (new), `docs/features/prd-rag-citations.md` (new), `active-task.md`.

- **2026-06-06 — Calendar Parts B + C shipped (pending provider Client IDs).** Per-user calendar OAuth (`F-CALENDAR-PERUSER`): new table `public.user_calendar_connections` (RLS-scoped to `auth.uid()`); canonical app-user OAuth helpers landed at `src/integrations/lovable/appUserConnector.ts` (server-only) + `appUserConnectorClient.ts` (popup-driver, browser-safe); new `src/lib/calendar-connections.functions.ts` (`startCalendarConnect` · `saveCalendarConnection` · `listMyCalendarConnections` · `disconnectCalendar` · `getPrimaryConnection`); `src/lib/calendar.functions.ts` `syncCalendar` / `createCalendarEvent` / `updateCalendarEvent` / `deleteCalendarEvent` are now provider-aware — Google → `google_calendar` connector path, Microsoft → `microsoft_outlook` (Graph) via `callAsAppUser`, and the existing workspace connector stays as fallback when the user has no per-user connection. - **2026-06-06 — v3 language / naming / microcopy companion audit landed.** Same operator-walk method as the main v3 audit, focused entirely on the words: naming, sidebar/IA copy, page H1s, empty states, buttons, placeholders, tooltips, approval-gate prompts, agent/AI surface vocabulary, governance verbs, marketing/public copy. **Findings:** (1) `/login` headline + subhead ("AI-native product operating system") still contradict v2 + v3 thesis on the single most-seen surface — closed-doc loop is broken at its most expensive seam. (2) Sidebar speaks two languages — user-time nouns (Today/Approvals) next to industry jargon (`AI Ops`, `Eval Harness`, `Swarm HUD`, `Build Console`, `Sync Inbox`, `Prompt Studio`). (3) `Phase N` / `Bundle N` internal version labels leak onto 4 operator routes (`/build`, `/discovery`, `/opportunities`, `/prds`) — commit topology shown as product structure. (4) Work-unit nouns drift across screens (Mission · Run · Trajectory · Step · Trace; Agents · Swarm · Specialists; Approvals · Inbox · Reactor activity · Sync Inbox · Attention queue) — operator can't form a stable mental model because the words won't hold still. (5) Tooltips paper over weak labels (`Autonomy dial` needs a tooltip just to define itself; trust chips carry paragraph-long tooltips because `Trust 72 · Proving` doesn't carry the meaning). **Output:** [`docs/strategy/archive/v3-audit-language.md`](./docs/strategy/archive/v3-audit-language.md) — one-page voice guide (operator-grade · reporter · coach; banned words like _unlock_/_seamless_/_humming_; preferred verbs per agent state); naming integrity matrix (11 concepts × current names × canonical proposal × blast radius); full sidebar rename mapping (31 routes → 12 surfaces with old→new label table and back-compat redirect plan); tooltip Keep/Delete/Rewrite/Add audit per route with proposed copy; 5 verbatim rewrites of the most-costly strings; agent/AI vocabulary spec (agent states, trust stages, approval modes, trace step labels, AI-chip copy contract that formalizes `DESIGN.md`); P0–P3 rewrite roadmap (LANG-01..10, TOOLTIP-DEL/REW, LANG-IA-12, LANG-NEW-OUTCOME, LANG-CHIP) with Impact × Effort × Horizon × Strategic × Benefit on every row. Headline ask: pick LANG-01 (`/login` rewrite) + LANG-02 (delete Phase/Bundle labels) + LANG-06 (Today/Swarm empty states) + LANG-08 (sentence-case H1s) for a week-1 ship — zero engineering risk, maximum first-impression lift. **No code changes, no backlog mutations** — same contract as the main audit. **WHY:** the product audit graded the _what_; the operator asked for the _words_ graded next. The two together give a single triage queue. Brand truth, IA legibility, and tooltip discipline are now the cheapest, highest-impact moves on the board — every one is a few-string edit that lifts the 10-second test the v3 audit failed. **Out of scope:** rename of the product itself (held — see [`docs/naming.md`](./docs/decisions/naming.md)), i18n, implementation. **Files:** new `docs/strategy/archive/v3-audit-language.md`; edited `docs/strategy/README.md`, `docs/strategy/session-decisions.md`, `docs/planning/feature-backlog.md`, `plan.md`.

- **2026-06-06 — Bundle 9 Slices 2 + 3 shipped — Builder now closes its own CI loop and runs safely in parallel. FND-RUNTIME 0.9 forced-restart playbook published.** **Slice 2 (CI loop):** two new built-in tools — `github.ci.read` (`read`/`auto`: `GET /pulls/{n}` → head sha → `GET /commits/{sha}/check-runs` + `/status`; returns `{overall: pending|success|failure|neutral, checks[], head_sha, …}`; cached via `withIdempotency('github_ci', '<pr>-<head_sha>', …)` so re-polls don't burn quota and the cache invalidates naturally when the branch's head_sha moves) and `github.commit.append` (`write`/`confirm`: PUTs a single new file on the PR's head branch via Contents API; same `.github/` / `supabase/migrations/` / `.env` / lockfile deny-list as `github.pr.open`; wrapped in `withIdempotency('github_commit', a.idempotency_key, …)` keyed by `issue-<n>-fix-<k>`). The Builder system prompt now mandates: after `github.pr.open`, call `github.ci.read` up to 3× per loop step; on `success`/`neutral` finalize; on `pending` finalize with a wait note and let `resume-runs` re-enter; on `failure` propose ONE follow-up `github.commit.append` whose message names the failing check, then finalize. `listBuilderRuns()` extended to surface the latest `github.ci.read` result per run and expose `failing.{name,html_url,summary}` so the `/build` card and `/missions/$id` timeline render a `CI · green | red · <check> | pending | n/a` chip that links to the failing check. **Slice 3 (conflict guard):** new `builder_file_claims` table — `(user_id, workspace_id, run_id, mission_id, mission_title, repo, path, status, claimed_at, released_at, released_reason)` with a **partial unique index `(repo, path) WHERE status='held'`** so only one held claim per `(repo, path)` exists at a time; RLS = workspace members read, owner writes; PostgREST grants in the same migration. `github.pr.open` now INSERTs the claim row BEFORE the Contents-API PUT and surfaces a typed `BuilderFileConflict: path "<p>" is already claimed by another Builder mission ("<title>")` error on the unique violation — second-mission PR never opens, no branch is created. New SECURITY DEFINER trigger `release_claims_for_terminal_run` (`AFTER UPDATE OF status ON agent_runs`) auto-releases every `held` claim for a run that hits `completed | completed_with_failures | halted | failed`. Operator can force-release via the new **Active file claims** panel on `/build` (5s refresh) which calls new server fn `releaseBuilderClaim({claim_id})` — the Release button is only enabled for the claim owner. **FND-RUNTIME 0.9 playbook:** new `docs/operations/fnd-runtime-restart-playbook.md` is the operator-driven verification — start a Builder mission, restart the worker mid-loop, verify the resume-runs sweeper picks the run up within ≤60s, every idempotency-keyed external write (`github_pr`, `github_commit`, `github_ci`) returns its cached result, repo state matches the single-mission contract (one branch, one PR, one initial commit, optionally one fix commit). `docs/planning/foundation-audit.md` row 0.9 flipped ❌ → 🟡 with a pointer to the playbook (✅ on a clean pass). **Docs loop closed in the same commit:** new `docs/features/bundle-9-builder.md` (canonical per-feature page covering Slice 1 + 2 + 3 — demo script, verification per slice, tool contracts, governance, known limits), new `docs/operations/fnd-runtime-restart-playbook.md`, both indexed in `docs/README.md` + `docs/features/README.md`; `architecture/orchestration.md` Bundle 9 paragraph extended with the new tools + claims ledger. **WHY:** Slice 1 proved the Plan→Build hop end-to-end against a real repo but left two open gaps that block claim C2 ("one governed loop") at production volume — (a) the Builder couldn't see whether its own PR passed CI, so the operator was still the test pipeline, and (b) two parallel missions could silently race on the same file, breaking the autonomy story the moment more than one PRD hit Builder. With Slices 2 + 3 in place the Builder closes its own loop on red and the conflict guard makes parallel Builder dispatch safe — both are prerequisites for an operator-trustable autonomous build lane. **Out of scope this turn (queued):** `github.ci.logs` tool (Builder still only sees check name + summary, not raw job log), `github.pr.update` / `github.pr.merge` (operator owns merge), per-workspace `GITHUB_REPO` (still a single global secret), Restructure Phases 3–4 (theme polish; operator deferred until feature tweaks settle), Proof Platform bundles 10–12 (Ship · Launch · Support→Learn). **Gotchas:** (1) the claim is held by `run_id`, so a single mission re-running `github.pr.open` (e.g. via the idempotency cache path) skips the conflict branch because the holder check matches `existing.run_id === runId`. (2) The CI cache key is `<pr>-<head_sha>`, so after `github.commit.append` lands a new commit the next `github.ci.read` call sees a new head_sha and bypasses the cache — exactly what we want. (3) The auto-release trigger keys off `OLD.status IS DISTINCT FROM NEW.status` so a no-op UPDATE on a terminal run won't try to release already-released rows. (4) `releaseBuilderClaim` is RLS-scoped to the claim's `user_id` — workspace peers can SEE the claim but cannot release each other's; this is intentional until we add a workspace-admin role. **Files:** new `supabase/migrations/<ts>_builder_ci_loop_tools.sql` (Builder prompt + 2 new tool seeds + backfill), new `supabase/migrations/<ts>_builder_file_claims.sql` (claims table + index + grants + RLS + auto-release trigger), new `docs/features/bundle-9-builder.md`, new `docs/operations/fnd-runtime-restart-playbook.md`; edited `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts` (two new tools + claim acquire in `github.pr.open`), `src/lib/build.functions.ts` (CI surface in `listBuilderRuns`, new `listBuilderClaims` + `releaseBuilderClaim`), `src/routes/_authenticated.build.tsx` (CI chip + active-claims panel), `docs/README.md`, `docs/features/README.md`, `docs/planning/foundation-audit.md`, `docs/planning/feature-backlog.md`, `architecture/orchestration.md`, `plan.md`.

- **2026-06-06 — F-AGENT-4: Swarm HUD + per-feature demo/operator docs pattern.** Closes the agent-ecosystem bundle. New route `/swarm` (nav slot: Agents → Swarm HUD, between Missions and Prompt Studio) is a single read-only governor's cockpit over the existing substrate — no new tables, no new tools, no new mutations. One server fn `getSwarmHud()` in `src/lib/swarm.functions.ts` parallel-fires every read (RLS-scoped to `auth.uid()` + workspace via `current_user_default_workspace`): agents + latest non-terminal `agent_runs` per agent (priority `running > paused > queued > terminal`) joined to `agent_autonomy.arc`; missions filtered to `planning|running|completed_with_failures` OR `completed_at >= now()-1h` with `mission_steps` `done/total/failed` aggregates; last 50 `agent_messages` for the handoff feed; pending `agent_approvals`; last 50 `event_queue` rows; throughput from `ai_events` last 60 min bucketed in JS into 5-min windows (count, sum `est_cost_usd`, p50 `latency_ms`); `guardrail_hits` count for the same hour. The page (`src/routes/_authenticated.swarm.tsx`) refreshes every 2s via TanStack Query (`refetchIntervalInBackground: false`), composes 7 inline section components, and has error + not-found boundaries. Writes are zero net-new: inline Approve/Reject calls `resolveApproval` from `governance.functions.ts`; Dispatch/Skip on pending `confirm` reactor rows calls `decideEventDispatch` from `reactor.functions.ts`. **Docs pattern alongside the build:** new `docs/features/` folder with one canonical operator/demo page per shipped feature — `docs/features/README.md` (index + template), `f-agent-1-orchestrator.md`, `f-agent-2-memory-reflection.md`, `f-agent-3-event-reactor.md` (backfilled, ~80 lines each, consolidated from the existing plan §4 entries + architecture bullets — no new claims), and `f-agent-4-swarm-hud.md` (full). Each follows the same skeleton: What it does · Why · Where to find · Demo script ≤ 90s · How it works · Governance & guardrails · Verification checklist · Limits · Related. `docs/README.md` got a new "Per-feature operator & demo guides" section linking the four pages. **WHY:** F-AGENT-1 made Cadence plan, F-AGENT-2 made it learn, F-AGENT-3 made it react — together they produce more concurrent activity than the operator can track from four separate surfaces (`/missions`, `/inbox`, `/agents`, `/governance`). The HUD makes governance scale with the swarm. The features folder makes every shipped capability demo-ready and onboardable from one page, so future demos, sales calls, and onboarding don't have to grep §4 entries + architecture bullets to reconstruct what a feature actually does. **Out of scope (deferred):** pause/steer-from-graph controls, `agent.spawn` fan-out + parent merge (E4 polish), per-mission message-cap loop guard, cross-workspace HUD, retro-priced cost re-calculation, numeric `trust_score` column on `agent_autonomy` (only the arc is shown), and any new mutations beyond the four reused buttons. **Gotchas:** (1) `agent_autonomy` does not have a `trust_score` column — only `arc`. (2) `getSwarmHud` returns jsonb blobs typed as `any` to satisfy TanStack Start's serialization checker. (3) Latest-run-per-agent is computed in JS (not SQL) so we can apply the `running > paused > queued > terminal` priority — an 80-row query window is sufficient for an active swarm. (4) No new index ships with this; if `getSwarmHud()` p50 climbs above ~200ms on a large workspace, add covering indexes on `agent_messages(created_at desc)` and `event_queue(created_at desc)` in a small follow-on migration. **Files:** new `src/lib/swarm.functions.ts`, new `src/routes/_authenticated.swarm.tsx`, new `docs/features/README.md` + 4 feature pages; edited `src/components/cadence/AppShell.tsx` (Swarm HUD nav item), `docs/README.md`, `architecture/orchestration.md`, `docs/planning/feature-backlog.md`, `plan.md`.

- **2026-06-06 — F-AGENT-3: Event reactor + auto-pipelines.** Closes the last "agents do, not just react when summoned" gap. Two new tables: `event_subscriptions` (per-workspace rules: `event_type ∈ {signal.created, opportunity.scored, prd.approved} → target_agent_slug` with `approval_mode auto|confirm` and jsonb `filter`; RLS workspace-member read + owner write, `is_default` flag distinguishes seeded vs operator rules) and `event_queue` (one row per firing, idempotent UNIQUE `(subscription_id, source_id)` so re-firing triggers is a no-op; statuses `pending → dispatched | skipped | failed`; carries `mission_id`/`run_id`/`error`). Three SECURITY DEFINER trigger fns fan-out matching subs into the queue: `signals` (AFTER INSERT), `opportunities` (only on insert or ICE-input change AND `NEW.ice_score >= COALESCE(filter->>'min_score', 8.0)`), `prds` (only on transition into `status='approved'`). New `seed_default_event_subscriptions(uuid)` seeds three defaults per workspace owner — `signal.created → discovery (auto)`, `opportunity.scored → strategist (confirm, min_score 8.0)`, `prd.approved → orchestrator (confirm)`; wired into `handle_new_user` for new signups and backfilled for every existing workspace owner. New `src/lib/reactor.functions.ts` exposes `listEventSubscriptions`, `upsertEventSubscription` (verifies the target agent exists for the user before saving), `deleteEventSubscription`, `listEventQueue`, `decideEventDispatch` (operator approve/reject for `confirm` rows), and a shared `dispatchEvent()` helper that creates a real mission via `createMission` + runs `runAgentLoop` with a templated, event-type-specific goal. New cron route `/api/public/hooks/event-reactor-tick` drains pending `auto`-mode rows (BATCH=10) every minute via pg_cron job `event-reactor-tick`. `confirm`-mode rows stay pending until the operator clicks Dispatch/Skip on the new **Reactor activity** panel on `/governance` (5s auto-refresh). `/governance` also gained an **Auto-pipelines** panel: rule list with enable/disable/delete + add-rule composer (event type / agent slug / mode / min-ICE filter). **WHY:** F-AGENT-1 gave Cadence a planner, F-AGENT-2 gave it memory + autonomy; without a reactor the system still required an operator to push every button. With the reactor in place, a high-ICE opportunity auto-queues a PRD-draft mission, an approved PRD queues an orchestrator plan, and a fresh signal auto-clusters — the discover→define→plan chain runs itself end-to-end behind governance gates. **Out of scope (queued):** F-AGENT-4 (Swarm HUD). **Gotchas:** (1) The dispatch helper calls `runAgentLoop` synchronously inside the cron handler — fine for `auto` orchestrator rows because backpressure already enqueues over-cap missions, but high-frequency event types should wrap with `withIdempotency` or move behind a true queue. (2) Opportunity trigger only checks `>=` against `filter->>'min_score'` (default 8.0); no other comparators yet. (3) Trigger functions are SECURITY DEFINER because the inserting role may not have direct INSERT on `event_queue` — do NOT switch to SECURITY INVOKER. (4) Defaults use `is_default=true` so a future "reset" button can re-seed without clobbering operator rules. **Files:** new `supabase/migrations/<ts>_event_reactor_and_subscriptions.sql`, new `src/lib/reactor.functions.ts`, new `src/routes/api/public/hooks/event-reactor-tick.ts`; edited `src/routes/_authenticated.governance.tsx`, `docs/planning/feature-backlog.md`, `architecture/orchestration.md`, `plan.md`.
- **2026-06-06 — F-AGENT-1: Orchestrator + multi-agent mission decomposition.** First half of the "agent ecosystem" bundle. The substrate (chokepoint, agent*runs, agent_messages, checkpoints, trust, guardrails, missions) already existed but every mission was effectively single-agent — `agent.handoff` was a primitive without a meta-planner. New seed agent `orchestrator` (created on first use via `seed_orchestrator_agent(p_user_id)` SECURITY DEFINER fn; idempotent re-seed bumps the system-prompt + tool wiring). New `mission_steps` table: `(mission_id, idx, agent_slug, sub_goal, depends_on int[], status, run_id, message_id, result, error, rationale, dispatched_at, completed_at)`; RLS scoped to `auth.uid()=user_id` with workspace_member read; unique on `(mission_id, idx)`. New SQL helper `next_ready_mission_steps(mission_id)` returns step rows whose `depends_on` are all `status='done'`. Four new agent tools registered: `mission.plan` calls a sub-model with a planning system prompt (lists the user's actual specialist roster, asks for strict JSON `{summary, steps:[{agent_slug, sub_goal, depends_on, rationale}]}`, 1–8 steps cap, validates every slug is real before persisting); `mission.dispatch` reflects in-flight child-run statuses, then for every ready step calls `enqueueHandoff()` (existing primitive) to insert a child `agent_runs` row + `agent_messages` row, marks the step `dispatched`, records `run_id` + `message_id`; `mission.observe` reflects + returns per-step state + a status histogram + `all_terminal` boolean; `mission.finalize` requires `all_terminal`, marks the mission `completed` or `completed_with_failures`. Loop step cap is per-agent now via `maxStepsFor(agentSlug)` — orchestrator gets 14 to fit plan + observe/dispatch cycles + finalize; specialists keep 6. Three new server fns in `src/lib/orchestrator.functions.ts`: `ensureOrchestrator()` for explicit bootstrap, `startOrchestratedMission({goal,title?,model?})` for the canonical entry (idempotent seed + roster pre-flight + mission row + orchestrator loop), `advanceMission({missionId})` for the operator to push the next round of dispatches manually until F-AGENT-3 wires automatic re-wake, plus `listMissionSteps({missionId})` for read. UI: `/missions` gained an inline "Plan & dispatch" composer (title + goal textarea + one button) so the operator never needs to escape to `/agents` to launch a multi-agent mission; `/missions/$id` gained an "Orchestrator plan" panel above the existing timeline + graph showing the DAG with status pills + deps + an **Advance** button when work remains. Specialist child runs execute asynchronously via the existing `resume-runs` cron — no new infra. **WHY:** the substrate was 95% there but the \_behavior* was missing — until something planned a goal into a graph and dispatched it, "agent-native OS" was the marketing phrase for a single-agent planner-executor. Closes the first of three F-AGENT- gaps that block the autonomous-product-OS thesis. **Out of scope this turn (queued):** F-AGENT-2 (persistent agent memory + auto self-reflection + trust-arc auto-advance), F-AGENT-3 (event reactor + auto-pipelines), F-AGENT-4 (Swarm HUD), Restructure Phases 3–4 (deferred per operator). **Files:** new `supabase/migrations/<ts>_mission_steps_and_orchestrator.sql` (+ a second migration patching the seed function with required `display_name`/`description` on `agent_tools` inserts), new `src/lib/ai/tools/orchestrator.server.ts`, new `src/lib/orchestrator.functions.ts`; edited `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts`, `src/lib/ai/loop.server.ts`, `src/routes/_authenticated.missions.index.tsx`, `src/routes/_authenticated.missions.$missionId.tsx`, `docs/planning/feature-backlog.md`, `plan.md`, `architecture/orchestration.md`.
- **2026-06-06 — F-AGENT-2: Persistent agent memory + auto self-reflection + trust-arc auto-advance.** Second half of the agent-ecosystem bundle (F-AGENT-3 reactor + F-AGENT-4 Swarm HUD still queued). New `src/lib/ai/reflection.server.ts` exports `autoReflect()` (calls Gemini Flash through the chokepoint with `surface='agent', surface_ref='reflect:<slug>'`, expects strict JSON `{lesson, what_worked, what_to_change, importance:1-5}`, writes a `kind='reflection'` row to `agent_memory` with embedding + structured metadata — `run_id`, `trace_id`, `goal`, `what_worked`, `what_to_change`) and `maybeAutoAdvanceArc()` (wraps the new `auto_advance_agent_arc(p_user_id, p_agent_id)` SECURITY DEFINER RPC). `loop.server.ts` calls both from BOTH finalize paths (fresh run + resumed run) when `!halted` — halted runs skip reflection by design, so a governance halt never turns into a self-confirming lesson without operator review. `recallMemory()` now merges two sources: the existing `match_agent_memory` semantic search and the new `recent_agent_reflections` RPC (importance + recency ranked, top 3), deduped by content, capped at 8 — so reflections surface even when the embedding store is sparse or the goal is novel. Two new tools in the registry: `memory.reflect` (category=memory; agent/operator on-demand reflection — reads the current run's input/output if available, wraps `autoReflect`) and `memory.promote` (escalate a memory's scope agent→global so every agent in the workspace recalls it; e.g. "Q3 priority is retention"). Autonomy RPC: `auto_advance_agent_arc` SECURITY DEFINER promotes Observing→Proving at 5 clean completed runs and Proving→Trusted at 20, only when no `agent_approvals.status='rejected'` row exists since the last `agent_autonomy.set_at`; never auto-promotes past Trusted (Ambient stays an explicit operator decision); never downgrades; tolerant of both legacy `status='complete'` (`runAgent` one-shot) and modern `status='completed'` (`loop.server.ts`); sets `set_by=NULL` on system promotion so the UI can distinguish operator vs system moves later. New `recent_agent_reflections(for_user, for_agent_slug, match_count)` SECURITY DEFINER RPC + new `listAgentReflections` server fn (`src/lib/agents.functions.ts`) power a **Recent reflections** panel on `/agents` showing each lesson with importance pill + what-worked / what-to-change sub-blocks pulled out of `metadata`. New cron route `/api/public/hooks/memory-tick` (daily 03:30 UTC via `memory-tick-daily` pg*cron job) deletes `importance <= 2 AND COALESCE(last_used_at, created_at) < now()-30d`, two split passes so the new `agent_memory_decay_idx` is actually used. Migration also fixed the long-standing `agent_memory` grants — table was created without `GRANT SELECT/INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE … TO authenticated`, only `sandbox_exec` had access; PostgREST + admin paths now work. Two new SECURITY DEFINER fns had EXECUTE revoked from PUBLIC (anon can't call them; only `authenticated` + `service_role`). **WHY:** F-AGENT-1 gave us a planner that decomposes goals — F-AGENT-2 makes the resulting work \_compound*. Without persistent reflection every run started cold; without auto-advance the trust dial was operator-only, defeating the point of an autonomy ladder. Together these two close the "agents that learn and earn autonomy" half of the autonomous-product-OS thesis. **Out of scope (queued):** F-AGENT-3 (event reactor: `signal.created`→Discovery, `opportunity.scored>=80`→Strategist, `prd.approved`→Orchestrator + `/governance` subscriptions CRUD), F-AGENT-4 (Swarm HUD route with live missions / handoffs / pending approvals / auto-pipeline firings panels), Restructure Phases 3–4. **Gotchas for the next tool:** (1) reflections write under the per-user supabase client RLS path, so they only land when `runId` exists; ad-hoc loop runs without an `agent_runs` row still reflect via the same helper but the `metadata.run_id` is null — UI handles that. (2) `auto_advance_agent_arc` is called with `set_by=NULL` for system promotions; if you add a "promoted by" badge later, NULL = system, non-NULL = operator. (3) the cron-side admin client bypasses RLS for `memory-tick` deletes — keep importance≤2 + 30d cutoffs tight so we never destroy operator-authored memories (`memory.remember` writes default importance=3, above the floor). (4) `memory.reflect` is intentionally `category=memory` (not `write`), so the autonomy dial cannot loosen it past `auto`; reflections should not be approval-gated. **Files:** new `src/lib/ai/reflection.server.ts`, new `src/routes/api/public/hooks/memory-tick.ts`, two new migrations (`<ts>_agent_memory_grants_and_autonomy_advance.sql` + `<ts>_revoke_public_execute_on_helpers.sql`); edited `src/lib/ai/loop.server.ts`, `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts`, `src/lib/agents.functions.ts`, `src/routes/_authenticated.agents.tsx`, `docs/planning/feature-backlog.md`, `plan.md`, `architecture/orchestration.md`.

- **2026-06-04 — Demo workspace seeding repaired + credentials documented + favicon shipped.** `public.seed_demo_workspace` was silently failing for both demo accounts (`demo@redcadence.app`, `demo2@redcadence.app`) because it tried to insert `slug='demo'` into `workspaces.slug`, which is globally `UNIQUE` and was already taken by an older demo row from another owner — the credential migration's `EXCEPTION WHEN OTHERS` swallowed the constraint violation, so both accounts only got an empty "My Workspace". New migration restores the full seeder body with a per-owner slug (`'demo-' || substr(user_id::text, 1, 8)`, NULL fallback if even that is taken), cleans the empty `My workspace` rows for both demo users, and re-runs `seed_demo_workspace` — both accounts now sign in to a fully populated Demo workspace (Lumen project, 3 themes, 9 signals, 5 opportunities, 2 PRDs, 10 tasks, 4 docs, 2 meetings, 3 decisions, 18 AI events, eval suite, drift snapshots, daily briefs). - **2026-06-04 — Bundle 6 lifecycle close shipped — Discover→Define→Plan can now exit to a real GitHub issue + PRD link-back.** The two tool handlers (`github.issue.create`, `prd.link_issue`) already lived in `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts` from FND-RUNTIME 0.9 + Bundle 2, but `prd.link_issue` was missing from `seed_pm_lifecycle_tools` and `github.issue.create` was seeded for new signups at `mode='review'` (and unseeded for legacy users), so the Planner couldn't actually pick either up under the trust dial. New migration rewrites both seed functions: `seed_pm_lifecycle_tools` now also installs `prd.link_issue` (write/`confirm`), `seed_default_agent_tools` re-affirms `github.issue.create` at write/`confirm` (was `review`) so the Plan stage can ship under arc-based gating, and both functions then run inside a backfill `DO` loop over every existing `profiles` row so missions starting today have the right `agent_tools` rows. UI surface: `/prds/$id` now renders a clickable `Github · GitHub issue #N` chip immediately below the back-link when `prds.github_issue_url` is set (number parsed from the URL). Idempotency: the `github.issue.create` handler is already wrapped in `withIdempotency('github_issue', a.idempotency_key, …)` so re-execution after a worker restart or the resume-runs sweeper picking up a stalled run returns the cached `{ number, url, id, repo, cached: true }` — it never double-creates the issue. **WHY:** claim C3 ("one governed loop") only becomes literally true once the Plan stage can exit the platform into the engineering system of record under an operator-controlled gate; without the seed + the link-back chip the loop visibly stopped at "draft PRD" and the operator had to copy/paste into GitHub. **Out of scope this turn (deferred to Bundle 9):** `github.pr.open`, CI read into the Mission Graph, branch/PR back-link on the PRD page, `github.issue.update`/`close`. **Files:** new `supabase/migrations/<ts>_seed_github_issue_and_link.sql`; edited `src/routes/_authenticated.prds.$id.tsx`, `architecture/orchestration.md`, `docs/planning/feature-backlog.md`.
- **2026-06-04 — Bundle 5 Live Mission Graph (E6) shipped.** `/missions/$id` only had a linear timeline + per-hop progress panel; multi-agent missions couldn't be _seen_ as a graph, which is the literal success criterion for Step 5 of the build-order rollup ("graph updates in real time as agents act; clicking a node opens that agent's trace + cost + tokens + approval state"). Added a pure-SVG DAG component `src/components/cadence/MissionGraph.tsx` and mounted it above the existing timeline + hops list. **Nodes** = one per `agent_runs` row in the mission; status color + glyph + agent name + slug + status text. **Edges** = one per `agent_messages` row, drawn `source_run_id → consumed_by_run_id`; for in-flight handoffs not yet consumed, fall back to the earliest later hop targeting `to_agent_slug`. Edges are violet bezier paths with arrow markers + the message `kind` label. **Layout** = BFS-depth columns (root hops at column 0, each handoff bumps the child's column) × chronological rows within column, so a single-agent mission renders 1 node / 0 edges and a Discovery → Strategist → Builder mission renders 3 nodes connected by 2 labelled edges; multiple outbound messages from the same parent stack as parallel children in the next column (E4 fan-out polish ready without a new tool). **Interaction**: nodes are real `role="button"` SVG groups with `onKeyDown` Enter/Space; clicking expands the matching hop card (adds to the existing `expanded` Set) and smooth-scrolls via `id="hop-{run_id}"` + `scroll-mt-24`. Re-uses the existing `refetchInterval: 2000` while mission `status='running'`/`queued`, so the graph fills in live. Pure read model — no schema change, no new server fn, consumes the existing `getMission` payload. WHY: Step 5 of the build-order rollup needs the graph to be literally true, and Bundle 4's claim ("A2A is first-class, no human in the routing path") only becomes operator-legible once the routing is visible as a graph rather than a list. **Out of scope this turn:** pause/steer-from-graph controls, zoom/collapse for >20-node graphs, per-node cost/token rollup pill (needs `getMission` to surface it), explicit `agent.spawn` tool. **Files:** new `src/components/cadence/MissionGraph.tsx`; edited `src/routes/_authenticated.missions.$missionId.tsx`, `architecture/orchestration.md`, `docs/planning/feature-backlog.md`.
- **2026-06-04 — Mission page: live progress panel + agent timeline + Firecrawl search fix.** Operator dispatched a Discovery mission and watched it sit at `running` with 0 hops and no visible activity. Two issues. (1) `web.search` was halting the loop on step 1 with `rows.map is not a function` — Firecrawl v2 `/search` returns `{data:{web,news,images}}` (object), not an array. Parser in `src/lib/ai/tools/firecrawl.server.ts` now handles array, `{web,news}` object, and the legacy `web`/`results` shapes. (2) `/missions/$id` had no live observability — once a hop was running there was nothing to look at. Extended `getMission` (`src/lib/missions.functions.ts`) to also fetch the latest `agent_run_checkpoints` row per run (extracts `traceId` + `steps[]`) and join `tool_calls` by trace id, then rebuilt `src/routes/_authenticated.missions.$missionId.tsx`: an **Agent timeline** strip at the top (one chip per hop with status icon, agent slug, elapsed duration, handoff arrows showing lineage end-to-end), a **live progress panel inside each hop card** listing the loop's `steps[]` (thought · tool*call · final, with per-call status + args/error preview), and a **Tool spans** subsection (per-tool name + ok/err + latency from `tool_calls`). Always visible while `running`/`queued`; collapses behind Detail when finished. Refresh interval tightened to 2s while live; header shows a live indicator; each hop card now exposes a one-click `/traces/$traceId` link. WHY: claim C1 ("agents \_do*, humans govern") requires the operator to _see_ the doing in real time — without per-step visibility a mission feels frozen even when it's running, and silent tool failures (like the Firecrawl bug) hide forever. **Out of scope this turn:** DAG view for parallel fan-out (still queued for Bundle 5), per-step token/cost rollup on the hop card, websocket push (we still poll). **Files:** edited `src/lib/missions.functions.ts`, `src/routes/_authenticated.missions.$missionId.tsx`, `src/lib/ai/tools/firecrawl.server.ts`, `docs/planning/feature-backlog.md`, `plan.md`.
- **2026-06-04 — Web access for agents shipped (Firecrawl-backed `web.*` tools).** Agents were siloed: a goal like _"scout how Linear's AI triage is positioned and give me a non-reactive one-pager"_ needed the public internet but had no tool to call, so they hallucinated or stopped short. Added four governed tools to `TOOL_REGISTRY` — `web.search` (ranked results + optional in-line scrape), `web.fetch` (single URL → markdown), `web.map` (URL discovery), `web.crawl` (bounded crawl, max 25 pages / depth 2) — all routed through one helper `src/lib/ai/tools/firecrawl.server.ts` that reads `FIRECRAWL_API_KEY` from `process.env` only. Search/fetch/map default to `auto`; `web.crawl` defaults to `confirm` because it spends real Firecrawl credits. Returns are clipped (search snippets 2 KB, fetch markdown 8 KB default / 20 KB max, crawl pages 4 KB each) so token spend stays predictable. Results re-enter the loop as untrusted input — the next `callModel()` already runs them through pre-guardrails (PII / prompt-injection / secret keyword) per `architecture/runtime.md`, no new code required. Trust arc + kill-switch + per-mission spend cap still apply unchanged because tools sit in the same registry. Connected Firecrawl as a workspace connector (`FIRECRAWL_API_KEY`). Migration updates `seed_default_agent_tools` for new signups and backfills the four tool rows for every existing user. WHY: closes the "agents _do_, humans govern" gap — without outbound web I/O the platform was a workspace-only reasoner, not an operator. **Out of scope this turn:** per-user domain allow/deny UI, a higher-level `web.research` chain tool, browser automation, swapping providers. **Files:** new `src/lib/ai/tools/firecrawl.server.ts`, new `docs/web-access.md`, new `supabase/migrations/<ts>_web_tools_seed.sql`; edited `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts`, `architecture/integrations.md`, `docs/planning/feature-backlog.md`, `docs/README.md`.
- **2026-06-04 — Bundle 4 Agent-to-Agent handoff (E1–E5 MVP) shipped.** New `missions` + `agent_messages` tables (RLS-scoped to workspace members; hop counter + current-agent kept in sync via trigger); `agent_runs.mission_id` added (nullable, single-agent runs still valid). New module `src/lib/ai/handoff.server.ts` exports `createMission`, `enqueueHandoff`, `consumeInboundHandoff`, `renderHandoffBlock`, `maybeCompleteMission`. New `agent.handoff` tool in `TOOL_REGISTRY` (write/`confirm`; structured payload = `task + context + artifacts + open_questions + constraints`) — inserts the message AND enqueues a child `agent_runs` row with the same `mission_id`; the existing FND-RUNTIME 0.9 resume-runs sweeper picks it up. `ToolCtx` extended with `missionId` + `workspaceId`. The loop (both fresh `runAgentLoop` and `resumeAgentLoop`) consumes the latest inbound handoff at run start and prepends a `--- Handoff from {agent} ---` block to the system prompt right after the workspace brief — receiver gets a typed JSON payload, never a pasted prompt. Receiver's autonomy arc continues to gate its own tool calls. Failure policy is option-b: hop failures stop the mission; operator re-dispatches manually (documented in `docs/a2a-handoff.md`). - **2026-06-04 — Bundle 3 Agent Trust Score + Autonomy Dial (C6) shipped.** New `agent_autonomy` table (one row per user+agent, arc enum `observing|proving|trusted|ambient`, owner-only RLS, standard GRANTs). Trust score is computed on read in `src/lib/ai/trust.server.ts` (`computeAllAgentTrust`) from real signals — mission completion rate (`agent_runs.status`), approval acceptance rate (`agent_approvals.status`), and eval mean (`ai_evals.score` joined via `ai_events.agent_id`) — Bayesian-shrunk toward 0.5 when sample <10 so a single-run agent doesn't render as 100. `resolveApprovalMode(toolMode, arc)` is the single combiner the loop calls at the gate decision: Observing forces `review` even on `auto` tools, Proving forces `confirm`, Trusted runs `confirm` inline, Ambient runs everything inline. Safety floor: `review` is sticky (never downgraded by the dial), and `calendar.create` keeps `confirm` even at Ambient. Server fns `getAllAgentTrust` + `setAgentArc` in `src/lib/trust.functions.ts` (both `requireSupabaseAuth`). `src/lib/ai/loop.server.ts` now loads the arc once per run (both fresh and resumed paths) and uses `resolveApprovalMode` at every tool-call gate instead of reading `modeOf.get(name)` directly. UI: `/agents` renders a color-tiered Trust chip (with hover tooltip showing the full breakdown + formula + suggested arc) on every roster button and the detail header, plus an inline AutonomyDial (4 arc buttons + suggested-arc hint + plain-language explainer) inside the detail card; the dispatch mutation also invalidates the trust query so a completed mission updates the score in place. WHY: makes C4 ("trust is dialed, not assumed") concrete and operator-controllable in the same surface where missions are dispatched — the dial visibly converts earned trust into reduced friction. Files: new `supabase/migrations/<ts>_agent_autonomy.sql`, `src/lib/ai/trust.server.ts`, `src/lib/trust.functions.ts`; edited `src/lib/ai/loop.server.ts`, `src/routes/_authenticated.agents.tsx`.

- **2026-06-03 — PM lifecycle tools shipped (`research.synthesize`, `prd.draft`, `backlog.prioritize`).** Added 3 PM-centric agentic tools to `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts` and seeded them into `agent_tools` for every existing user (and for new signups via the updated `seed_default_agent_tools(uuid)`), all default `confirm` mode. (1) `research.synthesize` — pulls recent ungrouped `signals` (filterable by tag/sentiment/lookback), asks the model (via `callModel`, surface=`discovery`, `responseFormat=json_object`) to cluster them into 2–6 cohesive themes, writes `themes` rows (severity 1–5, confidence 0–1, frequency = signal count) and links source signals via `signals.theme_id`. (2) `prd.draft(opportunity_id)` — reads the opportunity, joins its `theme` + top 8 supporting signals, asks the model (surface=`prd`) to draft a structured PRD (Problem / Target user / Goals / Non-goals / Stories / Solution sketch / Success metrics / Risks) and writes a `prds` row in `draft` status with `model` recorded. (3) `backlog.prioritize` — for each backlog opportunity, gathers supporting-signal count + recency (last 7d), asks the model to re-score ICE (1–10 integers) with rationale, updates `opportunities.{impact,confidence,ease}` (ice_score is a generated column so it recomputes), returns the new ranked list with rationales. All three flow through the AI chokepoint so they hit guardrails + budgets + tracing, and through the agent loop they pick up `runId`/`stepIndex` automatically for idempotent retry on resume. No per-agent assignment needed — the loop filters `TOOL_REGISTRY` by what the user has enabled, so Discovery Scout / PRD Writer / Strategist see them immediately. Closes the Define + Plan halves of the Bundle 6 lifecycle slice that previously had only the GitHub-issue write on the Build edge. Files: `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts`, migration `seed_pm_lifecycle_tools(uuid)` + folded into `seed_default_agent_tools(uuid)` with a backfill loop.
- **2026-06-03 — FND-RUNTIME 0.9 runtime instrumentation + N1 `github.issue.create` shipped.** Added `src/lib/runtime/idempotency.server.ts` (`withIdempotency(scope,key,userId,runId,fn)` → execute → INSERT-on-conflict-fall-back-to-cached against the new `idempotency_keys` table). Refactored `src/lib/ai/loop.server.ts` so both `runAgentLoop()` (fresh) and new exported `resumeAgentLoop(runId)` (rehydrates from latest `agent_run_checkpoints` row) feed a shared `executeLoop()`; every iteration upserts a checkpoint _before_ the provider call (so a `GovernanceHaltError` mid-stream never re-bills on resume) and wraps tool execution in `withIdempotency` keyed `tool:{runId}:{stepIndex}:{toolName}` — replaying a step short-circuits to the cached result instead of re-invoking the side-effecting tool. Added per-workspace **backpressure** (default 5 concurrent `running` runs); over-cap missions insert as `status='queued'` and are promoted by the new `/api/public/hooks/resume-runs` sweeper, which also resumes `running` runs whose `last_checkpoint_at` is >2 min stale (worker eviction). Sweeper is `pg_cron`-driven every minute against the stable preview URL. Added **`github.issue.create`** agentic tool to `TOOL_REGISTRY` (category `write`, default `confirm` mode): writes to the single allow-listed `GITHUB_REPO` env, validated `owner/name` format, idempotent via caller-supplied `idempotency_key` (e.g. PRD id) so re-execution from a checkpoint never double-creates an issue. ToolCtx extended with optional `runId` + `stepIndex` so future tools can key their own idempotency without re-deriving. Files: `src/lib/runtime/idempotency.server.ts` (new), `src/lib/ai/tools/registry.server.ts`, `src/lib/ai/loop.server.ts`, `src/routes/api/public/hooks/resume-runs.ts` (new), plus a `pg_cron` migration scheduling `resume-runs` every minute. Forced-restart integration test still TODO. Lifecycle slice (Bundle 6 Discover→Define→Plan against a real Cadence signal, approving the real GitHub-issue write) is now the operator-driven next step.
- **2026-06-03 — FND-RUNTIME 0.9 foundation landed (decision + schema + secrets).** Wrote `docs/decisions/durable-runtime.md` selecting a **DB-backed durable job table** over Cloudflare Queues — rationale: matches existing `/api/public/hooks/*` + `pg_cron` + tenancy patterns; zero new infra/runtime/auth model; portable off Cloudflare; visible to the human governor as ordinary rows. Applied a migration adding (1) `agent_run_checkpoints` — append-only, one row per loop iteration, `UNIQUE (run_id, step_index)`, `state JSONB`, full tenancy keys, RLS scoped to `auth.uid()`; (2) `idempotency_keys` — `UNIQUE (scope, key)` dedup table for `/api/public/hooks/*` ticks (`tick:{hook}:{run_id}:{step_index}`) and tool execution (`tool:{run_id}:{step_index}:{tool_name}`) so a resumed step never re-executes a side-effecting tool; (3) `agent_runs.step_index` + `last_checkpoint_at` for heartbeat + resume cursor. Both new tables have `GRANT … TO authenticated`/`service_role` and RLS. Requested + received `GITHUB_TOKEN` + `GITHUB_REPO` secrets so the next stage — first lifecycle slice end-to-end on the Cadence repo (Bundle 6 Discover→Define→Plan + N1 `github.issue.create`) — has no hard blocker. `active-task.md` extended with the loop-checkpoint, `resumeAgentLoop`, `/api/public/hooks/resume-runs` sweeper, backpressure, and lifecycle-slice sub-steps; Live status board now shows "Now building: FND-RUNTIME (0.9) · Lovable · main".
