## 5. Legacy build log (retained — the previous source, for reuse)

> This is the earlier build (the "vibe-coded" source). **It is a reuse reference, not the plan.** Mine it for what survives the stress-test; supersede entries as they're rebuilt into section 4. Do not treat anything here as current truth without checking the code.

- **Foundation** — Supabase auth (email + Google OAuth), `profiles`, workspaces + extended `projects`, persistent SSE chat with workspace grounding, model-agnostic router with per-surface defaults, command palette (⌘K), Mission Control widgets, OKLCH dark theme, RLS, loader+Suspense pattern, route boundaries, global auth middleware. _(Largely reusable.)_
- **Discovery & specs** — `signals` ingest (paste/CSV, chunked inserts; sentiment on insert), clustering (k-medoid + synthesis with `evidence_ids[]`), themes → ICE opportunities, one-click PRD → Tiptap with `/ai` slash menu, `prd_versions` autosave + diff, early pgvector RAG (512/64 chunks, 1536-d). _(Reusable; this is the first-slice base.)_
- **Planning & meeting intelligence** — Now/Next/Later board (`@dnd-kit`). _(Tail of this legacy entry was lost in an earlier edit collision that spliced the §6 heading mid-line — recover details from git history if ever needed.)_

## 6. Product-agent roster (re-examined: explicit vs. implicit)

**The question:** is a fixed roster of 16 named agents right? **Answer:** no — split it. Use a small set of **durable, named lifecycle agents** (explicit, one owner per stage) plus an orchestrator that **dynamically spawns ephemeral specialist sub-agents** for sub-tasks (implicit). Fixed seats for micro-roles create clutter; dynamic sub-agents scale with the work.

**6 outcome-focused durable agents (explicit, one per lifecycle band):**

The roster is kept narrow and delivery-oriented. Each agent owns a clear band of the product lifecycle. Fixed seats for micro-roles are avoided — those collapse into ephemeral specialists.

| Agent            | Lifecycle band                                                  | Owns                                                                                                             | Primary pain point addressed                                    |
| ---------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Orchestrator** | All stages                                                      | Mission coordination, spawns ephemeral specialists, manages approval routing, parallelism                        | Coordination overhead, context loss between stages              |
| **Discovery**    | S1 Signal Capture + S2 Audio Sync                               | Signal Ingest (Zendesk/Intercom/Slack), clustering opportunities, WhisperFlow transcription and audio extraction | Shallow discovery, anecdotal signals, missing verbal alignments |
| **Strategist**   | S3 ICE Prioritization + S4 Spec Definition + S5 Sprint Planning | Opportunity scoring, cited PRD generation, Linear/GitHub Issues sync, dependency-aware task graphs               | Spec drafting overhead, weak prioritization, feature factories  |
| **Builder**      | S6 Agentic Build + S7 Visual QA + S8 Safe Release               | Multi-file coding, file claims ledger, sandbox previews, PR merge checks and deploy monitoring                   | Developer bottlenecks, styling drift, release quality checks    |
| **Growth**       | S9 GTM Launch                                                   | Outbound changelogs, blog posts, Slack notifications and release announcements                                   | Launch overhead, delayed go-to-market communication             |
| **Analyst**      | S10 Support Triage + S11 Cohort Analytics + S12 Learn & Reflect | Support ticket routing to S1, adoption funnels, performance metrics vs PRD specs, Product Memory                 | Closed-loop support, un-measured features, memory decay         |

**Ephemeral specialists (spawned by Orchestrator per task):** competitor scan, UX critique, stakeholder brief, data analysis, security review, code review, and any other short-lived specialist. They inherit the chokepoint, tool allow-list, and governance. No permanent seats for micro-roles.

**Persona mapping:**

- **P1 (Director / VP of Product)**: strategic oversight, budget controls, audit log reviews, portfolio health, uses Analyst + Orchestrator.
- **P2 (Lead / Senior PM)**: daily operator, runs swarm briefs, PRD editor, discovery feeds, uses Discovery + Strategist + Analyst.
- **P3 (Engineering Lead)**: code review, Builder agent claims review, CI verification, uses Builder.
- **P4 (UX/UI Designer)**: sandbox preview validation, style token audit, uses Builder (Visual QA).
- **P5 (GTM Lead)**: launch copywriting, distribution approvals, uses Growth.
- **P6 (Support Lead)**: triage validation, bug signal loops, uses Analyst.

Schema per agent: `slug, name, system_prompt, tool_allowlist[], default_model, temperature/top_p/seed, max_tokens, schedule_cron?, approval_mode (auto|confirm|review), memory_enabled`. Roster changes need a migration + a build-order entry.

---

## 7. Testing strategy

- **Unit:** pricing math, each guardrail rule kind, RAG chunker boundaries, ICE/cron/date helpers.
- **Integration:** chokepoint (one `ai_events` row + trace; budget throws before provider; cache short-circuits but logs; guardrail block aborts + logs; ticks idempotent); orchestration (parallel sessions isolated; checkpoints resume; cancellation saves partial trace); RLS isolation across products/workspaces.
- **Autonomous build/test loop:** the Builder agent's output must pass the QA agent's generated tests before Ship; a failing eval suite ("Cadence core") blocks deploy (≥10-point regression on the 0–100 scale, without override — KI-14).
- **E2E:** intent → discover → define → plan → build → test → ship, watched in the orchestration view; multi-product isolation; ⌘K across routes; `/observe` renders on seeded data.
- **Manual QA before release:** auth + tenancy isolation; every route empty/partial/full; AI message contract present ([`DESIGN.md`](./DESIGN.md)); guardrail block works; budget breach is friendly; light-theme Cohere editorial contrast.

---

## 8. Lessons learned (kept from the legacy build)

One AI chokepoint paid for itself (judge added in half a day). Loader + `useSuspenseQuery` killed `useEffect+fetch` regressions. OKLCH tokens ended dark-mode contrast bugs. Bugs fixed: name-vs-email leak; duplicate agent fan-out (advisory lock); action-item due-date glitch; Notion BFS reorder; trace recursion blow-up; cache cross-user poisoning (salted key); CSV params cap (chunked inserts). Known limits: clustering degrades past ~1000 signals/run; Studio truncates files >2k lines; Docs sync drops comments; `model_pricing` hand-maintained.

---

## 9. Out of scope (for now)

Fine-tuning workflows from `ai_events`; cross-workspace vector sharing; public agent/skill-pack marketplace; cross-workspace SSO; fully autonomous _strategic_ decisions (strategic conclusions keep a human gate by design — tactical ones may auto-apply). These are deliberate exclusions, revisited when the core loop is solid.

**H3 · Scheduling (calendar-aware work blocks) — SHIPPED.** Agent proposes deep-work blocks into free time within the operator's working hours, fitting the task around meetings and respecting focus. Built: (1) `proposeWorkBlocks` server fn in `calendar.functions.ts` — reads open deep-work tasks (is_deep_work=true, status != done) from the `tasks` table, fetches the user's working-hours bounds from the profile, queries calendar events for the next 7 days (daysAhead param), and uses a simple greedy algorithm (30-min slot buckets, skip weekends/out-of-hours, skip conflicts) to place one block per task into the first-fit free slot. Returns a list of WorkBlock (start_at, end_at, title, label with formatted time). Boundaries are soft (a packed calendar yields fewer blocks; no forced fit). (2) UI affordance in `CalendarPanel.tsx` — a "Plan deep work" button in the action bar triggers the proposal, showing a panel with the proposed blocks + "Add to calendar" per-block buttons; a visual state change (color shift) marks added blocks; a "Re-plan · new proposal" option re-runs the algorithm (useful if the calendar changed). (3) Mutations integrate with the existing `createCalendarEvent` so added blocks sync two-way with the user's calendar provider (Google/Microsoft). **Scope:** the proposal algorithm is honest (no speculative ML or scoring); the 7-day window and 30-min bucket size are sensible defaults (tunable via params). Deferred: adaptive working-hour inference, multi-day blocks, and conflict re-routing (schedule around soft-constraints rather than hard skip). **Verification:** `bun test` 163 green, `bun run build` green, `eslint` clean, dev server boots. Manual: seeded workspace with 3 open deep-work tasks + a calendar with 6 events → "Plan deep work" proposes 2 blocks (Tue afternoon, Thu morning, both 60-min, both fit free slots, both fit within 09:00–18:00). **Files:** `src/lib/calendar.functions.ts` (proposeWorkBlocks + type), `src/components/knowledge/CalendarPanel.tsx` (affordance + mutations + UI), dashboard/this log.

**U6 · Workspace data export (data portability), CORE SHIPPED (autonomous overnight cycle 1, 2026-06-18).** The trust escape-hatch: Settings > Data downloads the entire workspace as one JSON file. Built: (1) `exportWorkspace` server fn in `projects.functions.ts` (mirrors B5 `exportProduct` at workspace scope): resolves the active workspace (passed from the client, falling back to first membership), gathers projects (by workspace_id), signals/opportunities/specs(`prds`)/tasks (by project_id across the workspace's projects, guarded against the empty-projects case so it never issues an empty `in()`), and the user's own `learnings` + `agent_memory` (owner-scoped by user_id). RLS scopes every read to the caller; returns a JSON-safe shape with a per-section `counts` map. No migration (read-only). (2) `DataExportCard.tsx` in `src/components/settings/` + a new "Data" tab on `/settings`: a calm-front card that calls the fn, downloads `cadence-workspace-export-<date>.json`, and toasts the record count. It passes the active workspace id so multi-workspace users export the right one. **Adversarial review folded 2 fixes:** the empty-projects `.in([])` guard, and the active-workspace-id pass-through (it was exporting the first workspace, not the active one). **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `eslint` clean, `bun run build` green. **Pending founder publish + live verify** (not deployed yet). **Remaining (◐):** per-section selective export + an export audit-log. **Files:** `src/lib/projects.functions.ts`, `src/components/settings/DataExportCard.tsx`, `src/routes/_authenticated.settings.tsx`, `docs/features/u6-data-export.md`, dashboard/this log.

**R3 · Notifications, in-app Attention feed CORE SHIPPED (autonomous overnight cycle 2, 2026-06-18).** The operator hears about what needs them, in one place. Built: (1) `getNotifications` server fn in a new `src/lib/notifications.functions.ts`: derives a unified feed live from the loop's own state, with no new table: pending tool-call approvals (`agent_approvals` status=pending), a stalled loop (`agent_runs` running/queued past the 30-minute window), and spend nearing or over a cap (`ai_budgets` daily/monthly vs `alert_at_pct`). Read-only, RLS-scoped by user_id; each probe degrades to a safe default so the feed can never break its surface. Returns a severity-sorted `AppNotification[]` (action > warning > info) with a deep-link href per item, plus a `count` for a future bell badge. (2) `NotificationsPanel.tsx` + a new "Attention" tab on the Engine Room (`/govern?tab=attention`): a calm feed of severity-coded cards, each linking to its home (approvals / spend / loop-health), with an "All clear" empty state. **Adversarial review folded 1 fix:** placed Attention second (not first) so the default-selected leftmost tab stays Controls (no behavior change; the default landing is left to a founder taste call). **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `eslint` clean, `bun run build` green. **Pending founder publish + live verify.** **Remaining (◐):** email + digests, per-user notification prefs, and the global bell badge. **Files:** `src/lib/notifications.functions.ts`, `src/components/governance/NotificationsPanel.tsx`, `src/routes/_authenticated.govern.tsx`, `docs/features/r3-notifications.md`, dashboard/this log.

**P7 · Incidents log, read-only CORE SHIPPED (autonomous overnight cycle 3, 2026-06-18).** A record when something goes wrong, instead of failures vanishing into the logs. Built: (1) `getIncidents` server fn in a new `src/lib/incidents.functions.ts`: derives a read-only "what went wrong" log with no new table from confirmed sources: `agent_approvals` (status=failed, by user_id) for failed tool executions, and `event_queue` (rows with a non-null error, scoped to the resolved default workspace) for errored auto-pipelines. Merged newest-first, capped at 40; each execution carries its `trace_id`. (2) `IncidentsPanel.tsx` + a new "Incidents" tab on the Engine Room (`/govern?tab=incidents`): cards with the error detail, a timestamp, and a "View trace" link per execution; "No incidents" empty state. **Adversarial review folded 1 fix:** explicit workspace scoping on `event_queue` (matching the reactor pattern) rather than relying on RLS alone. **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `eslint` clean, `bun run build` green. **Pending founder publish + live verify.** **Remaining (◐):** guardrail/cost incident sources + a persistent incidents table for manual logging. **Files:** `src/lib/incidents.functions.ts`, `src/components/governance/IncidentsPanel.tsx`, `src/routes/_authenticated.govern.tsx`, `docs/features/p7-incidents.md`, dashboard/this log.

**C4/E7 · Agent inspector (run history), CORE SHIPPED (autonomous overnight cycle 4, 2026-06-18).** See what each agent has actually been doing, not just its trust score. Built: (1) `getAgentRuns` server fn in a new `src/lib/agent-runs.functions.ts`: reads `agent_runs` filtered by user_id (RLS + explicit, defense-in-depth) and agent_id, newest-first, capped at 25; returns each run's status, mission_id, step_index, created_at. (2) `AgentInspector.tsx` in `src/components/cockpit/` + a one-line mount in `AgentsPanel` (Missions > Agents, below the trust dial): an agent dropdown + that agent's recent run list (status, mission, step, time), with a "no runs yet" empty state. **Adversarial review: clean** (hooks kept unconditional before the early return; RLS + explicit user_id filter; schema grounded against `agent_runs` before building). **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `eslint` clean, `bun run build` green. **Pending founder publish + live verify.** **Remaining (◐):** the shared/private memory inspector (needs agent-scope columns on `agent_memory` confirmed live). **Files:** `src/lib/agent-runs.functions.ts`, `src/components/cockpit/AgentInspector.tsx`, `src/components/cockpit/AgentsPanel.tsx`, `docs/features/c4-e7-agent-inspector.md`, dashboard/this log.

**C4/E7 · Agent memory inspector, COMPLETES C4/E7 (autonomous overnight cycle 5, 2026-06-18).** What each agent knows, alongside its run history. Built: (1) `getAgentMemory` server fn (in `agent-runs.functions.ts`): returns the selected agent's memories, its own (private, `agent_id=agentId`) plus the shared/global pool (`scope=global`), via two injection-safe `.eq()` queries merged and deduped by id (no `.or()` string interpolation, so a crafted agentId cannot rewrite the filter), RLS-scoped. (2) extended `AgentInspector.tsx` with a "What this agent knows" section below the run history: each memory labelled shared or private, with its kind + content. **Adversarial review: clean** (injection-safe two-query merge; hooks kept unconditional). **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `eslint` clean, `bun run build` green. With this, C4/E7 is complete (run history + shared/private memory). **Pending founder publish + live verify** (incl. confirming `agent_memory.agent_id` matches the swarm agent id). **Files:** `src/lib/agent-runs.functions.ts`, `src/components/cockpit/AgentInspector.tsx`, `docs/features/c4-e7-agent-inspector.md`, dashboard/this log.

**D4 mission cancellation (the per-mission brake) + H1-TASKS reconciliation (autonomous overnight cycle 10, 2026-06-18).** This cycle corrects cycle 8's read that D4 was "NOT gate-verifiable, unsafe to build blind." That call lumped D4's cancellation slice in with the harder replay/checkpoint work. Deep recon proved the **cancellation slice** is safe and fully offline-gateable: the auto-advance tick already selects missions by `.in("status",["running","in_progress"])` and `advanceMissionCore` early-returns for any non-running mission, so cancelling is a pure state transition with **zero loop surgery**; `missions.status`/`agent_runs.status` carry no CHECK and `agent_approvals.status` already allows `cancelled`, so **no migration**. Built `cancelMission` (`missions.functions.ts`) + a "Cancel mission" control in the mission-detail hero (`useConfirm`, shown only while active) + a `cancelled` `StatusBadge`. The cascade stops the resume cron resuming orphaned child runs (required for correctness, not cosmetics), releases held Build file claims (the `release_claims_for_terminal_run` trigger skips `cancelled`, so locks would otherwise orphan), and clears pending approvals. **Gate:** `tsc --noEmit` clean, `bun run build` green, the 3 touched files lint clean (the repo-wide `bun run lint` shows pre-existing prettier debt in untouched files, flagged in the report; not mass-reformatted). **Adversarial review** folded a TOCTOU guard (only flip to `cancelled` if still non-terminal, so a mission that finishes in the read→write window keeps its honest state) and confirmed `completed_at` does not corrupt the analytics completion metric (it filters on `status='completed'`). Also reconciled **`H1-TASKS` → ✅**: PRD → engineering task graph is already built end to end (`generateTaskGraph` in `discovery.functions.ts` + the dependency-ordered task-graph card on `/prds/$id`). **Permission policy hardening + capture (autonomous overnight cycle 13, 2026-06-18, founder-requested).** The founder was getting a permission prompt on every read/edit/command. Root cause: a session reads the `.claude/settings.local.json` of the directory it is LAUNCHED from; this session runs from the repo ROOT, but the bypass config only existed in the WORKTREE's copy, so the root session prompted on everything. **Fix:** (1) set `defaultMode: bypassPermissions` + the broad allow + destructive deny + both directories in the **root** `.claude/settings.local.json` (local, gitignored, per-machine); (2) added a shared `permissions` allow/deny block to the **committed** `.claude/settings.json` so the lists travel with the repo and cover regular daytime builds too (no `defaultMode` there — bypass stays a per-machine opt-in, never committed); (3) wrote [`docs/operations/permissions.md`](docs/operations/permissions.md) capturing the two-layer model, the deny-list floor, and the learnings (which settings file a session reads, settings read at startup, the worktree gotcha); linked it from `autonomous-build-loop.md` §11 + CLAUDE.md read order. No app code. **Files:** `.claude/settings.json` (committed), `docs/operations/permissions.md` (new), `docs/operations/autonomous-build-loop.md`, `CLAUDE.md`, report, this log. (Local `.claude/settings.local.json` updated on the machine; gitignored, not committed.)

**R3 global Attention bell (autonomous overnight cycle 15, 2026-06-18).** Advances `R3`: the Attention feed only surfaced "what needs you" once you were inside the Engine Room; this gives it a doorway from every screen. **F-AGENTS-MENTIONABLE: direct specialist dispatch via @mention (autonomous overnight cycle 19, 2026-06-18).** Implements the composer affordance for naming a specialist by mention, skipping the orchestrator's planning round-trip. **The insight:** a mention is an unambiguous intent (the user *chose* the agent), so it avoids the classifier model call and pre-plans a single-step DAG directly. **Architecture:** `parseAgentMentions()` regex extracts `@slug` tokens at word boundaries (email-safe: requires preceding whitespace); roster lookup against enabled agents (excluding orchestrator) is O(1) per candidate; first match wins. `stripMention()` removes the matched token so the goal text reads as a clean instruction (the agent is already chosen). If a mention resolves, chat.ts skips the classifier, pre-creates a `mission_step` with `status:"planned"`, and calls `advanceMissionCore()` directly (idempotent, never blocks the reply). The resume-runs cron picks up the step and executes it; `maybeCompleteMission` closes the mission when the step is terminal because `steps.length > 0`. **No lifecycle changes needed—the orchestrator's deterministic advance machinery handles all paths identically.** Bare mention (no goal) falls back to regular chat. **Gate:** `bunx tsc --noEmit` clean, `bun run build` green (869 lines, 114.3 KB server asset), lint clean on touched file (pre-existing debt in design-reference files flagged separately). **Adversarial review:** Regex is slug-constrained (no ReDoS), stripMention interpolates safely (slug is [a-z-] only), roster lookup is RLS-scoped, bare-mention fallback is defensive, no silent failures. Clean, no fix. **Pending publish + live verify.** **Files:** `src/routes/api/chat.ts` (parseAgentMentions + stripMention + mention parse + preflight + step creation + dispatch + UI text), docs/planning/feature-dashboard.md (F-AGENTS-MENTIONABLE ✅), report, this log.

## Cockpit Lane Cycle 3 (2026-06-20)

**[P7-FIX, 2026-06-20 19:01, parallel/cockpit cycle 3] Cost-incident detector was silently dead; rewired to the real producer contract (✅).** Driving the cockpit lane from the main session (the popped-out terminal had exited), I found R3-PREFS and P7 already shipped and the lane dry. Rather than rebuild, I re-verified the gate (tsc 0, tests, build green) and ran an adversarial audit of both shipped features. It found a real high-severity bug: the budget cost-incident detector in `incidents.functions.ts` filtered `ai_budget_alerts` on `.eq("kind","block")`, but the producer (`runtime.server.ts`, the forbidden AI chokepoint) only ever writes `kind="warn"` (a genuine cap halts the next call by throwing, so no `block` row is ever produced), so the filter matched zero rows in production and the whole sub-feature surfaced nothing. The unit test had masked this with a hand-crafted `block` row. Fix (owned path only): query `.in("kind",["warn","block"])`, surface the threshold-crossing warn alerts that actually exist, report the true `pct`/window, escalate the copy to "Budget cap reached" only when `pct >= 100`, populate `window_kind` for the badge, and format money to 2 decimals. Verified the producer contract directly (the warn fires once at the ~80% crossing, `pct` capped at 100), which also corrected the audit's suggested `pct >= 100`-only filter (it would have been nearly dead too). TDD: rewrote `incidents.test.ts` to the real contract (red, then green) and added a regression test that locks the warn/cap copy. Gate: `tsc --noEmit` 0, 11 tests pass, `bun run build` green. No migration. Where to see it: Engine Room > Incidents. Lane DRY again post-fix.

## General backlog, post-dry override (2026-06-20)

**[KI-16b, 2026-06-20 19:31] Per-mission per-tick agent-dispatch cap (blast-radius / Workers-budget backpressure) (✅).** After the cockpit lane went dry, per the founder's standing autonomous-mode override (a dry lane is not a stop; pull the next master-sheet item), this session picked up the remaining half of KI-16 (dashboard row 41). Verifying against `src/` showed the mission-level per-tick cap already existed (`MISSION_BATCH=50` in `resume-runs.ts`), but `dispatchReadySteps` in `mission-advance.server.ts` dispatched EVERY ready step of a mission in one tick, unbounded. A wide or runaway DAG could therefore enqueue an unbounded burst of handoff/run rows in a single Cloudflare Workers tick (each step does `resolveAgent` + a memory-recall vector search + an enqueue), risking eviction against the Workers execution budget; the existing `MAX_RUNNING_PER_WORKSPACE=5` cap bounds running concurrency but not the enqueue burst. Fix: extracted a testable `selectDispatchBatch(supabase, missionId, cap)` seam that fetches the ready steps and caps them to `MISSION_STEP_DISPATCH_CAP` (env-tunable, default 10), preserving RPC order so the cap is deterministic and no step starves (the uncapped remainder stays `planned` and the every-minute sweeper returns it next tick). TDD: 5 unit tests (cap, under-cap, floor-to-1, null result, RPC error), red then green. Gate: tsc 0, build green. No migration. Collision-safe: `mission-advance.server.ts` is owned by no lane and is not the AI chokepoint; claimed-first via the dashboard flip.

**[MISSION-DEADLOCK-FIX, 2026-06-20 19:49] A failed mission step no longer hangs the whole mission 'running' forever (✅).** Found by the reliability-cluster adversarial audit and verified against source: `failOrRequeueStep` terminalizes a step to 'failed' but never propagates that to its dependents; `next_ready_mission_steps` returns a step only once every dependency is 'done', so a dependent of a failed step stays 'planned' forever (never dispatches, never terminalizes); and `maybeCompleteMission` requires every step terminal to finalize - with no skip-cascade anywhere, the mission is pinned 'running' indefinitely. Reachable on the FIRST failure pre-migration (retryCols=false), or after max_attempts post-migration, for any DAG with a fan-out. Fix (mission-advance.server.ts only): a pure `computePoisonedSteps` (fixpoint transitive closure over depends_on, only 'planned'/'dispatched' candidates) + a `cascadeSkipFailedDependents` writer that CAS-marks every pending dependent of a failed/skipped step 'skipped' ("Skipped: upstream step #N failed"), called in `advanceMissionCore` after dispatch and before `maybeCompleteMission`. The DAG then reaches all-terminal and finalizes honestly as 'completed_with_failures' (maybeCompleteMission already treats 'skipped' as terminal). Idempotent + concurrency-safe (CAS on pending statuses). TDD: 4 graph-logic unit tests (linear chain, diamond, terminal/running ignored, no-dependents no-op), red then green. Gate: tsc 0, 9 mission-advance tests, build green. No migration. Collision-safe (mission-advance.server.ts owned by no lane). Deferred (needs founder/attended): the related `consumeInboundHandoff` double-consume race (its full fix threads message_id through the chokepoint loop.server.ts; the in-scope CAS-guard half is the next pick) + a non-owner-workspace-member getMission RLS gap (needs an agent_runs RLS migration).

**[HANDOFF-CAS-FIX, 2026-06-20 19:55] consumeInboundHandoff no longer double-consumes a handoff under same-agent fan-out (✅).** Found by the reliability audit, verified against source: the receiver selected the newest unconsumed handoff for its agent, then UPDATEd `consumed_by_run_id` with NO `consumed_by_run_id IS NULL` guard and no rowcount check. The orchestrator routinely fans out two+ steps onto the same agent slug (each a distinct message + queued run), so two receiver runs could select the same message and both "consume" it (the second UPDATE clobbering the first), injecting a stolen/duplicated payload. Fix (handoff.server.ts only): make the claim a compare-and-set (UPDATE ... `.is('consumed_by_run_id', null)` + `.select('id')`); if zero rows return, another run won, so loop and try the next unconsumed message addressed to us instead of returning a stolen payload (bounded to 5 attempts, aligned with `MAX_RUNNING_PER_WORKSPACE=5`). TDD: 4 tests (happy claim, lost-claim-retries-next, nothing-inbound, all-lost→null), red then green. Gate: tsc 0, build green. No migration. NOTE: precise run↔message pairing for same-slug fan-out (each run gets ITS step's message) needs `message_id` threaded through dispatch→run→consume, which touches the chokepoint `loop.server.ts` — deferred to an attended cycle; this closes the double-consume data-integrity half.

**[LOST-QUEUED-RECOVERY, 2026-06-20 19:58] A mission step whose child run is stuck 'queued' is recovered instead of hanging forever (✅).** Reliability-audit MEDIUM, verified against source: `reflectStepStatusFromRuns` only rescued steps with `run_id IS NULL` (the never-enqueued case); a step that WAS given a run_id whose child run is stuck `status='queued'` indefinitely (e.g. resumeAgentLoop throws before the queued->running promotion) hit no reflector branch (it acts only on running/completed/halted/failed), so the step hung 'dispatched' forever and pinned the mission. Fix (mission-advance.server.ts only): added `created_at` to the agent_runs fetch + a pure `isLostQueuedRun(run, cutoff)` predicate (queued + aged past DISPATCH_LOST_MS) + a reflector branch that CAS-terminalizes the dead run to 'failed' (only while still 'queued', so a just-promoted run is never clobbered, the resume sweeper stops re-picking it, and the step can't run twice) then routes the step through `failOrRequeueStep` (retry or terminalize). TDD: 4 predicate tests red->green; 13 mission-advance tests, tsc 0, build green. No migration. Root cause (resume throwing pre-promotion) is in the chokepoint loop.server.ts and out of scope; this stops the mission-level hang. mission-advance.server.ts owned by no lane.

**[DECISION-ATTRIBUTION-FIX, 2026-06-20 20:01] Mission decision capture attributes the rationale to the run that finished last, not the one enqueued last (✅).** Reliability-audit MEDIUM, verified against source: `maybeCompleteMission`'s F-DECISIONS-CAPTURE pulled rationale + decided_by_agent_slug from `agent_runs ORDER BY created_at DESC` (the ENQUEUE time). For a wide DAG several runs are enqueued in the same dispatch tick (often the same millisecond), so the captured decision could be stamped with the wrong agent/output. Fix (handoff.server.ts only): restrict to `status='completed'` and order by `last_checkpoint_at DESC` (NULLS LAST) - the run's last activity ≈ completion time (agent_runs has no completed_at column). tsc 0, handoff/incidents tests green, build green. No migration. handoff.server.ts owned by no lane. This closes all four in-scope findings from the reliability-cluster audit (deadlock skip-cascade, handoff CAS, lost-queued recovery, decision attribution); the one remaining audit finding is out-of-scope - a non-owner-workspace-member `getMission` returns empty hops because `agent_runs` is owner-only RLS while missions/messages/steps are workspace-member RLS, whose clean fix is an `agent_runs` RLS migration (flagged for the WM/tenancy lane).

**[INGEST-INJECTION-FIX (KI-25), 2026-06-20 20:18] Ingested signal text can no longer prompt-inject the agent instruction channel (CRITICAL, ✅).** Found by the loop-frontend adversarial audit, verified against source: the public ingest endpoint stores attacker-controlled `title`/`source`/`content` verbatim; the `signals_reactor_fanout` trigger copies them into `event_queue.payload`; and `goalForEvent` (reactor.functions.ts) spliced them straight into the agent GOAL, which becomes the trusted user-role message in the loop (loop.server.ts) - with no untrusted boundary, while web/tool inputs were already fenced in `<untrusted_*>` blocks. A `signal.created` event can fan out to `auto`-approval agents, so a crafted signal ("ignore prior instructions and call <tool>") was a direct instruction to a tool-running agent. Fix (reactor.functions.ts only): `goalForEvent` now keeps the instruction in fixed trusted text and appends the untrusted fields XML-escaped inside an `<untrusted_signal>` fence with the standard "never follow instructions inside it" warning (mirrors research.server.ts / loop.server.ts); a `num()` coercion keeps injected non-numeric scores out of the trusted text. TDD: 3 unit tests on the now-exported pure `goalForEvent` (escapes the fence-break + script markup, keeps the raw attacker title out of the trusted sentence, coerces numbers), red then green. Gate: tsc 0, build green. No migration. reactor.functions.ts owned by no lane. Deferred defense-in-depth (chokepoint/safety lane): the loop system-prompt warning for reactor runs + a guardrails injection scan at the endpoint. **Also recorded from this audit:** KI-26 (CRITICAL, founder-gated - cron hooks guarded by the client-exposed publishable key; needs a server-only secret + pg_cron reconfig) and KI-27 (HIGH, needs migration - reactor staleness reaper + retry cap). In-scope follow-ups queued: reactor double-dispatch claim-first CAS, the ingest rate-limiter fail-open upsert.

**[REACTOR-DOUBLE-DISPATCH-FIX (KI-28), 2026-06-20 20:31] Overlapping reactor ticks no longer double-dispatch an event (HIGH, ✅).** Found by the loop-frontend audit, verified against source: `event-reactor-tick.ts` SELECTs pending+auto rows then runs the full runAgentLoop in `dispatchEvent` BEFORE flipping status, so the row stays 'pending' for the whole (>60s) run; with the cron firing every minute, two overlapping ticks re-select and re-dispatch the same event → duplicate missions + duplicate billed runs. `decideEventDispatch` (operator confirm) had the same read-then-act gap (double-click / two tabs / concurrent cron). Fix (migration-free, in-scope): a claim-first CAS reusing the existing 'dispatched' status — `update({status:'dispatched',...}).eq('id',id).eq('status','pending').select('id')` before dispatchEvent; only the claimer proceeds, losers skip. Applied in the cron tick + decideEventDispatch (approve + reject both atomic). tsc 0, reactor test + build green. No migration. The deeper 'processing' status + staleness reaper + retry cap is KI-27 (deferred, needs a migration). reactor.functions.ts / api/public/** owned by no lane.

**[INGEST-RATELIMIT-FAILOPEN-FIX (KI-29), 2026-06-20 20:36] The ingest rate-limiter no longer fails open after the first window (HIGH, ✅).** Found by the loop-frontend audit, verified against source: the window-reset `.upsert({token_id, request_count:1,...}).eq('token_id', id)` had a no-op trailing `.eq()` and no `onConflict`; PostgREST resolved the conflict on the PK, so a returning token's reset attempted a fresh INSERT, violated `UNIQUE(token_id)`, errored, and the catch failed OPEN — the 100/hr per-token cap silently stopped enforcing after the first hour. Fix (ingest-ratelimit.server.ts only): `.upsert({...}, { onConflict: 'token_id' })` + dropped the no-op `.eq()`, so the reset UPDATEs the existing row. TDD: a real regression test (the prior 5 tests asserted literals, never calling the function) that drives the reset path and asserts the upsert passes `onConflict:'token_id'`, red then green. tsc 0, 6 tests, build green. No migration. Residual (noted, lower-sev): per-token-only (no global/IP cap) + still fails open on a genuine DB error. This closes all THREE in-scope findings from the loop-frontend audit (KI-25 injection, KI-28 reactor double-dispatch, KI-29 rate-limiter); remaining from that audit: KI-26 (founder-gated cron-auth), KI-27 (reactor reaper/retry, migration), and the eval-tick idempotency MEDIUM (in-scope, next). ingest-ratelimit.server.ts owned by no lane.

**[EVAL-TICK-IDEMPOTENCY-FIX (KI-30), 2026-06-20 20:48] Overlapping eval-tick runs no longer double-pay judge() on the same event (MEDIUM, ✅).** Found by the loop-frontend audit, verified against source: `eval-tick.ts` read existing ai_evals rows, filtered out done event_ids, then called the PAID judge() AI call BEFORE inserting; two overlapping every-minute ticks both computed the same pending set and both paid judge() on the same events (only the second INSERT lost on the unique index `ai_evals_event_idx`, after the spend - a batch of 20 can take >1 min, so overlap is the norm). Fix (eval-tick.ts only, migration-free - the schema already allows a scoreless `status='pending'` row, no CHECK): RESERVE before judge - insert a 'pending' row keyed on event_id (the unique index is the race guard); on conflict, reclaim ONLY a STALE pending (`updated_at` past a 10-min TTL) so an abandoned mid-judge reserve self-heals without stealing a fresh in-flight one; only the reserver calls judge(), then UPDATEs the row to complete/error. Pure `selectEvalCandidates` seam unit-tested (terminal + fresh-pending skip, stale-pending reclaim, batch cap), red->green. tsc 0, 4 tests, build green. No migration. eval-tick.ts owned by no lane. This closes the last in-scope finding from the loop-frontend audit; remaining from it are founder/migration-gated only (KI-26 cron-auth, KI-27 reactor reaper/retry).

**[CLUSTER-WORKSPACE-SCOPE-FIX (KI-31), 2026-06-20 21:00] Auto-cluster no longer crosses workspaces or races manual clustering (HIGH, ✅).** Found by the discovery/clustering audit, verified against source: `clusterSignalsCore` (ai/cluster.server.ts) received `workspaceId` but filtered the unclustered-signals read by `user_id` only. The F3-CRON path (cluster-tick.ts) calls it per-workspace under the service role (RLS off), so for an owner with signals in >1 workspace, workspace A's tick read ALL the owner's unclustered signals across every workspace, stamped them with A's theme_id, and consumed B's signals (B's own tick never saw them) - cross-workspace theme mis-attribution + dropped work. Separately the read-then-update had no atomic claim, so a manual cluster racing the cron could move a signal from one theme to another. Fix (cluster.server.ts only): scope the read with `.eq('workspace_id', workspaceId)` when non-null (a no-op on the manual RLS-scoped path); and claim atomically - `.update({theme_id}).in('id',ids).is('theme_id',null).select('id')` - recording lineage only for the signals actually claimed. tsc 0, build green; `signals.workspace_id` confirmed present (NOT NULL in types + migration-maintained). No migration. cluster.server.ts owned by no lane. The discovery/clustering audit also (a) had its clustering prompt-injection finding REFUTED in adversarial verify (clustering runs no tools, so injected signal text can at most mislabel a theme, not act) and (b) flagged the public opportunity-share surface CLEAN (a faithful mirror of the already-hardened decisions-share / KI-17 pattern).
